Now he remembered coming down through the timber in the dark holding the horse's tail when you could not see and all the stories that he meant to write.

About the half-wit chore boy who was left at the ranch that time and told not to let any one get any hay,

and that old bastard from the Forks who had beaten the boy when he had worked for him stopping to get some feed.

> ==chore英 [tʃɔ:(r)] 美 [tʃɔ:r] n. 零星工作（尤指家常杂务）；令人讨厌的或繁重的工作==
>
> <font color=red>About the half-wit chore boy / who was left at the ranch that time / and told not to let any one get any hay, / and that old bastard from the Forks / who had beaten the boy when he had worked for him / stopping to get some feed.</font>
>
> 还想起那个打杂的愣头青，那次把他留在了牧场，叮嘱他别让任何人偷干草。有个从福克斯过来的老混蛋想弄点饲料，男孩过去曾经给他干过活，还挨过他的揍。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> 这个句子没有独立的主谓结构，可以看作由两部分构成：
>
> ①About the half-wit chore boy / who was left at the ranch that time / and told not to let any one get any hay...
>
> the half-wit chore boy是中心词，who was left...and (was) told...是定语从句修饰boy;
>
> ②...and that old bastard from the Forks / who had beaten the boy when he had worked for him / stopping to get some feed.
>
> and that old bastard from the Forks中的that是指示代词，who had beaten the boy作定语从句修饰the old bastard, when he had worked for him要注意指代问题，he是the old bastard, him是the boy; stopping to get some feed作the old bastard的后置定语。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> the half-wit chore boy “那个打杂的愣头青”；wit作名词表示“机智，颖悟力”（the ability to think quickly and make the right decisions），所以half-wit指“傻瓜，笨蛋”（sb who behaves in a stupid, silly, or irresponsible way）; chore表示“杂务，琐事”，chore boy也就是“打杂的男孩”。

The boy refusing and the old man saying he would beat him again.

The boy got the rifle from the kitchen and shot him when he tried to come into the barn and when they came back to the ranch he'd been dead a week, frozen in the corral, and the dogs had eaten part of him.

But what was left you packed on a sled wrapped in a blanket and roped on and you got the boy to help you haul it,

and the two of you took it out over the road on skis, and sixty miles down to town to turn the boy over.

He having no idea that he would be arrested.

Thinking he had done his duty and that you were his friend and he would be rewarded.

He'd helped to haul the old man in so everybody could know how bad the old man had been and how he'dtried to steal some feed that didn't belong to him,

and when the sheriff put the handcuffs on the boy he couldn't believe it.

Then he'd started to cry. That was one story he had saved to write.

He knew at least twenty good stories from out there and he had never written one. Why?

"You tell them why," he said. "Why what, dear?" "Why nothing."

She didn't drink so much, now, since she had him.

But if he lived he would never write about her, he knew that now.

Nor about any of them. The rich were dull and they drank too much, or they played too much backgammon.

They were dull and they were repetitious.

> ==repetitious英 [ˌrepəˈtɪʃəs] 美 [ˌrɛpɪˈtɪʃəs] adj. 重复的，反复的==

He remembered poor Julian and hisromantic awe of them and how he had started a story once that began,"The very rich are different from you and me."

And how some one had said to Julian, Yes, they have more money.

But that was not humorous to Julian.

He thought they were a special glamourous race and when he found they weren't it wrecked him just as much as any other thing thatwrecked him.

He had been contemptuous of those who wrecked.

You did not have to like it because you understood it.

He could beat anything, he thought, because no thing could hurt him if he did not care.

All right. Now he would not care for death. One thing he had always dreaded was the pain.

He could stand pain as well as any man, until it went on too long, and wore him out, but here he had something that had hurt frightfully and just when he had felt it breaking him, the pain had stopped.

### 背景知识

**💧****The History of The Paris Commune**

**巴黎公社的历史**

我们今天的内容讲到酒徒和运动员是巴黎公社的后裔（hey were the descendants of the Communards and it was no struggle for them to know their politics. ）以及巴黎公社的情形，我们今天就一起来看一下巴黎公社的历史吧～

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/0a979faf06895d05371381727983be3c-sz_2792841.png?x-oss-process=style/xmhigh)



巴黎公社是一个在1871年3月18日到5月28日期间短暂地统治巴黎的政府。巴黎工人团结起来推翻现存的法国政权，因其未能保护这座城市不受普鲁士的围攻，从而形成了该市和整个法国的第一个真正民主的政府。

1870年9月4日，巴黎爆发革命，宣布成立第三共和国。由资产阶级共和派和奥尔良派分子组成的新政府，称为“国防政府”。普鲁士并不满足于皇帝的投降，继续大举进攻法国。9月19日，普军包围巴黎。多年来不断加剧的贫富分化，再加上当前的食物短缺，军队失败，还有普鲁士军队的不断炮轰终于大大激化了社会各界的不满情绪。巴黎市民，特别是工人阶级和下层中产阶级一直以来都希望能建立一个民主共和国。

1871年3月18日凌晨，政府军企图夺取巴黎市内的蒙马特尔高地和梭蒙高地时，被人发现。巴黎人民奋起反击，当晚就占领了城内的战略要地，临时政府总理梯也尔狼狈逃出巴黎，迁往凡尔赛。不久，巴黎公社成立，它是第一个无产阶级政权的雏形。

5月23日，政府军通过普鲁士军队的防线攻陷蒙马特尔高地。当天晚上面临失败的公社政权下令纵火烧毁巴黎。在当天和次日被烧毁的建筑包括波旁王朝和第二帝国的王宫杜伊勒里宫和与其相连的卢浮宫、法国参议院、内政部、财政部、司法部、王宫（Le Palais Royal）、巴黎市政厅、圣马丁门歌剧院，同时开始枪杀人质。

最顽强的抵抗发生在东部的工人阶级区，战斗一直持续，直到流血周最后的巷战。到了当年5月27日，只有极少数的抵抗仍在持续，特别是最贫困的东部地区，如Belleville和Ménilmontant。当年战斗到5月28日下午或晚间全部结束。数万人被军队俘虏，其中许多人被处决。在“血腥的一周”中被杀害的人和被囚犯被处死的人被埋葬在城市周围无标记的坟墓中，公墓大屠杀的其中一个地方是在出名的拉雪兹神父公墓，那里现在存在纪念被杀的人。

### 课文理解

今天的内容开头依然是Harry的记忆闪回（昨天的结尾部分提到了他祖父的原木房子还有德国的黑森林），其中有一大段关于巴黎的描写，言语措辞之间充满明亮，这里也象征着他的青春、快乐，以及充满潜能和希望的时光——

💧**Clue 1**: His memory of Paris represents his youth, happiness, and potential.



**Evidence 1**: You could dictate that, but you could not dictate the Place Contrescarpe where the flower sellers dyed their flowers in the street and the dye ran over the paving...

这个你可以口授，但你口授不了康特斯卡普广场，花贩在大街上染花，染液一直流到了人行道上……



**Evidence 2**: There never was another part of Paris that he loved like that, the sprawling trees, the old white plastered houses painted brown below, the long green of the autobus in that round square, the purple flower dye upon the paving, the sudden drop down the hill of the rue Cardinal Lemoine to the River, and the other way the narrow crowded world of the rue Mouffetard.

巴黎再没有另一个让他如此喜爱的地方了，这里树木蔓生，白灰泥墙老房子的下半截被刷成了棕色，圆形广场上长长的绿色公交车，人行道上紫色的染色液，依山而下、直通塞纳河的勒穆瓦纳红衣大主教街，而拥挤狭窄的莫菲塔德街则是另一番景象。



还需要注意的一个细节是，虽然Harry对死亡既焦虑又恐惧，但他对于妻子的照顾和叮嘱丝毫不放在心上，他一刻也不停地在喝酒——



💧**Clue 2**: Harry wouldn't stopped drinking.



**Evidence 1**: "Wouldn't you like some more broth?" the woman asked him now.

"No, thank you very much. It is awfully good."

"Try just a little."

"I would like a whiskey-soda."

“不再喝点肉汤吗？”女人此刻问他。

“不要了，多谢你。这味道真好。”

“再喝一点儿吧。”

“我想喝威士忌苏打。”



**Evidence 2**:  Too tired. He was going to sleep a little while. He lay still and death was not there. It must have gone around another street. It went in pairs, on bicycles, and moved absolutely silently on the pavements.

太累了。他想睡一会儿。他静静地躺着，死神不在身边，一定是到了另一条街上。死神成双结对，骑着自行车，悄无声息地行使在人行道上。



在今天内容的结尾，Harry提到自己曾经最害怕的是疼痛（One thing he had always dreaded was the pain.）但是现在有一件更让他无法忍受的事情（but here he had something that had hurt frightfully and just when he had felt it breaking him, the pain had stopped）, 这件事情是什么呢？我们一起期待明天的情节进展~

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****Horsemeat**

**西方人对马肉的好恶**



在我们今天的内容中有这样的描写：The golden horse's head outside the Boucherie Chevaline where the carcasses hung yellow gold and red in the open window.（马肉铺子外面挂着金黄色的马头，在马肉铺的橱窗里挂着金黄色和红色的马肉。）法国人钟情于马肉，而英美等国却对马肉嗤之以鼻，不同国家对马肉的态度有很大差异，我们今天就一起来了解一下吧～

\1. 法国人爱吃马肉

在巴黎的街头巷尾的马肉铺门外，排成长队的人们挑选各自喜爱的部位，带回家去用油、柠檬汁和胡椒烹制。吃马肉的传统可以追溯到拿破仑时代。据记载，这一传统起源于19世纪初法俄两军在波兰激烈对垒，在弹尽粮绝时只得杀马充饥。马肉还帮助法国人度过了第二次世界大战后经济萧条的那些艰难岁月。如今法国的食客们仍保持着对马肉的忠诚，面包马脑、煎马心、马排都是法国厨房里的经典菜肴。

在欧洲，马都是用纯天然草料饲养的，因此马肉有利于人体吸收。不少法国人认为，马肉营养价值高，脂肪少、易烹饪，铁元素和蛋白质含量丰富，对治疗贫血效果很好，在法国经常被医生当作药膳推荐给妇女、青少年和运动员。

一些马肉美食家还联手办起一家网店，叫“我的马肉店”，不仅交流马的信息及马肉烹饪知识，还销售马肉，甚至提供送马肉上门的服务。吃马肉也从贫穷和绝望的象征变为品质的享受。在巴黎的一些知名餐馆，大厨们又恢复了马肉美味菜肴的制作，吸引了众多外国游客前来品尝。



\2. 英美人不吃马肉

英国拒绝马肉，或许是因为幅员辽阔的大英帝国有足够的红肉——猪牛羊鹿兔——可吃。2013年，英国人发现他们购买的牛肉制品中含有马肉而难以抑制怒火，出现了“马肉风波”。美国人即使在食物供应短缺的时候也不把刀叉指向他们的驮兽朋友，这也许是因为美国人和马从开拓时代起就建立起了深厚关系，以至于在20世纪的食物大短缺时代，吃马肉近乎是不道德的。 

《旧约·利未记》中禁止食用马肉。逃亡美洲的清教徒将基督教的饮食禁忌带到新大陆，美国人最开始也不吃马肉。除了宗教原因，北美大陆物产丰富，广袤的牧场提供足够多的饮食选择。9世纪的美国报纸满是对旧大陆残忍食马肉行为的报道。



由于吃马肉总与不愉快的主题（贫穷和丧失原则）相连，“马肉”一词演变成一种政治嘲讽的手段。在1948年的食物短缺中，杜鲁门总统被反对党讥讽为“马肉哈里”。

## Chapter 1.6

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/333a995128daa2e0be91936193f132cb-sz_897179.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

The Snows of Kilimanjaro

He remembered long ago when Williamson, the bombing officer, had been hit by a stick bomb some one in a German patrol had thrown as he was coming in through the wire that night and

> ==patrol==
>
> n. 巡逻队 (a group of soldiers, vehicles, etc. that patrol an area)
>
> 原文：He remembered long ago when Williamson, the bombing officer, had been hit by a stick bomb some one in a German patrolhad thrown...
>
> 他记得在很久以前，投弹军官威廉逊那天晚上钻过铁丝网爬回阵地的时候，给
>
> 一名德国巡逻兵扔过来的一枚手榴弹打中了......
>
> 💧patrol还可以做动词，表示“巡逻；巡查 ”，比如：Troops patrolled the border day and night.
>
> 军队日夜在边境地区巡逻。

screaming, had begged every one to kill him.

He was a fat man, very brave, and a good officer, although addicted to fantastic shows.

> ==addicted英 [əˈdɪktɪd] 美 [ə'dɪktɪd] adj. 上瘾的；沉迷于某种嗜好的 vt. 使…上瘾(addict的过去分词)==

But that night he was caught in the wire, with a flare lighting him up and his bowels spilled out into the wire,

so when they brought him in, alive, they had to cut him loose.

Shoot me, Harry. For Christ sake shoot me.

They had had an argument one time about our Lord never sending you anything you could not bear

and some one's theory had been that meant that at a certain time the pain passed you out automatically.

> <font color=red>They had had an argument one time / about our Lord never sending you anything you could not bear / and some one's theory had been / that meant that at a certain time the pain passed you out automatically.</font>
>
> 他们曾就上不会把你不能承受的东西降临在你身上有过一次争论，论点之一是只要疼痛持续一段时间，你就会自动失去知觉。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> ①我们先来看这个句子的主体部分：They had had an argument one time about...and some one's theory had been...
>
> ②about our Lord never sending you anything you could not bear是一个介词宾语结构，our Lord never sending...是动名词作宾语，you could not bear是修饰anything的定语从句；
>
> ③that meant that at a certain time the pain passed you out automatically是省略了that的表语从句，这里的第一个that是指示代词，指代前面的an argument, 而第二个that引导的是meant的宾语从句。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> the pain passed you out automatically “疼痛会使你自动失去知觉”；sb pass out表示“昏倒”（to faint or collapse）, 比如：When she heard the news she passed out.（她听到这个消息后就直接昏倒了。）这里sth pass sb out也就是“使某人昏倒”的意思。

But he had always remembered Williamson, that night.

Nothing passed out Williamson until he gave him all his morphine tablets that he had always saved to use himself and then they did not work right away.

> ==tablet英 [ˈtæblət] 美 [ˈtæblɪt] n. 药片；碑，匾；便笺簿；小块 vt. 用碑牌纪念；将（备忘录等）写在板上；将…制成小片或小块==
>
> <font color=red>Nothing passed out Williamson / until he gave him all his morphine tablets / that he had always saved to use himself / and then they did not work right away.</font>
>
> 没有一样东西能让威廉森失去知觉，直到哈里把自己所有的吗啡片都给了他，那是他留着给自己用的，就连那些吗啡片也没能立刻起到作用。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> ①Nothing did...until... “直到……时候才……”
>
> ②that he had always saved to use himself 是修饰morphine tablets的定语从句；
>
> ③and then they did not work right away 中的they指代的是morphine tablets.

Still this now, that he had, was very easy; and if it was no worse as it went on there was nothing to worry about.

> <font color=red>Still this now, that he had, was very easy; and if it was no worse as it went on there was nothing to worry about.</font>
>
> 现在，他（哈里）身上的疼痛并不难忍受，只要它不再恶化，就没有什么好担心的。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> ①still 在这里表示“然而”，相当于however;
>
> ②this now, that he had “现在他身上的疼痛”；this指pain, that he had是修饰this的定语从句，he指Harry.
>
> *这一句话表示Harrry重新回到现实里，在上文他回忆了投弹官威廉森曾经遭受的惨痛经历。

Except that he would rather be in better company.

He thought a little about the company that he would like to have.

No, he thought, when everything you do, you do too long, and do too late, you can't expect to find the people still there.

The people all are gone. The party'sover and you are with your hostess now.

I'm getting as bored with dying as with everything else, he thought.

"It's a bore," he said out loud.

"What is, my dear?"Anything you dotoo bloody long."

He looked at her face between him and the fire. She was leaning back in the chair and the firelight shone on her pleasantly lined face and he could see that she was sleepy.

He heard the hyena make a noise just outside the range of the fire.

"I've been writing," he said. "But I got tired."

"Do you think you will be able to sleep?"

"Pretty sure. Why don't you turn in?"

> <font color=red>"Pretty sure. Why don't you turn in?"</font>
>
> “没问题。你怎么还不去睡？”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> turn in 除了我们平时熟悉的“上交，递交”，还有“上床睡觉”的意思（to go to bed for the night）, 比如：I have to be up at 6 AM, so I'll need turn in early tonight.（我早上6点就得起床，所以我今晚要早点上床睡觉。）

"I like to sit here with you."

"Do you feel anything strange?" he asked her.

"No. Just a little sleepy."I do," he said.

He had just felt death come by again.

"You know the only thing I've never lost is curiosity," he said to her.

"You've never lost anything. You're the most complete man I've ever known."

"Christ," he said. "How little a woman knows. What is that? Your intuition?"

> ==intuition==
>
> n. 直觉（an idea or a strong feeling that sth is true although you cannot explain why）
>
> 原文："Christ," he said. "How little a woman knows. What is that? Your intuition?"
>
> “天哪，”他说。“女人知道的东西实在太少啦。你根据什么这样说？是直觉吗？”
>
> 💧intuition还可以表示“直觉力”，比如：In daily life it is easy to confuse intuition with our fears, desires or projections. 
>
> 在日常生活中，我们的直觉力很容易被恐惧，欲望及投射所混淆。

Because, just then, death had come and rested its head on the foot of the cot and he could smell its breath.

"Never believe any of that about a scythe and a skull," he told her.

"It can be two bicycle policemen as easily, or be a bird. Or it can have a wide snout like a hyena."

> <font color=red>"Never believe any of that about a scythe and a skull," he told her. "It can be two bicycle policemen as easily, or be a bird. Or it can have a wide snout like a hyena."</font>
>
> “千万别信什么镰刀和骷髅，”他对她说，“它完全有可能是两个自在地骑在自行车上的警察，或者是一只鸟，它也许长得像鬣狗那样的猪鼻子。”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> any of that about a scythe and a skull “千万别信什么镰刀和骷髅（的说辞）”；scythe和skull在西方文化里是“死亡”的象征，Harry是在和妻子描绘（调侃）死神可能有的模样。
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> hyena（鬣狗），体型似犬，长颈，后肢较前肢短弱，躯体较短，肩高而臀低。棕鬣狗体型较大，分布于非洲西南部海岸，常到海滩寻食螃蟹、鱼等。而斑鬣狗仅见于非洲，体型较大，成群猎食，除食腐肉外，能猎捕羚羊。土狼为特化的食蚁动物。

It had moved up on him now, but it had no shape any more. It simply occupied space.

"Tell it to go away." It did not go away but moved a little closer.

"You've got a hell of a breath," he told it. "You stinking bastard."

It moved up closer to him still and now he could not speak to it, and when it saw he could not speak it came a little closer,

and now he tried to send it away without speaking, but it moved in on him so its weight was all upon his chest

and while it crouched there and he could not move or speak, he heard the woman say, "Bwana is asleep now. Take the cot up very gently and carry it into the tent."

He could not speak to tell her to make it go away and it crouched now, heavier, so he could not breathe.

And then, while they lifted the cot, suddenly it was all right and the weight went from his chest.

It was morning and had been morning for some time and he heard the plane.

It showed very tiny and then made a wide circle and the boys ran out and lit the fires, using kerosene,

and piled on grass so there were two big smudges at each end of thelevel place and the morning breeze blew them toward the camp and theplane circled twice more,

low this time, and then glided down and levelled off and landed smoothly and,

coming walking toward him, was oldCompton in slacks, a tweed jacket and a brown felt hat.

"What's the matter, old cock?" Compton said.

"Bad leg," he told him. "Will you have some breakfast?"

"Thanks. I'll just have some tea. It's the Puss Moth you know.

I won't be able to take the Memsahib. There's only room for one. Your lorry is on the way."

Helen had taken Compton aside and was speaking to him. Compton came back more cheery than ever.

"We'll get you right in," he said. "I'll be back for the Mem. Now I'm afraid I'll have to stop at Arusha to refuel. We'd better get going."

"What about the tea?"I don't really care about it, you know."

The boys had picked up the cot and carried it around the green tents and down along the rock and out onto the plain and along past the smudges that were burning brightly now,

the grass all consumed, and the wind fanning the fire, to the little plane.

It was difficult getting him in, but once in he lay back in the leather seat, and the leg was stuck straight out to one side of the seat where Compton sat.

Compton started the motor and got in. He waved to Helen and to the boys and, as the clatter moved into the old familiar roar,

> ==clatter英 [ˈklætə(r)] 美 [ˈklætɚ] vt.& vi. 发出咔哒声；嘁嘁喳喳地说笑；使卡搭卡搭的响 n. 哗啦声；嘁嘁喳喳的谈笑声；咔哒声==

they swung around with Compie watching for warthog holes and roared, bumping,

along the stretch between the fires and with the last bump rose and he saw them all standing below, waving,

and the camp beside the hill, flattening now, and the plain spreading, clumps of trees, and the bush flattening,

while the game trails ran now smoothly to the dry waterholes, and there was a new water that he had never known of.

The zebra, small rounded backs now, and the wildebeeste, big-headed dots seeming to climb as they moved in long fingers across the plain,

now scattering as the shadow came toward them, they were tiny now, and the movement had no gallop,

and the plain as far as you could see, gray-yellow now and ahead oldCompie's tweed back and the brownfelt hat.

Then they were over the first hills and the wildebeeste were trailing upthem, and then they were over mountains with sudden depths of green-rising forest and the solid bamboo slopes,

> <font color=red>Then they were over the first hills / and the wildebeeste were trailing up them, / and then they were over mountains with sudden depths of green-rising forest / and the solid bamboo slopes...</font>
>
> 他们飞过第一群山岭，角马正在往山上走，然后他们飞过生长着绿色参天大树的山峰，还有生长着茂密竹林的山坡……
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①the wildebeeste were trailing up them “角马正在往山上走”；them在这里指前面的the first hills; trail表示“（慢悠悠地）走”，比如：We spent the afternoon trailing around the shops.（我们整个下午都在慢悠悠地逛商店。）
>
> ②with sudden depths of green-rising forest“生长着绿色参天大树的山峰”；depths of在这里可以理解为“大片的”（a vast space of）.
>
> ③the solid bamboo slopes “生长着茂密竹林的山坡”；solid表示“连绵的，茂密的”（continuous; thick, dense）. 

and then the heavy forest again, sculptured into peaks and hollows until they crossed, and hills sloped down and then another plain, hot now, and purple brown, bumpy with heat and Compie looking back to see how he was riding.

> <font color=red> ...and then the heavy forest again, /sculptured into peaks and hollows / until they crossed, / and hills sloped down and then another plain, / hot now, and purple brown, /bumpy with heat / and Compie looking back to see / how he was riding.</font>
>
> 接着又是一片茂密的森林，随地势起伏成峰谷，缓缓向下的山坡连着另一片平原，现在热起来了，到处都是紫棕色，飞机在热浪中颠簸，康毕回头查看他的状况。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①sculptured into peaks and hollows “随地势起伏成峰谷”；这个过去分词短语作forest的后置定语，sculptured into表示“形成……形状”；peaks and hollows“山峰和低谷”；
>
> ②until they crossed “直到他们飞过这片森林”；they指Compie和Harry;
>
> ③bumpy with heat “飞机在热浪中颠簸”；bumpy既可以指“颠簸的”，也可以表示“坎坷的，困难的”，a bumpy ride/time指“一段坎坷艰难的时期”，比如：Shareholders have had a bumpy ride.（股民日子难过。） 

Then there were other mountains dark ahead.

And then instead of going on to Arusha they turned left, he evidently figured that they had the gas, and looking down he saw a pink sifting cloud, moving over the ground,

and in the air, like the first snow in at a blizzard, that comes from nowhere, and he knew the locusts were coming, up from the South.

> ==blizzard英 [ˈblɪzəd] 美 [ˈblɪzərd] n. 暴风雪；大量==
>
> ==locust英 [ˈləʊkəst] 美 [ˈloʊkəst] n. 蝗虫，蚱蜢；[植]角豆树；[植]洋槐；破坏者==

Then they began to climb and they were going to the East it seemed, and then it darkened and they were in a storm, the rain so thick it seemed like flying through a waterfall,

and then they were out and Compieturned his head and grinned and pointed and there, ahead, all he could see, as wide as all the world, great, high, and unbelievably white in the sun, was the square top of Kilimanjaro.

And then he knew that there was where he was going.Just then the hyena stopped whimpering in the night and started to make a strange,human, almost crying sound.

> ==whimper英 [ˈwɪmpə(r)] 美 [ˈhwɪmpɚ, ˈwɪm-] vi. 啜泣，呜咽；抱怨 vt. 啜泣或呜咽着说 n. 啜泣声，呜咽声；怨声==

The woman heard it and, stirred uneasily. She did not wake.

In her dream she was at the house on Long Island and it was the night before her daughter's debut.

> ==debut英 ['deɪbju:] 美 [deˈbju, ˈdeˌbju] n. 初次露面，初次表演，首次出场，处女秀 v. 初次表演，初次登台 adj. 首张的，首场的，首次的==

Somehow her father was there and he had been very rude.

Then the noise the hyena made was so loud she woke and for a moment she did not know where she was and she was very afraid.

Then she took the flashlight and shone it on the other cot that they had carried in after Harry had gone to sleep.

She could see his bulk under the mosquito bar but somehow he had gotten his leg out and it hung down alongside the cot.

The dressings had all come down and she could not look at it.

"Molo," she called, "Molo! Molo!"

Then she said, "Harry, Harry!" Then her voice rising, "Harry! Please. Oh Harry!"

There was no answer and she could not hear him breathing.

Outside the tent the hyena made the same strange noise that had awakened her.

But she did not hear him for the beating of her heart.

### 背景知识

**💧****The Symbols in The Snows of Kilimanjaro**

**小说中意象的象征含义**

今天是我们这篇小说学习的最后一天，今天要给大家分析一下小说中出现的意象有哪些象征含义～



\1. 坏疽：肉体与精神的双重腐败

原文：Since the gangrene started in his right leg he had no pain and with the pain the horror had gone and all he felt now was a great tiredness and anger that this was the end of it.（自从他的右腿开始生坏疽以来，他就不觉得痛，随着疼痛的消失，恐惧也消失了，他现在感到的只是一种强烈的厌倦和愤怒：这居然就是结局。）

小说中男主人公Harry因左腿被荆棘刺破后未能及时医治而感染了坏疽，最终导致了死亡。Harry左腿的坏疽开始于非洲之行，但其精神上的“坏疽”早就已经蔓延。Harry本是一位作家，在经历了诸多挫折与磨难之后放弃了对爱以及写作的追求，“坏疽”的长期存在导致了Harry精神的腐败。他的懒惰、势利与傲慢毁灭了自己的创作才能。

他与妻子Helen来到非洲狩猎就是为了重拾创作的激情，医治精神上的“坏疽”。在Harry纵情酒色之中的时候，精神的“坏疽”就已经一发不可收拾，哈利废弃了自己的写作才华和对写作的追寻，沉醉在纸醉金迷之中，而富有的妻子Helen也成为了Harry精神上“坏疽”蔓延的催化剂。实际Harry腿上的坏疽是其精神“坏疽”的象征性显现，而二者结合最终夺去了Harry的肉体和灵魂。



\2. 鬣狗和秃鹰：死亡的迫近与物质的寄生

原文：... but of a sudden, evil-smelling emptiness and the odd thing was that the hyena slipped lightly along the edge of it.（而是一股无影无踪的臭气的冲击，令人奇怪的是，那只鬣狗却沿着这股无影无踪的臭气的边缘轻轻地溜过了。）

Harry左腿的坏疽散发出腐肉的气息，吸引着只食腐肉的鬣狗和秃鹰。鬣狗和秃鹰的这种习性使得二者成为了象征死亡的重要意象，它们始终与死亡和黑暗相联系。鬣狗和秃鹰出现“在天色渐暗之时，它们寻着Harry左腿上腐肉所散发的腐败气味徘徊在哈利的周遭，使人感觉到仿佛死亡也在一点一点逼近”。

而鬣狗和秃鹰的生活习性又是Harry生活的写照：哈利就像终日食腐肉的鬣狗和秃鹰一样，在寄生中生存，空有写作的才华却完全放弃了自我对写作的追寻。Helen是个富有的女人，在与妻子的生活中，Harry是个彻头彻尾的寄生者。他巧言令色、满嘴谎言，出卖自己换取Helen在物质上的无限供应。



\3. 雪山猎豹：追寻的精神永生 

原文：Kilimanjaro is a snow covered mountain 19,710 feet high, and it is said to be the highest mountain in Africa.（乞力马扎罗是一座海拔一万九千七百一十英尺的长年积雪的高山，据说它是非洲最高的一座山。）

Close to the western summit there is the dried and frozen carcass of a leopard. No one has explained what the leopard was seeking at that altitude. （在西高峰的近旁，有一具已经风干冻僵的豹子的尸体。豹子到这样高寒的地方来寻找什么，没有人作过解释。）

小说开始是一段景物描写，乍看起来颇令人费解，但细细咀嚼完故事的高潮，即Harry灵魂飞升的过程后，再回过头来品味这一段，才使人真正步入海明威创造的神奇的意境之中。猎豹是海明威极为喜爱甚至崇拜的动物。他曾在《非洲的青山》（*The Green Hills of Africa*）中通过人与豹耐力与智力的较量，对豹做过人格化和描叙。

在这段描写中，海明威只是写了雪山与猎豹。以雪山之巅的死豹意象作为开头给出了一个谜：豹子为什么要到这么高的雪山上来？为了追寻什么：为了食物，或是因为某种神秘的冲动？生命虽然终结，但因冻僵，尸体得以风干保存，这意味着什么？小说没有给出答案，设置了悬念。

### 课文理解

在最后的闪回中，Harry想起了过去在战争中，一个投弹官被手榴弹击中，最后痛不欲生的场景（He remembered long ago when Williamson, the bombing officer, had been hit by a stick bomb some one in a German patrol had thrown as he was coming in through the wire that night and, screaming, had begged every one to kill him.）接着他回到现实里，对于现在的他来说，疼痛已经不算什么了，他唯一遗憾的是身边没有一个称心的伴侣，即便是Helen也无法让他满意——

💧**Clue 1**: Harry is not satisfied with Helen's company.

**Evidence 1**: Still this now, that he had, was very easy; and if it was no worse as it went on there was nothing to worry about. Except that he would rather be in better company.

现在，他身上的疼痛并不难忍受，只要它不再恶化，就没有什么好担心的。  他只是希望自己能有一个好一点儿的伴儿。

**Evidence 2**: "You know the only thing I've never lost is curiosity," he said to her.

"You've never lost anything. You're the most complete man I've ever known."

"Christ," he said. "How little a woman knows. What is that? Your intuition?"

“你知道，我唯一没有失去的东西，就是好奇心。”他对她说。

“你什么都没有失去。你是我知道的最完美的男人。”

“上帝啊。”他说，“女人真是见识短。那是什么？你的直觉？”



Harry不断地感觉死神在向他逼近（It had moved up on him now, but it had no shape any more. It simply occupied space.）在他清醒的最后时刻，他听到Helen吩咐仆人把他轻轻抬进帐篷里去（he heard the woman say, "Bwana is asleep now. Take the cot up very gently and carry it into the tent."）接着Harry再次进入潜意识中，这一次，他梦见自己在第二天早晨等到了救援飞机，但是这架飞机没有按照原定计划去加油，或是飞向附近的城镇，它飞去的是乞力马扎罗的山顶——



💧**Clue 2**: Before Harry dies, he dreamt of being on a plane and flying to the top of Kilimanjaro.



**Evidence 1**: Compie turned his head and grinned and pointed and there, ahead, all he could see, as wide as all the world, great, high, and unbelievably white in the sun, was the square top of Kilimanjaro. And then he knew that there was where he was going.

康毕转过头来，对他咧嘴一笑，用手指了指，前方，他目所能及的像整个世界一样壮阔，雄伟高耸，在阳光下白得令人难以置信的，正是乞力马扎罗山方形的山顶。他于是明白了，那就是他要去的地方。



**Evidence 2**: Just then the hyena stopped whimpering in the night and started to make a strange, human, almost crying sound. The woman heard it and, stirred uneasily. She did not wake.

就这时候，鬣狗在夜色中停止了悲嚎，它开始发出一种奇怪的、几乎像人的哭声那样的叫喊声。女人被这个声音搅得心神不宁，但她并没有醒来。



乞力马扎罗的山顶一直被称为“上帝的居所”（the House of God）, 因此Harry在临死之际想象自己飞向了乞力马扎罗的山顶也可以理解为一种对“在精神世界安息”的渴望。在现实中他并未能完全实现自己的理想，而是终日在安逸享乐之中（尤其是遇上了Helen这样可以供他吃穿的妻子）。意外受伤以及濒临死亡的体验让他开始深刻地思考这个问题，但最终矛盾依旧没有在现实中得到解决，而是以迂回的方式，在他的潜意识里画上了句号。

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****战争小说推荐**

**War Novels**

在我们今天的内容当中出现了一个投弹军官被一名德国巡逻兵扔过来的一枚手榴弹打中之后的血腥场面（when Williamson, the bombing officer, had been hit by a stick bomb some one in a German patrol had thrown as he was coming in through the wire that night and, screaming, had begged every one to kill him. ）

海明威参加过两次世界大战、第二次希腊土耳其战争和西班牙内战，因此在他的小说中出现过很多战争场面。今天我们给大家推荐几部战争题材的小说，有的作家描写战争暴露而血腥，有的作家隐忍而克制，我们来一起了解一下吧～



\1. 《红色英勇勋章》(The Red Badge of Courage) 斯蒂芬·克莱恩（Stephen Crane）

小说以美国南北战争（1861-1865）为历史背景。主人公亨利是一个农妇的独子。他怀着对战争的奇妙幻想，渴望过军队生活，不顾母亲的劝阻，参加了北方军。激烈的战斗场面虽然对他有刺激性的引诱，但死亡的威胁在他心里发生着强烈的动摇作用。战场上的炮声解除了他的矛盾心理，亨利勇敢地投入了战斗，但当遭到敌人突然袭击时，他惊恐万状，扔下枪枝，从阵地上逃跑了。

当他听到北方军重又获胜的消息时，他不幸被从火线上溃退下来的一个士兵用枪托打伤了脑袋。伙伴们见亨利负了伤，不仅不怀疑他是逃兵，反而敬佩他那种轻伤不下火线的勇敢精神。可是亨利万分羞愧，暗暗下决心寻找立功机会。

\2. 《第22条军规》（Catch-22）约瑟夫·海勒（Joseph Heller）

该小说以第二次世界大战为背景，通过对驻扎在地中海一个名叫皮亚诺扎岛上的美国空军飞行大队所发生的一系列事件的描写，揭示了一个非理性的、无秩序的、梦魇似的荒诞世界。小说中，根据“第二十二条军规”理论，只有疯子才能获准免于飞行，但必须由本人提出申请。但你一旦提出申请，恰好证明你是一个正常人，还是在劫难逃。

第二十二条军规还规定，飞行员飞满25架次就能回国。但规定又强调，你必须绝对服从命令，要不就不能回国。因此上级可以不断给飞行员增加飞行次数，而你不得违抗。如此反复，永无休止。突出代表一种美国式的“黑色幽默”（black humor）。

\3. 《第五号屠宰场》（Slaughterhouse-Five）库尔特·冯内古特（Kurt Vonnegut）

主人公毕利，在第二次世界大战中，他随部队到达欧洲，参加了保吉战役，结果被德军俘虏，随后到德国德累斯顿的一个地下屠宰场做苦工。德累斯顿是一座历史悠久的美丽古城，没有任何军事目标。然而就是这样一座城市，1945年却遭到英美联军的联合轰炸，被一夜间夷为平地。毕利被关在地下冷藏室而幸免于难，然而这段经历却给他造成无法愈合的精神创伤。 

毕利由于战争精神深受刺激，心理受创伤之后经常出现幻想：他遭遇飞碟绑架，被送到特拉法玛多星球，在星球动物园中像动物般被展出和观看。毕利挣脱了时间的羁绊，他就寝的时候，是个衰老的鳏夫，醒来时却在举行婚礼。他从1955年的门进去，却从另一个门1941年出来了。

\4.  《辛德勒名单》  ( Schindler's List) 托马斯·基尼利(Thamas Keneally)

布克奖的获奖小说，以高度纪实的手法，刻画了二次大战时期德国商人奥斯卡·辛德勒冒着生命危险，倾注所有财力和智慧，营救数百位犹太人生命的真实故事。问世以来，这部小说以其撼人心魄的真实性和洋溢于字里行间的人道主义的光辉，感动了无数读者，被斯皮尔伯格改编成电影以后成为电影史上的经典之作。

奥斯卡·辛德勒是一位具有传奇色彩的真实的历史人物。作者尽量避免一切的虚构，作了大量的案头工作和调查取证，尽量区别真实与神话传奇。将辛德勒描写得有血有肉，十分逼真，凡人的弱点和美德都统一于他一身。

## Chapter 2

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/232548bbbc9234ad2ca4119478eeab30-sz_1430282.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

A Clean, Well-Lighted Place

It was very late and everyone had left the café except an old man who sat in the shadow the leaves of the tree made against the electric light.

> <font color=red>It was very late / and everyone had left the café / except an old man / who sat in the shadow / the leaves of the tree made / against the electric light.</font>
>
> 天已经很晚了，所有人都离开了咖啡馆，只剩下一位老人，他坐在遮住电灯的树叶投下的阴影里。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①the leaves of the tree made 作修饰shadow的定语从句，指“树叶投下的阴影”；
>
> ②against the electic light “在电灯（的背景）下”，against有“以……为背景，衬托”的意思，比如：He could see a line of figures silhouetted against the sky.（他看到在天空的映衬下有一排人影。） 

In the day time the street was dusty, but at night the dew settled the dust and the old man liked to sit late because he was deaf and now at night it was quiet and he felt the difference.

The two waiters inside the café knew that the old man was a little drunk, and while he was a good client they knew that if he became too drunk he would leave without paying, so they kept watch on him.

"Last week he tried to commit suicide," one waiter said. "Why?"

"He was in despair." "What about?" "Nothing."

"How do you know it was nothing?" "He has plenty of money."

They sat together at a table that was close against the wall near the door of the café and looked at the terrace where the tables were all empty except where the old man sat in the shadow of the leaves of the tree that moved slightly in the wind.

> ==terrace英 [ˈterəs] 美 [ˈtɛrɪs] n. 阳台；台阶，阶地；柱廊，门廊；斜坡上房屋间的街巷 vt.把（如山坡或坡地）修成梯田；给（如房屋）建阳台==

A girl and a soldier went by in the street. The street light shone on the brass number on his collar.

The girl wore no head covering and hurried beside him.

"The guard will pick him up," one waiter said.

> <font color=red>"The guard will pick him up," one waiter said. "What does it matter if he gets what he's after?"</font>
>
> “警卫会把他抓起来的。”一个侍者说。“如果他得到了他想要的，抓起来又有什么关系？”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> pick up 在这里表示“逮捕”（to arrest or take sb to a police station）. 比如：Rawlings had been picked up by police at his office.（罗林斯在他的办公室被警察逮捕了。） 

"What does it matter if he gets what he's after?"

"He had better get off the street now. The guard will get him. They went by five minutes ago."

The old man sitting in the shadow rapped on his saucer with his glass.

The younger waiter went over to him. "What do you want?"

The old man looked at him. "Another brandy," he said.

"You'll be drunk," the waiter said.

The old man looked at him. The waiter went away.

"He'll stay all night," he said to his colleague.

"I'm sleepy now. I never get into bed before three o'clock. He should have killed himself last week."

The waiter took the brandy bottle and another saucer from the counter inside the café and marched out to the old man's table.

He put down the saucer and poured the glass full of brandy.

"You should have killed yourself lastweek," he said to the deaf man.

The old man motioned with his finger. "A little more," he said.

> ==motion==
>
> n. 运动；手势；动机，意向；请求
>
> vt. 打手势；向某人点头或摇头示意；打手势要求[指示]（you move your hand or head as a way of telling them to do something or telling them where to go）
>
> 原文：The old man motioned with his finger.
>
> 老人用手指示意。
>
> 💧motion 作名词有“动作，手势”的意思，put sth in motion也就是“使某事开始发生”的意思，这里的motion作动词，表示“做动作示意”，相当于signal. 比如：The police officer motionedfor me to pull over.（警察示意我靠边停车。） 

The waiter poured on into the glass so that the brandy slopped over and ran down the stem into the top saucer of the pile.

> ==slop英 [slɒp] 美 [slɑ:p] vi. 溢出，泼出；在泥浆（或雪泥）中走 vt.（液体）晃出；使（某物）溢出或泼出；休息，放松，偷懒 n. 污水；粪便与废水；宽松的罩衣；剩菜屑==
>
> <font color=red>The waiter poured on into the glass so that the brandy slopped over and ran down the stem into the top saucer of the pile.</font>
>
> 侍者把白兰地倒进酒杯，酒溢出了酒杯，顺着杯脚流到了一叠托碟最顶端的那一个上。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①poured on into the glass 应理解为“继续把酒倒进酒杯里”；pour into是“倾倒”，on在这里表示“继续”，因为前面老人老人示意侍者接着再倒点（"A little more," he said）.
>
> ②slop over 表示“溢出”（to come out over the edge of the container）, 比如：A little cognacslopped over the edge of the glass.（少量法国白兰地溢出了酒杯的边缘。）
>
> ③ran down the stem “顺着杯脚”，stem指“（酒杯或花瓶的）颈，柄，脚”，比如long-stemmed wine glasses 就是指“高脚酒杯”。

"Thank you," the old man said. The waiter took the bottle back inside the café.

He sat down at the table with his colleague again.

"He's drunk now," he said. "He's drunk every night."

"What did he want to kill himself for?" "How should I know."

"How did he do it?" "He hung himself with a rope."

"Who cut him down?" "His niece."

"Why did they do it?" "Fear for his soul."

"How much money has he got?" "He's got plenty."

"He must be eighty years old." "Anyway I should say he was eighty."

"I wish he would go home. I never get to bed before three o'clock. What kind of hour is that to go to bed?"

"He stays up because he likes it."

"He's lonely. I'm not lonely. I have awife waiting in bed for me."

"He had a wife once too." "A wife would be no good to him now."

"You can't tell. He might be better with a wife."

"His niece looks after him. You said she cut him down." "I know."

"I wouldn't want to be that old. An old man is a nasty thing."

"Not always. This old man is clean. He drinks without spilling. Even now, drunk. Look at him."

"I don't want to look at him. I wish he would go home. He has no regard for those who must work."

The old man looked from his glass across the square, then over at the waiters.

"Another brandy," he said, pointing to his glass.

The waiter who was in a hurry came over.

"Finished," he said, speaking with that omission of syntax stupid people employ when talking to drunken people or foreigners.

> ==omission英 [əˈmɪʃn] 美 [oˈmɪʃən] n. 遗漏；疏忽；省略，删节；[法]不履行法律责任==
>
> ==syntax英 [ˈsɪntæks] 美 [ˈsɪnˌtæks] n. 语法；句法；句法规则[分析]；语构==

"No more tonight. Close now." "Another," said the old man. "No. Finished."

> <font color=red>"Finished," he said, / speaking with that omission of syntax / stupid people employ /  when talking to drunken people or foreigners. "No more tonight. Close now."</font>
>
> “打烊了。”他说。他用的是蠢人对醉汉或者外国人说话时的那种省略句法，“今晚没有。现在关门。”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①that omission of syntax “省略句法”；syntax指“句法”，也就是单词组成短语或句子的结构和方法（the way words are arranged to form sentences or phrases）. 这里的省略句法也就是像上下文出现的"Finished."和"Not more tonight. Close now."这样的不完整句，显得态度非常轻蔑傲慢。
>
> ②stupid people employ 作定语从句修饰that omission of syntax; employ指“使用，运用”（to use）, 常见的搭配有emply a method/technique/tatic等，比如：The report examines teaching methods employed in the classroom.（这个报告探讨了课堂教学方法。）

The waiter wiped the edge of the table with a towel and shook his head.

The old man stood up, slowly counted the saucers, took a leather coin purse from his pocket and paid for the drinks, leaving half a peseta tip.

The waiter watched him go down the street, a very old man walking unsteadily but with dignity.

"Why didn't you let him stay and drink?" the unhurried waiter asked.

They were putting up the shutters. "It is not half-past two."

"I want to go home to bed." "What is an hour?"

"More to me than to him." "An hour is the same."

"You talk like an old man yourself. He can buy a bottle and drink at home."

"It's not the same." "No, it is not," agreed the waiter with a wife.

He did not wish to be unjust. He was only in a hurry.

"And you? You have no fear of going home before your usual hour?"

"Are you trying to insult me?"

"No, hombre ([西]先生，老弟), only to make a joke."

"No," the waiter who was in a hurry said, rising from pulling down the metal shutters.

> ==shutter英 [ˈʃʌtə(r)] 美 [ˈʃʌtɚ] n. 快门；百叶窗；遮光器 vt. 使…停止运行，关闭；装上百叶窗或以百叶窗关闭==

"I have confidence. I am all confidence."

"You have youth, confidence, and a job," the older waiter said. "You have everything."

"And what do you lack?" "Everythingbut work."

"You have everything I have."

"No. I have never had confidence and I am not young."

"Come on. Stop talking nonsense and lock up."

"I am of those who like to stay late at the café," the older waiter said.

"With all those who do not want to go to bed. With all those who need a light for the night."

"I want to go home and into bed."

"We are of two different kinds," the older waiter said. He was now dressed to go home.

"It is not only a question of youth and confidence although those things are very beautiful.

Each night I am reluctant to close up because there may be some one who needs the café."

"Hombre, there are bodegas (尤指西班牙卖酒的小杂货店) open allnight long."

"You do not understand. This is a clean and pleasant café. It is well lighted.

The light is very good and also, now, there are shadows of the leaves."

"Good night," said the younger waiter. "Good night," the other said.

Turning off the electric light he continued the conversation with himself.

It was the light of course but it is necessary that the place be clean and pleasant.

You do not want music. Certainly you do not want music.

Nor can you stand before a bar with dignity although that is all that is provided for these hours.

What did he fear? It was not a fear or dread.

It was a nothing that he knew too well. It was all a nothing and a man was a nothing too.

It was only that and light was all it needed and a certain cleanness and order.

Some lived in it and never felt it but he knew it all was nada y pues nada y nada y pues nada ([西]除了虚无还是虚无).

Our nada who art in nada, nada be thy name thy kingdom nada thy will be nada in nada as it is in nada.

Give us this nada our daily nada and nada us our nada as we nada our nadas and nada us not into nada but deliver us from nada; puesnada.

Hail nothing full of nothing, nothing is with thee.

> <font color=red>Some lived in it and never felt it but he knew it all was nada y pues nada y nada y pues nada. Our nada who art in nada, nada be thy name thy kingdom nada thy will be nada in nada as it is in nada. Give us this nada our daily nada and nada us our nada as we nada our nadas and nada us not into nada but deliver us from nada; pues nada. Hail nothing full of nothing, nothing is with thee.</font>
>
> 有人生在其中，却从来感觉不到，但他知道一切都是虚无，除了虚无还是虚无。我们在虚无的虚无，愿人都尊你的名为虚无，你的国为虚无，愿你的虚无行走在虚无，如同行走在虚无，赐给我们虚无，作为我们日用的虚无，虚无我们的虚无，因为我们虚无我们的虚无，并虚无我们没有遇见的虚无，把我们救出虚无；除了虚无还是虚无。歌颂充满虚无的虚无，虚无与你同在。
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> 侍者自言自语说的这一段祈祷词来自对基督教主祷文的改编，原文如下：
>
> 我们在天上的父，愿人都尊你的名为圣。愿你的国降临，愿你的旨意行在地上，如同行在天上。
>
> 我们日用的饮食，今日赐给我们。
>
> 免我们的债，如同我们免了人的债。
>
> 不叫我们遇见试探，救我们脱离凶恶。
>
> 因为国度，权柄，荣耀，全是你的，直到永远。
>
> 而这位侍者把诸如“天上的”、“父”、“旨意”等词都替换为了“虚无”（nada）, 表示对虚无的颂赞。

He smiled and stood before a bar with a shining steam pressure coffee machine.

"What's yours?" asked the barman. "Nada."

"Otro loco mas ([西]又是个神经病)," said the barman and turned away.

"A little cup," said the waiter. The barman poured it for him.

"The light is very bright and pleasant but the bar is unpolished," the waiter said.

> ==unpolished英 ['ʌn'pɒlɪʃt] 美 ['ʌn'pɒlɪʃt] adj. 粗鲁的；无光泽的；未磨光的；未磨练的==

The barman looked at him but did not answer. It was too late at night for conversation.

"You want another copita?" the barman asked.

"No, thank you," said the waiter andwent out.

He disliked bars and bodegas. A clean, well-lighted café was a very different thing.

Now, without thinking further, he would go home to his room.

He would lie in the bed and finally, with daylight, he would go to sleep.

After all, he said to himself, it's probably only insomnia. Many must have it.

> ==insomnia英 [ɪnˈsɒmniə] 美 [ɪnˈsɑ:mniə] n. [医]失眠，失眠症==
>
> n. 失眠（the condition of being unable to sleep）
>
> 原文：After all, he said to himself, it's probably only insomnia.
>
> 毕竟，他对自己说，这可能只是失眠症。
>
> 💧insomnia 指“失眠症”，这个词来源于拉丁文，in是否定前缀，somnia是睡眠的意思，而hypersomnia则相反，指“嗜睡症”，比如：Oversleeping could be a sign of hypersomnia, a medical condition that causes sleepiness during the day and the need for increased sleep at night.
>
> 睡眠过多可能是嗜睡症的征兆，也就是白天易昏昏欲睡而晚上所需睡眠时间也增长。

### 背景知识

**💧****创作背景**

《一个干净明亮的地方》是海明威短篇小说中的经典之作，讲述了两个男服务生（一长一少）准备结束一个在咖啡厅工作的夜晚，结果遇到一个老人常客又来买醉迟迟不归。

该短篇小说写于1933年，收在1938年出版的《海明威短篇小说》中。亲历了第一次世界大战的灾难，海明威不仅身体受到重创（身中二百多块弹片），更可怕的是心灵的创伤再也无法弥合，“像神圣、光荣、牺牲这些空洞的字眼总令我困窘……我观察了很久，没有见到什么神圣的东西，原来光荣的东西也没呈现出光荣，而牺牲就像芝加哥的屠宰场，不同的只是把肉埋掉罢了”。

战争的体验使海明威这一代人对生活感到痛苦迷旧，对生命的本质和人的生存意义产生了怀疑。在这篇故事中，海明威的虚无主义得到集中的表达和呈现：生命的本质是虚无飘渺（Life is nothingless）. 同时故事中的这个老人，和海明威笔下的其他主角也有异曲同工之处——从他自杀和饮酒的两个选择行为来分析，他展现了重压之下的优雅风度和精神不败的尊严感。

**💧****写作手法**



《华盛顿邮报》的图书编辑罗恩·查尔斯就曾评价说，海明威的短篇小说比他的长篇小说更优秀（Washington Post's books editor, Ron Charles, has said that Hemingway’s short stories are better than his novels）. 《一个干净明亮的地方》里除了大量使用简短句子外，还运用了其他手法来达到一种四两拨千斤的效果和味道：



\1. 对比（Contrast）

海明威使用的主要是传统的对比手法，比如：咖啡馆的干净、安宁与酒吧的嘈杂形成对比；树叶的阴影与咖啡馆的明亮形成对比（The light is very good and also, now, there are shadows of the leaves）; 再比如，街道上嬉笑行走的大兵和少女与咖啡馆低头喝酒的老人的对比（...the old man sat in the shadow of the leaves of the tree that moved slightly in the wind. A girl and a soldier went by in the street）.

还有黑夜与明亮的对比；阴影与亮光的对比；老人的孤独、迷惘与年轻侍者的忙碌、满足及年老侍者的空虚、无奈的对比；年轻的侍者性急、有老婆、有信心与年老的侍者无老婆、无信心、没有稳定感的对比。

一切的对比无不显示着小说主题的表达：第一次世界大战后，随着美国梦的破灭，许多人的迷惘、借酒消愁、追求刺激、精神上一片荒芜，人们渴望关心和被理解，却依然生活在空虚的阴影之下。



\2. 象征（Symbolism）

首先这个西班牙的小咖啡馆就是一个象征：有灯光且清洁，是保持尊严的地方。但在作者的心里，它不是一个具体的场所“干净”，象征人的平静状态，以及对自我的坚定把握“光亮”则象征保持冷静清醒的头脑。

老人有清醒的头脑，但他感到时间、环境、家对他的毁灭性的打击，感到死亡带来的威胁与空虚，于是他到咖啡馆来“买醉”，因为这是“一个清洁明亮的地方”，他需要有个明亮的地方找寻安慰、友谊，他需要明亮的地方对抗心里无边的黑暗。



\3. 重复（Repetition）

年老侍者在他的内心独自中，多次重复“空虚”。海明威生活在理想、幻想破灭的时代，他一生都像一勇士去战斗，对抗孤独、黑暗与死亡。但另一方面，面对动荡不安的社会、没有信心和稳定感的人们，所以开始思考人的心灵深处的东西：孤独、麻木、没有信仰，没有物质和精神上的支持，没有具体方法摆脱现实处境的孤独与无奈。

此外“干净”和“光亮”也是小说中出现频率很高的词。这是在空虚之中迷惘一代所追求的——一个有着亮光而不孤独的地方去排遣自己的孤独。

### 课文理解

故事发生在西班牙的一家咖啡馆，到了很晚的时候，一位老人还在喝酒，他是这家咖啡馆的常客。两个侍者开始讨论起他来。从他们的对话中我们可以得知，这位老人很有钱，但却因为仅仅感到绝望而尝试上吊自杀，最后被外甥女给救了下来——



💧**Clue 1**: A rich man who frequents the café has tried to kill himself out of despair.



**Evidence 1**: "Last week he tried to commit suicide," one waiter said.

"Why?"

"He was in despair."

"What about?"

"Nothing."

"How do you know it was nothing?"

"He has plenty of money."

“上个礼拜他想自杀。”一个侍者说道。

“为什么？”

“绝望呗。”

“为了什么？”

“不为什么。”

“你怎么知道不为什么？”

“他很有钱。”



**Evidence 2**: "He's lonely. I'm not lonely. I have a wife waiting in bed for me." "He had a wife once too."

"A wife would be no good to him now."

"You can't tell. He might be better with a wife."

“他孤单，我可不孤单，我有一个在床上等我的老婆。”

“他也有过老婆。”

“现在老婆对他来说已经没什么用了。”

“这很难说。有老婆他可能会活得好一点。”



老人看起来已经有八十多岁（"He must be eighty years old." ）虽然家产丰厚，但并无亲近的人，只有一个外甥女在照顾他。年轻的侍者不能理解老人为何每天在咖啡馆待到凌晨，并且永远喝得大醉，他甚至觉得人老了就是邋里邋遢的模样（"I wouldn't want to be that old. An old man is a nasty thing."）



但另一位年长侍者的态度却截然不同，他不仅看到老人身上依然残存的风度，并且对他的孤独也深有所感——



💧**Clue 2**:  The older waiter full sympathizes with the old man and his loneliness.



**Evidence 1**: "Not always. This old man is clean. He drinks without spilling. Even now, drunk. Look at him."...The waiter watched him go down the street, a very old man walking unsteadily but with dignity.

“也不都是那样。这个老头就很干净。他喝酒从不流出来，就像现在，都喝醉了。你看他。”……侍者看着他顺着街道往前走，一个很老的老人，虽然步履蹒跚，但不失尊严。



**Evidence 2**: It was not a fear or dread. It was a nothing that he knew too well. It was all a nothing and a man was a nothing too. It was only that and light was all it needed and a certain cleanness and order.

这不是害怕或恐惧，是一种他太熟悉了的虚无。一切都是虚无，人也是一种虚无。所需要的只是灯光和某种程度的整洁。



老人富有，但缺乏其他情感支撑，而对年长的侍者来说也是如此，除了工作，其余的他也一无所有（"You have youth, confidence, and a job," the older waiter said. "You have everything." "And what do you lack?" "Everything but work."）因此他格外理解这种空虚，并不是只要在热闹的酒吧就能得到慰藉的。这种空虚需要的是灯光和整洁（象征着“体面和尊严”）。



因此这个短篇探讨的其实是虚无（nothingness）的问题，以及如何去面对虚无。咖啡馆提供的整洁和光亮虽然不能完全消除孤独和虚无，但却延缓了这种痛苦，所以老人每天在这喝酒到凌晨，而年长侍者也愿意让想留下来的客人待得更久一点（"I am of those who like to stay late at the café," the older waiter said. "With all those who do not want to go to bed. With all those who need a light for the night."）



而回到家之后，他还是必须得面对现实、承受失眠的痛苦。（He would lie in the bed and finally, with daylight, he would go to sleep. After all, he said to himself, it's probably only insomnia. Many must have it.）

### 今日彩蛋

**💧Coffee Shop Etiquette Rules**

**咖啡店的礼貌守则**

当老人迟迟不肯离去的时候，年轻的侍者十分不耐烦："I don't want to look at him. I wish he would go home. He has no regard for those who must work."（“我不想看。我希望他回家去。他一点都不在乎那些必须上班的人。”）

当时已经凌晨三点了，老人这么做显然不够礼貌得体。今天的彩蛋我们就来了解一下在咖啡店必须注意哪些礼貌守则吧~

\1. Don't sit there all day with one drink in front of you

别在咖啡店坐一整天但只点一杯饮品

长时间地占有咖啡厅的座位虽然不会遭受驱赶，但其实是一件非常不礼貌的事情哦~就像我们不会在饭店里吃完午饭就坐上一整天直到晚饭时间一样，否则别人会当你这是在咖啡店“借宿”（to camp in a coffee shop）.



并且当有人只是想进来吃个蛋糕、喝杯咖啡或者坐下来休息聊会天，结果发现里面的人都是只点了一杯咖啡而坐着对了仨小时电脑的人，不免会很失望（Two people might want to come in and have cake, coffee, and a conversation. But they might be stopped by someone sitting at a laptop for three hours sipping a cup of tea.）长期以往也会影响咖啡店的盈利（对于独立的小咖啡馆而言）。



\2. Don't take conference calls in shops and talk loudly

别旁若无人地大声打视频电话

如果真的需要打视频电话，最好走到外面，而不是在安静或者需要维持个人空间独立的咖啡厅内（If you have to jump on a conference call, please take it outside it you can）. 

尤其是当你还是主讲人的时候，更不要旁若无人地在咖啡店里高谈阔论（If you're the dominant audio source in the cafe, you shouldn't be）. 



\3. Don't stretch an extension cord across the floor to plug in your laptop

别在咖啡店拉插线板来给电脑充电

不能插线板主要是出于安全考虑，尤其当其他客人在咖啡店里端着热咖啡到处移动的时候，除了可能会被绊倒，如果咖啡撒到插线板上，还有可能起火灾（Someone might trip on extension cords and spill out hot coffee）.

实在需要充电，可以和坐在插座旁的客人商量是否可以换位。但绝对不要自作主张地在咖啡厅里拉起插线板哦~



\4. Don't ask someone to watch your laptop

不要叫旁边的人帮你看电脑

有时候我们会犯懒，需要上洗手间或是短暂离开座位的时候总爱让旁边的人帮我们看一下电脑，而不愿意花一点工夫把电脑收进包里然后一起带到洗手间（Don't burden some poor sap sitting next to you just because you're too lazy to put your laptop into a bag and haul it into the bathroom）.

虽然对方也许会客气地答应，但这实际上是一件不太礼貌的事情。比如万一对方也需要上洗手间或者有急事需要马上离开呢？另一方面，假设对方真的离开了，又由谁来看着呢？（Besides, what if they have to go to the bathroom too? Who will watch the watcher's laptop.）因此出于为双方的考虑，最好的是自己能做的事情自己来完成。

## Chapter 3

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/f1ba415f526680f178c08d5b26495a64-sz_697675.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

The Doctor and the Doctor's Wife

Dick boulton came from the Indian camp to cut up logs for Nick’s father.

He brought his son Eddy and another Indian named Billy Tabeshaw with him.

They came in through the back gate out of the woods, Eddy carrying the long cross-cut saw.

It flopped over his shoulder and made a musical sound as he walked.

> ==flop==
>
> vi. （笨拙地、不由自主地或松弛地）移动或落下（to hang or fall loosely, in an uncontrolled way）
>
> 原文：It flopped over his shoulder and made a musical sound as he walked.
>
> 他走路时，锯子在肩上啪嗒啪嗒地颠动，发出乐声来。
>
> 💧flop 可以形容物体“垂下、落下”，也可以形容人“耷拉着脑袋（显出沮丧可怜的样子）”，比如：His head flopped back pathetically.
>
> 他脑袋向后仰着，一副可怜相。

Billy Tabeshaw carried two big canthooks.

Dick had three axes under his arm. He turned and shut the gate.

The others went on ahead of him down to the lake shore where the logs were buried in the sand.

The logs had been lost from the big log booms that were towed down the lake to the mill by the steamer Magic.

> <font color=red>The logs had been lost from the big log booms that were towed down the lake to the mill by the steamer Magic.</font>
>
> 这些原木是从“魔法”号轮船在湖上托运到锯木厂来的大批浮木中飘失的。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①the big log booms “大批浮木”；boom指用带环的铁钉钉在每根原木的末端从而做成的木筏，主要是为了方便在水面上运输原木。
>
> *下文也提到，如果这些飘失的浮木没有人来收集，可能“魔法”号上的水手们还会回来再把这些浮木做成木筏然后运走：...the crew of the Magic would come along the shore in a rowboat, spot the logs, drive an iron spike with a ring on it into the end of each one and then tow them out into the lake to make a new boom.
>
> ②were towed down the lake “在湖面上托运”；tow和pull意思相同，表示“牵引，拖，拉”，比如：The ship had to be towed into the harbor.（那艘轮船不得不被拖进港口。） 

They had drifted up onto the beach and if nothing were done about them sooner or later the crew of theMagic would come along the shore in a rowboat, spot the logs, drive aniron spike with a ring on it into the end of each one and then tow themout into the lake to make a new boom.

But the lumbermen might never come for them because a few logs were not worth the price of a crew to gather them.

If no one came for them they would be left to waterlog and rot on the beach.

> ==waterlog英 ['wɔ:təlɒg] 美 ['wɔ:təˌlɔ:g] n. 涝灾==

Nick’s father always assumed that this was what would happen, and hired the Indians to come down from the camp and cut the logs up with the cross-cut saw and split them with a wedge to make cord wood and chunks for the open fireplace.

Dick Boulton walked around past the cottage down to the lake.

There were four big beech logs lying almost buried in the sand.

Eddy hung the saw up by one of its handles in the crotch of a tree.

Dick put the three axes down on the little dock.

Dick was a halfbreed and many of the farmers around the lake believed he was really a white man.He was very lazy but a great workeronce he was started.

He took a plug of tobacco out of hispocket, bit off a chew and spoke in Ojibway to Eddy and Billy Tabeshaw.

> <font color=red>He took a plug of tobacco out of his pocket, bit off a chew and spoke in Ojibway to Eddy and Billy Tabeshaw.</font>
>
> 他从口袋里掏出一块嚼烟来，咬下一小块，就用奥吉布瓦语对埃迪和比利·泰布肖说话。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> a plug of tobacco “一块嚼烟”；plug常见义是“插头；塞，栓”，这里指“（压实的）块”，a plug of tobacco即“烟草块”，也就是一般说的“嚼烟”（chewing tobacco），最初在某些印第安人部落中曾很普遍。
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> Ojibway（奥吉布瓦）也称Chippewa（奇珀瓦），是居住在北美苏必利尔湖一带地方的一个印第安部族。20世纪后主要分布在美国明尼苏达、北达科他、威斯康星、密执安和蒙大拿诸州; 少数住在加拿大。

They sunk the ends of their cant-hooks into one of the logs and swung against it to loosen it in the sand.

> <font color=red>They sunk the ends of their cant-hooks intoone of the logs and swung against it to loosen it in the sand.</font>
>
> 他们把两根钩杆扎进一根原木，使劲转动，想把它从沙子中松开。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①sink...into... “把…扎进…”；sink有“沉没”的意思，这里指“戳，捅，扎”（to put sth sharp into）, 比如：She sank her fork into the pie.（她把叉子插进馅饼。）
>
> ②swung against it “（抵着原木）转动”；这里的it指one of the logs “其中一根原木”，swing指“（举着，握着）使某物旋转”，比如：He marched around, swinging the gun by its handle.（他快步走来走去，手握枪把挥动着。）
>
> *这里形容他们握着钩杆抵在原木上转动，cant-hook是一种一端装有活动钩的木杆，用来钩住原木使其翻转。

They swung their weight against theshafts of the cant-hooks. The log moved in the sand.

Dick Boulton turned to Nick’s father.

“Well, Doc,” he said, “that’s a nice lot of timber you’ve stolen.”

“Don’t talk that way, Dick,” the doctor said.

“It’s driftwood.” Eddy and Billy Tabeshaw had rocked the log out of the wet sand and rolled it toward the water.

“Put it right in,” Dick Boulton shouted.

“What are you doing that for?” asked the doctor.

“Wash it off. Clean off the sand on account of the saw. I want to see who it belongs to,” Dick said.

The log was just awash in the lake. Eddy and Billy Tabeshaw leaned ontheir cant-hooks sweating in the sun.

> ==awash==
>
> adj. 被淹没的（covered with water or another liquid）
>
> 原文：The log was just awash in the lake.
>
> 原木就这么泡在湖里头。
>
> 💧awash 表示“被淹没的”，是一个由前缀a-加动词形成的形容词（其他例子比如a+wake=awake “醒着的”）。另外awash还有“充斥的，泛滥的”的含义，比如：All the pavements were awash with rubbish.
>
> 所有的人行道上全是垃圾。

Dick kneeled down in the sand and looked at the mark of the scaler’s hammer in the wood at the end of the log.

“It belongs to White and McNally,” he said, standing up and brushing off his trousers knees.

The doctor was very uncomfortable.

“You’d better not saw it up then, Dick,” he said, shortly.

Don’t get huffy, Doc,” said Dick. “Don’t get huffy. I don’t care who you steal from. It’s none of my business.”

“If you think the logs are stolen, leave them alone and take your tools back to the camp,” the doctor said.

His face was red. “Don’t go off at half cock, Doc,” Dick said.

He spat tobacco juice on the log. It slid off, thinning in the water.

> <font color=red>He spat tobacco juice on the log. It slid off,thinning in the water.</font>
>
> 他唾了一口烟沫在木头上。烟沫一滑，滑进水里给冲淡了。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①tobacco juice “烟沫”；这里的He是Dick，前面提到他在咬嚼烟，所以这里的juice可以理解为他在咀嚼烟草时嚼出的烟沫（烟液）；juice在俚语中经常被用来指各种液态或流体的东西，比如“酒精类饮料”（alcoholic drinks）、“引擎油”（fuel for the engine）、“电流”（electric current）.
>
> ②thin 作动词表示“变薄，变稀”（to become thinner and weaker）, 比如：The clouds had begun to thin.（云层渐稀。）

“You know they’re stolen as well as I do. It don’t make any difference to me.”

“All right. If you think the logs are stolen, take your stuff and get out.”

“Now, Doc—” “Take your stuff and get out.” “Listen, Doc.”

“If you call me Doc once again. I’ll knock your eye teeth down your throat.”

> <font color=red>"I’ll knock your eye teeth down your throat."</font>
>
> “我就敲断你的虎牙，叫你咽下去”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> eye teeth 指“上尖牙”，也就是我们俗话说的“虎牙”；此外在习语里，give one's eye teeth for sth/to do sth还表示“迫切渴望得到某物/做某事”，比如：I'd give my eye teeth to own a car like that.（我巴不得有一辆那样的汽车。） 

“Oh, no, you won’t, Doc.” Dick Boulton looked at the doctor.

Dick was a big man. He knew how big a man he was.

He liked to get into fights. He was happy.

Eddy and Billy Tabeshaw leaned on their cant-hooks and looked at the doctor.

The doctor chewed the beard on hislower lip and looked at Dick Boulton.

Then he turned away and walked up the hill to the cottage.

They could see from his back how angry he was.

They all watched him walk up the hill and go inside the cottage.

Dick said something in Ojibway. Eddy laughed but Billy Tabeshaw looked very serious.

He did not understand English but he had sweat all the time the row was going on.

He was fat with only a few hairs of mustache like a Chinaman.

He picked up the two cant-hooks. Dick picked up the axes and Eddy took the saw down from the tree.

They started off and walked up past the cottage and out the back gate into the woods.

Dick left the gate open. Billy Tabeshaw went back and fastened it.

They were gone through the woods.

In the cottage the doctor, sitting on the bed in his room, saw a pile of medical journals on the floor by the bureau.

They were still in their wrappers unopened. It irritated him.

“Aren’t you going back to work, dear?” asked the doctor’s wife from the room where she was lying with the blinds drawn.

“No!” “Was anything the matter?” “I had a row with Dick Boulton.”

“Oh,” said his wife. “I hope you didn’t lose your temper, Henry.” “No,” said the doctor.

“Remember, that he who ruleth his spirit is greater than he that taketh acity,” said his wife.

> <font color=red>“Remember, that he who ruleth his spirit is greater than he that taketh a city,” said his wife.</font>
>
> “记住，克己的人胜过克城的人，”他妻子说。
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> ruleth和taketh分别是古英语里rule和take的第三人称单数形式。这句话出自《圣经·旧约·箴言》第16章第32节，强调自制能力的重要。

She was a Christian Scientist. Her Bible, her copy of Science and Health and her Quarterly were on a table beside her bed in the darkened room.

> <font color=red>She was a Christian Scientist. Her Bible, her copy of Science and Health and her Quarterly were on a table beside her bed in the darkened room.</font>
>
> 她是个基督教科学派。她的《圣经》、她那本《科学与健康》和《季刊》就放在暗洞洞的房里床边的桌上。
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> 基督教科学派是玛丽·贝克·埃迪于1866年首创的一种医疗学说，将基督教与科学相结合，以精神力量战胜疾病。《科学与健康》初版于1875年，是她认为得到上帝启示后所写的该教派的权威读物。

Her husband did not answer. He was sitting on his bed now, cleaninga shotgun.

> ==shotgun英 [ˈʃɒtgʌn] 美 [ˈʃɑ:tgʌn] n. 鸟枪，散弹猎枪==

He pushed the magazine full of the heavy yellow shells and pumped them out again.

They were scattered on the bed.

“Henry,” his wife called. Then paused a moment.

“Henry!” “Yes,” the doctor said.

“You didn’t say anything to Boulton to anger him, did you?” “No,” said the doctor.

“What was the trouble about, dear?”“Nothing much.”

“Tell me, Henry. Please don’t try and keep anything from me. What was the trouble about?”

“Well, Dick owes me a lot of money for pulling his squaw through pneumonia and I guess he wanted a row so he wouldn’t have to take itout in work.”

His wife was silent. The doctor wiped his gun carefully with a rag.

He pushed the shells back in against the spring of the magazine.

He sat with the gun on his knees. He was very fond of it.

Then he heard his wife’s voice from the darkened room.

“Dear, I don’t think, I really don’t think that any one would really do a thing like that.” “No?” the doctor said.

“No. I can’t really believe that any one would do a thing of that sort intentionally.” The doctor stood up and put the shotgun in the corner behind the dresser.

> ==intentionally英 [ɪn'tenʃənəlɪ] 美 [ɪnˈtɛnʃənl:ɪ] adv. 有意地，故意地==

“Are you going out, dear?” his wife said. “I think I’ll go for a walk,” the doctor said.

If you see Nick, dear, will you tell him his mother wants to see him?” his wife said.

The doctor went out on the porch. The screen door slammed behind him.

He heard his wife catch her breath when the door slammed.

“Sorry,” he said, outside her windowwith the blinds drawn.

“It’s all right, dear,” she said.

He walked in the heat out the gate and along the path into the hemlockwoods.

It was cool in the woods even on such a hot day.

He found Nick sitting with his back against a tree, reading.

“Your mother wants you to come and see her,” the doctor said. “I want to go with you,” Nick said.

His father looked down at him. “All right. Come on, then,”

his father said. “Give me the book, I’ll put it in my pocket.”

“I know where there’s black squirrels, Daddy,” Nick said. “All right,” said his father. “Let’s go there.”

> ==squirrel英 [ˈskwɪrəl] 美 [ˈskwɜ:rəl] n. 松鼠==

### 背景知识

**💧Fireplace in Western Family**

**壁炉——西方家庭的标志物**

医生带着帮手来到岸边锯原木，就是为了能把它们做成小木料或者是敞口壁炉用的柴禾（...and cut the logs up with the cross-cut saw and split them with a wedge to make cord wood and chunks for the open fireplace）. 说到壁炉，它几乎已经成为西方家庭（寒冷地区）的一个标志物，除了发展历史悠久，还衍生出了不少文化和迷信传统——

壁炉（fireplace或masonry heater）是独立或者就墙壁砌成的室内取暖设备，以可燃物为能源，内部上通烟囱，起源于西方家庭或宫殿取暖设施。由于其燃料为可再生资源，加以现代化改进，目前仍然在西方普遍使用，尤其在主张环保理念的高等教育阶层受到欢迎。壁炉分开放式和封闭式两种，后者热效率高的多。

开放式壁炉

早期人们在小屋或住处的中心挖一个浅坑，在其中放置木材生火取暖。燃烧产生的烟从屋顶的洞冒出。几千年后，随着两层建筑的出现，人们将壁炉移到建筑的外面。这时候的壁炉仍然是水平式的，因此常常将烟吹到外面，或是飘进室内。后来，利用烟囱将烟带到住处的外面，解决了这个困扰。

1578年的时候，Prince Ruppert建立改良气流和排放系统的壁炉炉囱。在18世纪时壁炉有两次重要的发展。Ben Franklin建立一个对流室，大大的改进壁炉和燃木室（wood stoves）的效率。而且，他在火堆的下方空出一个空间（basement）吸入空气，以造成一个由下往上的气流，将废气带到较高处。在18世纪后期，Count Rumford设计出一个高且浅的燃烧室，使其有更好的排气效果，能将废气往上引导且排放至屋外。

Rumford的设计是现代壁炉的基础。在北美和欧洲，在气候上较冷的地方，壁炉一直是一个家庭的主要特点，因为它给人们温暖，而得以渡过漫长冬季。烘烤温暖的感觉，和跳跃与闪烁的火焰，即使到了今天，依然让人在寒冷天气下觉得愉快。

由于壁炉的特殊重要性，它和人们的生活以及文化也产生了或大或小的联系。比如有这样一个仪式：在点燃炉火的时候，把和周围人数一样多的小石头放置在壁炉中，如果第二天早上如果有一块石头被挪动，主人就会在这一年去世。另外在多塞特的礼拜五节，在壁炉中悬挂一块烤面包据说会保证来年五谷丰登。

对于西方家庭来说，只要有条件，壁炉绝对是不可或缺的东西。虽然国内也有设计有壁炉的房屋，但一般受限于房屋结构，采暖方式大都是集中供暖，所以壁炉只作为装饰用，实用价值不大。 

### 课文理解

这个短篇的标题里提及的The Doctor是海明威另一篇故事《印第安人营地》（*Indian Camp*）里的主角，讲述的是他带着儿子Nick到印第安人那儿为一位难产的孕妇接生，并且展现出了重压下从容不迫的风度。但在今天的故事里，这位医生则显露了与之前截然不同的一面，也就是他的伪善之处。

当他的其中一位雇工Dick既调侃又鄙夷地说到他把河滩边的原木锯下来带回家无异于偷窃时——这些木头是从开往锯木厂的轮船上遗失下来的，之后很有可能会有轮船工人来回收（The logs had been lost from the big log booms that were towed down the lake to the mill by the steamer Magic）——医生恼羞成怒，因为自己就这么被堂而皇之地当成了窃贼（事实也的确如此）。



💧**Clue 1**: The Doctor is angrily embarrassed and shamed by being known as a thief.



**Evidence 1**: Dick Boulton turned to Nick’s father. “Well, Doc,” he said, “that’s a nice lot of timber you’ve stolen.” “Don’t talk that way, Dick,” the doctor said. “It’s driftwood.”

迪克·博尔顿对尼克的父亲回过头来说：“我说，医生，”他说，“你偷到了好大一批木材啊。”

“别这么说，迪克，”医生说。“这是飘上岸来的木头。”



**Evidence 2**: “Don’t get huffy, Doc,” said Dick. “Don’t get huffy. I don’t care who you steal from. It’s none of my business.” “If you think the logs are stolen, leave them alone and take your tools back to the camp,” the doctor said. His face was red.

“别发火啊，医生。”迪克说。“别发火。我才不管你是偷谁的。这不关我的事。”

“你要是认为木头是偷来的，就不锯算了，带着你的工具会营地去。”医生说。他的脸都红了。



医生气冲冲地回到了家，并且向妻子讲述了经过。他还猜想这个印第安人Dick可能是为了拖欠之前医生治好他妻子肺炎的医疗费，才故意找茬和医生吵架，接着被医生赶走得以脱身。（“Well, Dick owes me a lot of money for pulling his squaw through pneumonia and I guess he wanted a row so he wouldn’t have to take it out in work.”）



但医生的妻子认为他是恶意揣测（“Dear, I don’t think, I really don’t think that any one would really do a thing like that.”）还用《圣经》里的道义来教育他（“Remember, that he who ruleth his spirit is greater than he that taketh a city,” said his wife）. 医生又走回到林子里，他的儿子Nick显然察觉出了发生的一切，并且他也用实际行动来表明自己站在父亲的一边——



💧**Clue 2**:  The Doctor's son Nick is on his side.



**Evidence 1**: “Are you going out, dear?” his wife said. “I think I’ll go for a walk,” the doctor said. “If you see Nick, dear, will you tell him his mother wants to see him?” his wife said.

“你这是要出去走吗，亲爱的？”他的妻子说。

“我想出去走走。”医生说。

“亲爱的，你要是看见尼克，请跟他说妈妈要找他，行吗？”妻子说。



**Evidence 2**: He found Nick sitting with his back against a tree, reading. “Your mother wants you to come and see her,” the doctor said. “I want to go with you,” Nick said. His father looked down at him. “All right. Come on, then,” his father said.

他看见尼克背靠着一棵树坐着，正在看书。

“你母亲要你进去看看她。”医生说。

“我要跟你一起去。”尼克说。

他父亲低头看着他。“行啊，那就快走吧。”他父亲说。



医生和妻子的处世态度及方式截然不同，这里俩人的矛盾虽然没有在明面上展现，但也暗暗埋下了紧张的气氛。临出门前，妻子最后“发号施令”，让儿子Nick进来找妈妈。但医生见到儿子传达后，Nick并没有服从母亲的传令，而是选择了跟父亲待在一起。说明儿子其实对父亲和母亲之间的对立矛盾有所察觉，在这种情况下，他选择和父亲一起走的用意就十分明显了。



因此也有很多人认为，这篇小说投射了海明威对母亲甚至是母性权威的厌恶和逃避（他自小和父亲亲密，但和母亲十分疏远）。这也解释了为什么海明威的小说中女性角色塑造往往有缺失和偏颇，而他打造的硬汉形象则深入人心。

### 今日彩蛋

**💧Fun Facts About Squirrels**

**松鼠趣闻**



儿子Nick最后说要带父亲一起去看黑色的松鼠（“I know where there’s black squirrels, Daddy,” Nick said. “All right,” said his father. “Let’s go there.”）松鼠在国外是一种很常见的动物，今天的彩蛋我们就来了解一下关于松鼠的那些趣事秘闻吧~



\1. Food 食物

松鼠除了喜欢吃坚果，其实也会以小型昆虫、草根、树皮、树叶和橡子为食（Aside from the famous love of nuts, the facts are these furry friends of ours can also dine on small insects, roots, tree bark, leaves and acorns）.

虽然松鼠一年四季都有储藏食物的习惯，但是到了秋天尤甚（Squirrels will typically gather and save a lot of their food all year round but this is definitely true when it comes to the autumn time）. 他们会到处搜集坚果并且埋起来，冬天一走，他们就会从休眠中醒过来然后去找过冬前埋下的食物（After they have buried all of their food and when winter comes and goes, the squirrel will wake up out of hibernation and go look for the food they buried）.



\2. Apperance 样貌

松鼠的英文名称squirrel其实来自古希腊语的Skiouros, 意思是“shadow tail”（“像黑影一样的尾巴”），这是因为松鼠的尾巴毛发旺盛，看起来毛茸茸的（brushy and fluffy）, 像把刷子一样。

在全球，松鼠的种类多达200多种（In fact, there are 200 different kinds of Squirrels worldwide）. 其中最著名的一种是“飞天松鼠”（the flying squirrel）, 它们的身体有和蝙蝠及其他滑行哺乳动物相似的特殊结构——“翼膜”（patagium）, 这就使得它们可以在空中飞行（to glide through the air）. 科学家还声称，飞天松鼠从150英尺高的地方急速俯冲下来都没问题（They could daringly take the plunge from 150 feet）.

另外，全世界最小的松鼠品种，身形不过比一只普通茶杯大不了几英寸（just a few inches bigger than a typical teacup）. 这种松鼠来自于非洲，身长只有大约10厘米。而世界上最大的松鼠（Alpine Marmot）体长则可以达到73厘米。



\3. Birth 出生

成年松鼠的视力非常好，但刚出生的松鼠其实是什么也看不见的，相当于全盲（Despitehaving perfect vision as adults, baby squirrels are blind at birth）.

松鼠妈妈每年最多生两胎，一次在春天，另一次在夏天快结束的时候（Once in the spring time and once at the end of the summer）. 一胎一般生2到8个小松鼠，松鼠宝宝也会称作kitten（kitten也可以指刚出生的小猫哦~）。在接下来的几个月里，松鼠宝宝都靠母乳喂养成长，之后才能独立出去觅食（After that, these individuals grow mature and can fully hunt for food themselves）.



\4. Behavior 行为

当松鼠们聚集在一起生活的时候，它们往往会发展出一种“同志情谊”（camaraderie）, 表现为一种利他主义（altruism）. 比如当危险靠近的时候，它们会向同伴发出警告并一起协同躲避捕食者（When they feel that there is danger approaching. They produce warning calls to alert their fellow rodents from lurking predators）.

而发现危险并进行预警的那只松鼠会特地留到最后才离开。如果不是强烈的利他主义精神，它肯定第一个就溜之大吉了！

一般松鼠住在树洞里（the holes of trunks）或者是树梢上乌鸦遗弃的鸟窝里（in the treetop in abandoned crow's nests）. 到了一岁左右，它们开始寻找配偶，这时候它们才会找筑巢的地方（Squirrels will usually start looking for a nest when they start to mate）.

## Chapter 4

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/358d569eb8ff3bfb61503ef0caf37b2f-sz_545771.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

The End of Something

In the old days Hortons Bay was a lumbering town.

No one who lived in it was out of sound of the big saws in the mill by the lake.

> <font color=red>In the old days Hortons Bay was alumbering town. No one who lived in it was out of sound of the big saws in the mill by the lake.</font>
>
> 霍斯顿湾早先是一座伐木重镇。住在城里的人每一个不听见湖边锯木厂里拉大锯的声音。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①lumber 指“木材，木料”，加上-ing变成名词，指“木材业”，包括砍伐、运输、加工、出售木材等一系列活动（the business or trade of cutting, transporting, preparing, or selling timber）.
>
> ②out of the sound of “没有听见，少了……的声音”；out of是“缺乏，没有”的（having none left）意思，比如out of breath指“喘不过气来”。

Then one year there were no more logs to make lumber.

The lumber schooners came into the bay and were loaded with the cut of the mill that stood stacked in the yard.

> ==schooner英 [ˈsku:nə(r)] 美 [ˈskunɚ] n. （有两个以上桅杆的）纵帆船==

All the piles of lumber were carried away.

The big mill building had all its machinery that was removable taken out and hoisted on board one of the schooners by the men who had worked in the mill.

> <font color=red>The big mill building / had all its machinery /that was removable / taken out / and hoisted /on board one of the schooners / by the men / who had worked in the mill.</font>
>
> 那大厂房里凡是能搬动的机械都被搬出来，由原先在厂里干活的工人吊上其中一艘双桅帆船。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> 我们先提炼出这句话的主谓：The big mill building had...taken out and hoisted... 这里是have sth done的结构，“让（某事）被做”，所以是大厂房里面的东西“被”搬出来并吊起来。后面by引导的介词短语结构就说明了这些动作的实际发出者是谁：by the men who had worked in the mill “原先厂里干活的工人”。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①all its machinery that was removable “（大厂房里）凡是能搬动的机械”；machinery是“机械”的总称（referring to machines in general）, 因此是集合名词，不可数。它也可以抽象为“组织，机构，体制”，比如：There is no machinery for resolving disputes.（根本没有解决纷争的机制。）
>
> ②hoist 指“吊起，升起”（to raise or pull sth up to a higher position, often using ropes or special equipment）, 比如“升旗/帆”就是hoist a flag/sail.
>
> ③on board one of the schooners “（被吊）上其中一艘双桅帆船”；on board一般指“上（船、飞机、火车）等”，在这里替换成onto会更好理解，也就是：onto one of the schooners.

The schooner moved out of the bay toward the open lake, carrying the two great saws,

the travelling carriage that hurled the logs against the revolving, circular saws and all the rollers, wheels, belts and iron piled on a hull-deep load of lumber.

Its open hold covered with canvas and lashed tight, the sails of the schooner filled and it moved out into the open lake, carrying with it everything that had made the mill a mill and Hortons Bay a town.

> ==lash==
>
> vt. 捆绑，捆扎（to tie something tightly to something else with a rope）
>
> n. （复数）眼睫毛；鞭打（a hit with a whip, especially as a punishment）
>
> 原文： Its open hold covered with canvas andlashed tight...
>
> 露天货舱上盖着帆布，系得紧紧的……
>
> 💧lash 在这里是“捆绑”的意思，相当于bind/tie.lash还有“鞭打”的意思，引申出“抨击”的含义（常指报纸上的），比如：Democrats lashedRepublican plans, calling them extreme.
>
> 民主党猛烈抨击共和党的计划，说是太极端了。

The one-story bunk houses, the eating-house, the company store, the mill offices, and the big mill itself stood deserted in the acres of sawdust that covered the swampy meadow by the shore of the bay.

> ==swampy英 ['swɒmpɪ] 美 [ ˈswɑmpɪ] adj. 沼泽的;似沼泽的，软而湿的==

Ten years later there was nothing of the mill left except the broken white limestone of its foundations showing through the swampy second growth as Nick and Marjorie rowed along the shore.

> ==limestone英 [ˈlaɪmstəʊn] 美 [ˈlaɪmstoʊn] n. 石灰岩，石灰石==

They were trolling along the edge of the channel-bank where the bottom dropped off suddenly from sandy shallows to twelve feet of dark water.

> <font color=red>They were trolling along the edge of the channel-bank where the bottom dropped offsuddenly from sandy shallows to twelve feet of dark water.</font>
>
> 他们正沿着航道边用拖曳线钓鱼，那边的水底从浅沙滩陡地下降到12英尺深的水域。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①troll along “沿着……拖钓”；troll指“用拖曳线钓鱼”，也就是在缓行的船尾后拖着钓丝钓鱼。troll还延伸出了“搜寻，询问”（to try to obtain something by searching, asking people etc）的意思，比如：Stewart spent hours trolling the Web for information.（斯图尔特花了很长时间在网上搜索信息。）
>
> ②drop off 表示“下降”（to become less）, 比如：Two years later, earnings from the stocks had dropped off by nearly 50%.（2年后，股票收益已下降了近50％。）

They were trolling on their way to set night lines for rainbow trout.

"There's our old ruin, Nick," Marjorie said.

Nick, rowing, looked at the white stone in the green trees. "There it is," he said.

"Can you remember when it was a mill?" Marjorie asked. "I can just remember," Nick said.

"It seems more like a castle," Marjorie said.

Nick said nothing. They rowed on out of sight of the mill, following the shore line. Then Nick cut across the bay.

"They aren't striking," he said.

"No," Marjorie said. She was intent on the rod all the time they trolled, even when she talked.

She loved to fish. She loved to fish with Nick.

Close beside the boat a big trout broke the surface of the water.

Nick pulled hard on one oar so the boat would turn and the bait, spinning far behind, would pass where the trout was feeding.

As the trout's back came up out of the water the minnows jumped wildly.

They sprinkled the surface like a handful of shot thrown into the water.

> ==sprinkle英 [ˈsprɪŋkl] 美 [ˈsprɪŋkəl] v. 洒，撒;用…点缀;下小雨 n. 小雨;少量==
>
> <font color=red>As the trout's back came up out of the water the minnows jumped wildly. They sprinkled the surface like a handful of shot thrown into the water.</font>
>
> 鳟鱼背露出水面的时候，那些可作饵的小鱼跳得正欢。它们跳得水面浪花四溅，像一梭枪弹射进水里似的。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①minnow 是多种小型鱼类的总称（a very small freshwater fish）, 这个词还可以用来指“无足轻重的小公司”（an organization or company that is small and unimportant）.
>
> ②widly 在这里不是“广泛地”，而是指“兴高采烈地”，相当于enthusiastically. 比如：She danced wildly to the tune.（她高兴地跟着曲调起舞。）
>
> ③sprinkled the surface “它们跳得水面浪花四溅”；sprinkle有“往……表面洒水滴”（to scatter in drops or particles）的意思，这里是指小鱼们跳起来的时候弄得水面浪花四溅。
>
> ④a handful of shot “一梭枪弹”；shot指“（猎枪用的）弹丸”，a handful of理解成“一把，一梭”。

Another trout broke water, feeding on the other side of the boat.

"They're feeding," Marjorie said.

"But they won't strike," Nick said.

He rowed the boat around to troll past both the feeding fish, then headed it for the point.

Marjorie did not reel in until the boat touched the shore.

They pulled the boat up the beach and Nick lifted out a pail of live perch.

The perch swam in the water pail. Nick caught three of them with his hands and cut heir heads off and skinned them while Marjorie chased with her hands in the bucket,

finally caught a perch, cut its head off and skinned it. Nick looked at her fish.

"You don't want to take the ventral fin out," he said. "It'll be all right for bait but it's better with the ventral finin."

He hooked each of the skinned perch through the tail.

There were two hooks attached to aleader on each rod.

Then Marjorie rowed the boat out over the channel-bank, holding the line in her teeth, and looking toward Nick, who stood on the shore holding the rod and letting the line run out from the reel.

"That's about right," he called.

"Should I let it drop?" Marjorie called back, holding the line in her hand.

"Sure. Let it go." Marjorie dropped the line overboard and watched the baits go down through the water.

> ==overboard==
>
> adv. 从船舷落入水中（over the side of a ship or boat into the water）
>
> 原文：Marjorie dropped the line overboard and watched the baits go down through the water.
>
> 玛乔丽把钓丝放到船舷外，眼望着鱼饵沉入水中。
>
> 💧overboard 表示“从船上，尤其是船舷的位置落入水中”，比如有人掉进水里了就会大喊Man overboard! 另外go overboard还可以表示“做事或说话过分、走极端”，比如：I hope politicians will not go overboard in trying to control the press.
>
> 我希望政客们在控制媒体方面不要做得太过分。

She came in with the boat and ran the second line out the same way.

Each time Nick set a heavy slab of driftwood across the butt of the rod to hold it solid and propped it up at an angle with a small slab.

He reeled in the slack line so the line ran taut out to where the bait rested on the sandy floor of the channel and set the click on the reel.

When a trout, feeding on the bottom, took the bait it would run with it, taking line out of the reel in a rush and making the reel sing with the click on.

Marjorie rowed up the point a little way so she would not disturb the line.

She pulled hard on the oars and the boat went up the beach. Little waves came in with it.

Marjorie stepped out of the boat and Nick pulled the boat high up the beach.

"What's the matter, Nick?" Marjorie asked.

"I don't know," Nick said, getting wood for a fire.

They made a fire with driftwood. Marjorie went to the boat and brought a blanket.

The evening breeze blew the smoke toward the point, so Marjorie spread the blanket out between the fire and the lake.

Marjorie sat on the blanket with her back to the fire and waited for Nick.

He came over and sat down beside her on the blanket.

In back of them was the close second-growth timber of the point and in front was the bay with the mouth of Hortons Creek.

It was not quite dark. The fire-light went as far as the water.

They could both see the two steel rods at an angle over the dark water. The fire glinted on the reels.

> ==glint英 [glɪnt] 美 [ɡlɪnt] vt.& vi. 闪烁，闪光;窥视;（箭一样）飞出;使发光，使闪光 n. 闪光，闪耀;短暂微弱的显露;（雷达的）回波起伏==
>
> ==reel英 [ri:l] 美 [ril] n. 卷轴;卷筒;卷盘;绕在卷轴上的线（或金属丝、胶卷等） vt. 卷;绕==

Marjorie unpacked the basket of supper. "I don't feel like eating," said Nick. "Come on and eat, Nick." "All right."

They ate without talking, and watched the two rods and the fire-light in the water.

"There's going to be a moon tonight," said Nick.

He looked across the bay to the hills that were beginning to sharpen against the sky.

Beyond the hills he knew the moon was coming up.

"I know it," Marjorie said happily. "You know everything," Nick said.

"Oh, Nick, please cut it out! Please, please don't be that way!"

"I can't help it," Nick said. "You do. You know everything. That's the trouble. You know you do." Marjorie did not say anything.

"I've taught you everything. You know you do. What don't you know, anyway?" "Oh, shut up," Marjorie said. "There comes the moon."

They sat on the blanket without touching each other and watched the moon rise. "You don't have to talk silly," Marjorie said. "What's really the matter?"

"I don't know." "Of course you know." "No I don't." "Go on and say it."

Nick looked on at the moon, coming up over the hills. "It isn't fun any more."

He was afraid to look at Marjorie. Then he looked at her.

She sat there with her back toward him. He looked at her back. "It isn't fun any more. Not any of it."

She didn't say anything. He went on.

"I feel as though everything was gone to hell inside of me. I don't know, Marge. I don't know what to say."

He looked on at her back."Isn't love any fun?" Marjorie said.

"No," Nick said. Marjorie stood up. Nick sat there, his head in his hands.

"I'm going to take the boat," Marjorie called to him. "You can walk back around the point."

"All right," Nick said. "I'll push the boat off for you."

"You don't need to," she said.

She was afloat in the boat on the water with the moonlight on it.

Nick went back and lay down with his face in the blanket by the fire. He could hear Marjorie rowing on the water.

He lay there for a long time. He lay there while he heard Bill come into the clearing walking around through the woods.

He felt Bill coming up to the fire. Billdidn't touch him, either.

"Did she go all right?" Bill said.

"Yes," Nick said, lying, his face on the blanket. "Have a scene?"

"No, there wasn't any scene." "How do you feel?"

"Oh, go away, Bill! Go away for a while."

Bill selected a sandwich from the lunch basket and walked over to have a look at the rods.

### 背景知识

**💧1. The vicissitudes of logging in America**

**美国伐木业的兴衰**

我们今天的故事发生在这样的背景之下：霍斯顿湾原来有丰富的木材资源，丰富的木材资源使这座城市变成木材业城市。但是现在由于木材已经开采完毕，城市开始衰败，木材工厂已经荡然无存（In the old days Hortons Bay was a lumbering town. No one who lived in it was out of sound of the big saws in the mill by the lake. Then one year there were no more logs to make lumber. ）我们今天一起来了解一下美国历史上真实存在的伐木业兴衰变迁。

美国伐木业兴起于17世纪，当英国的先驱者开始探索非洲大陆的茂密的原始森林时，美国的伐木业开始第一次腾飞。

加利福尼亚州的硬木对投资者特别有吸引力，18世纪90年代，新英格兰地区生产了36000000英尺松木板。在1840年至1900年，这里失去了大部分森林。

19世纪末到20世纪初，伐木工是个让人羡慕的职业。随着美国西部“淘金热”（Gold Rush）的兴起，成千上万人涌入加州淘金，伐木业也由此兴盛，并迅速成为美国西部最大的支柱产业。

当时，这些伐木工仅有斧子、锯子等简陋工具，却展现出了强大的破坏力，大片两三千年树龄、数十到上百米的红杉被砍伐倒下。

随着森林砍伐造成的环境问题越来越突出，美国社会对森林的认识观念也发生着变化。著名的浪漫主义作家夏多布利昂（Viscount De Chateaubriand）曾说过：“除了森林以外，美国没有什么是古老的。” 伟大的超验主义者亨利·梭罗（Henry David Thoreau）把森林所代表的荒野与人类文明相提并论，写道：“在荒野中世界得以保存！”

时光飞逝，百年过去，当时让人羡慕的伐木工却成为了一个濒临消失的职业。美国劳工局数据显示，2012年到2022年，预计伐木工的雇佣下滑率将达到43.3%，曾经盛极一时的伐木业已成明日黄花。

对自然环境的保护固然是让伐木业衰落的一个原因，另一方面，随着科技的进步，自动化的机器作业逐渐取代了传统人力劳动，导致伐木业大量劳动力过剩，大批伐木工人下岗。

\2. Autobiography

小说的自传性质

我们今天的短篇是海明威的半自传体小说，在1919年夏天，20岁的海明威与一个17岁的度假村服务生Marjorie Bump约会。Marjorie经常给海明威准备野餐的食物，他们会在夜晚的营火边用餐。在劳动节后Marjorie的暑期工作结束后，海明威又开始和其他人约会。文中虚构的人物Bill是以Bill Smith为原型，他是和海明威一起度过那个夏天的好朋友。

海明威很多短篇小说都以Nick Adams为主人公，比如：*Indian Camp*，*The Killers*等，他以自身为原型塑造了Nick，海明威和Nick拥有相似的经历，使这些短篇小说带有明显的自传性质。

在这些小说中Nick经历了生活的磨难，慢慢地体验和认识到了许多新的知识，学会了接受自己及现实世界的不如意之处。他所经历的这种从天真走向成熟、从依附走向独立、从盲从走向自主、从关注自我走向关注社会以及从无知走向自我完善的过程就是其从儿童期走向成年期，成为一名成熟的社会成员的过程。著名的评论家杨·菲力浦曾说 “典型的尼克·亚当斯故事就是成长故事。”

### 课文理解

今天故事的主角是长大后了的Nick（在The Doctor and the Doctor's Wife里出现的医生的儿子），他和一位叫作Marjorie的姑娘正在交往，并且一起来到霍尔顿斯湾（Hortons Bay）钓鱼。这一片地区曾经是伐木重镇，但是在伐木业衰落后，就只剩寥寥的遗迹来显示曾经的兴盛了。



因此标题The End of Something里的Something也是一个双关，它同时代表了伐木全盛时期的衰落（the end of the heydays of logging industry）以及Nick和女友Marjorie关系的结束. （the end of the romantic relationship between Nick and Marjorie）. 我们分别来看这两条主线是如何交叉联系在一起的——



💧**Clue 1**: The end of the heydays of logging industry.



**Evidence 1**: The one-story bunk houses, the eating-house, the company store, the mill offices, and the big mill itself stood deserted in the acres of sawdust that covered the swampy meadow by the shore of the bay.

一座座平房工棚、食堂、公司栈房、工厂办公室和大厂房本身都空无一人，留在湖湾边潮湿的草地上大片大片的锯木屑中。



**Evidence 2**: "There's our old ruin, Nick," Marjorie said.

Nick, rowing, looked at the white stone in the green trees. "There it is," he said.

"Can you remember when it was a mill?" Marjorie asked.

"I can just remember," Nick said.

"It seems more like a castle," Marjorie said.

Nick said nothing.

“那就是我们那老厂的废墟，尼克。”玛乔丽说。

尼克一边划着船，一边看着绿树从里的白石。“就在这儿。”他说。

“你还记得当初这是个工厂的情景吗？”玛乔丽问。

“我就快不记得了。”尼克说。

“看上去更像座城堡。”玛乔丽说。

尼克一言不发。



这里就已经为Nick和Marjorie的分手埋下了伏笔。Marjorie看到废墟的时候觉得它们就像城堡一样，但Nick并没有对她的这种浪漫联想（romantic imagination）作出任何回应，凸显出了他的兴致寡然以及冷淡疏离。尔后俩人上岸野餐，结果爆发了争吵——



💧**Clue 2**: The end of the romantic relationship betwen Nick and Marjorie.



**Evidence 1**: "It isn't fun any more." He was afraid to look at Marjorie. Then he looked at her. She sat there with her back toward him. He looked at her back. "It isn't fun any more. Not any of it."

“再也没劲了。”他不敢对玛乔丽看。过了会儿才对她看。她背朝着他，坐在那儿。他看着她的背影。“再也没劲儿了。一点劲儿也没了。”



**Evidence 2**: She didn't say anything. He went on. "I feel as though everything was gone to hell inside of me. I don't know, Marge. I don't know what to say." He looked on at her back.

"Isn't love any fun?" Marjorie said.

"No," Nick said.

她一言不发。他径自说下去。“我感到心里万念俱灰。我不知道，玛吉（Marge是Marjorie的昵称）。我不知道说什么才好。”他继续看着她的背影。

“难道爱情也没劲儿？”玛乔丽说。

“对。”尼克说。



Marjorie十分生气，走的时候连Nick提出帮她把船推下水的请求也拒绝了（Nick said. "I'll push the boat off for you. "You don't need to," she said.）但故事的紧张氛围并没有以此为结束，最后出现的一幕可以说才是整篇小说的点睛之笔：Nick在空地上躺了一会儿，他的朋友Bill出现了，Bill开口的第一句话就是："Did she go all right?"（“她当真走了吗？”）接着又问道："Have a scene?"（“吵了一场？”）



为什么不在场的Bill知道Nick和Marjorie提了分手呢？只能说明Nick其实早有计划并且一直在酝酿，而不是一时冲动做的决定（not spur-of-the-moment）. 这样也解释了Nick为什么在钓鱼的过程中表现冷淡，甚至还刻意找茬和Marjorie闹不愉快（"I know it," Marjorie said happily. "You know everything," Nick said. "Oh, Nick, please cut it out! Please, please don't be that way!"）



和Marjorie分手也并没有让Nick多好受（"How do you feel?" "Oh, go away, Bill! Go away for a while."）而他具体的心理活动和想法并没有再展开描述。作者把这一部分留在了我们下一个短篇小说The Three-Day Blow里：山顶小屋外大风刮了三天，借此Nick也向Bill袒露了自己的真实感受，他究竟是追悔莫及还是对于自己的选择坚定不移呢？我们一起期待明天的故事吧~

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****Second-growth/Secondary Forest**

**次生林**

在我们今天的内容中有这样的场景：十年以后，尼克和玛乔丽沿岸划着船来，这里除了厂基那断裂的白灰石露出在沼泽地的次生林之外，工厂已荡然无存。（Ten years later there was nothing of the mill left except the broken white limestone of its foundations showing through the swampy second growth as Nick and Marjorie rowed along the shore.）那么什么是次生林呢，我们一起来了解一下吧～

关于次生林的定义，国内外多有不同。中国的定义为：次生林是原始林或人工林经人为或自然破坏之后未经合理经营，又借助自然力恢复起来的一类天然林。国际热带木材组织（International Tropical Timber Organization)的定义为：次生林是在原始林植被遭受破坏后形成的裸露土地上再生的林木植被，这种次生植被是以自然的方式在游垦地、农地、牧地或培育用材林不成功的废弃地上自然发育和演替的。ITTO还将强度干扰后暂以灌木和杂草为主的林地称为“退化林地”。各种定义都认为：次生林来源于原始林遭受干扰后形成的裸地，并以天然恢复为主。

次生林可分为以下类型：过度采伐的次生林（post-extraction secondary forests）；弃耕后恢复的次生林（swidden fallow secondary forests）；火灾引起的次生林（post-fire forests）；人工恢复的次生林（rehabilitated secondary forests）.

次生林涵盖了从裸地到已接近天然林的所有次生植被类型，它以区域形式存在，或许也会镶嵌有少量的原始林或人工林。特别重要的是，次生林区域是山区居民主要的生产和生活场所，因此次生林受到的人类社会压力比一般森林资源更大。次生林代表着一种日益重要的森林资源，如果得到正确的经营，它完全能够为地方、国家和国际社会提供所需要的各种财产与服务。

次生林占全球森林面积的近60%，其余的是天然林、人工林和经济林等。从这个意义上说，只有次生林实现了可持续经营，才会真正地实现森林可持续经营目标。次生林的重要性体现在：维系社区生态环境和居民生计，满足木材及其他各种林产品需求，具有环境战略价值。次生林的可持续经营和利用是一个战略性问题。



位于英国牛津郡泰晤士河上游盆地的中心的威萨姆森林（Wytham woods），为牛津大学所有， 被称为淡褐色（Hazel）的森林，是落叶林地和草地的美丽集合。它的林地大致分为三个区域：原生代、次生林和种植园林。其中次生林地占地面积三分之一，是曾经用于牧草或种植的地区，但自然恢复到林地。

## Chapter 5.1

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/adfba303c395dbb1b22c995825e08e4f-sz_778644.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

The Three-Day Blow

The rain stopped as Nick turned into the road that went up through the orchard.

The fruit had been picked and the fall wind blew through the bare trees.

Nick stopped and picked up a Wagner apple from beside the road,shiny in the brown grass from the rain. He put the apple in the pocket of his Mackinaw coat.

The road came out of the orchard on to the top of the hill.

There was the cottage, the porch bare, smoke coming from the chimney.

In back was the garage, the chickencoop and the second-growth timber like a hedge against the woods behind.

The big trees swayed far over in the wind as he watched.

> ==sway[sweɪ] vi. 摇摆;摆动;摇晃 vt. 影响;使改变看法 n. 影响力;支配;摇摆，摆动==

It was the first of the autumn storms.

As Nick crossed the open field above the orchard the door of the cottage opened and Bill came out. He stood on the porch looking out.

"Well, Wemedge," he said.

"Hey, Bill," Nick said, coming up thesteps.
