They stood together, looking out across the country, down over the orchard, beyond the road, across the lower fields and the woods of the point to the lake.

> <font color=red>They stood together, looking out across the country, down over the orchard, beyond the road, across the lower fields and the woods of the point to the lake.</font>
>
> 他们站在一起，眺望着原野，从下面的果园望到大路下边，目光掠过低处的田野和那地岬上的林子，一直望到那湖上。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> 这句话的主谓其实非常短，也就是They stood. 其余的部分则是以looking out为首的现在分词短语作伴随状语，其中包含多个介词结构：looking out across...down over...beyond...across...to...
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> the woods of the point “地岬上的林子”；point指“尖岬，岬角”（a long thin piece of land that stretches out into the sea），即陆地伸入海洋的一端。比如：We sailed round the point into a small, sheltered bay.（我们驾船绕过岬角驶入一个小小的避风港。）

The wind was blowing straight down the lake. They could see the surf along Ten Mile point.

"She's blowing," Nick said.

"She'll blow like that for three days,"Bill said.

"Is your dad in?" Nick said. "No. He’s out with the gun. Come on in."

Nick went inside the cottage. There was a big fire in the fireplace.

The wind made it roar. Bill shut the door.

"Have a drink?" he said.

He went out to the kitchen and came back with two glasses and a pitcher of water.

> ==pitcher[ˈpɪtʃɚ] n. 投手;壶，罐;双柄陶罐==

Nick reached the whisky bottle from the shelf above the fireplace.

"All right?" he said. "Good," said Bill.

They sat in front of the fire and drank the Irish whisky and water.

"It's got a swell, smoky taste," Nick said, and looked at the fire through the glass.

“That’s the peat,” Bill said.

“You can’t get peat into liquor,” Nick said.

“That doesn’t make any difference,” Bill said.

“You ever seen any peat?” Nick asked. “No,” said Bill.

“Neither have I,” Nick said.

His shoes, stretched out on the hearth, began to steam in front of the fire.

“Better take your shoes off,” Bill said. “I haven’t got any socks on.”

“Take them off and dry them and I’ll get you some,” Bill said.

He went upstairs into the loft and Nick heard him walking about overhead.

Upstairs was open under the roof and was where Bill and his father and he, Nick, sometimes slept.

In back was a dressing room. They moved the cots back out of the rain and covered them with rubber blankets.

Bill came down with a pair of heavy wool socks.

"It’s getting too late to go around without socks,” he said.

“I hate to start them again,” Nick said.

He pulled the socks on and slumped back in the chair, putting his feet up on the screen in front of the fire.

“You’ll dent in the screen,” Bill said. Nick swung his feet over to the side of the fireplace.

“Got anything to read?” he asked. “Only the paper.”

“What did the Cards do?” “Dropped a double header to the Giants.”

“That ought to cinch it for them.” “It’s a gift,” Bill said.

> <font color=red>“What did the Cards do?”</font>
>
> “Dropped a double header to the Giants.”
>
> “That ought to cinch it for them.”
>
> “卡斯队打得怎么样？”
>
> “一天连续两场比赛都输给了巨人队。”
>
> “这下子他们该稳赢了。”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①dropped a double header to “一天连续两场比赛都输给了”；drop to sb指“输给某人”，也可以用drop behind sb来表示“落后某人”, 比如：We cannot afford to drop behind our competitors.（我们可担当不起落后于竞争对手的后果。）
>
> double header指“连续举行的两场棒球赛”（two baseball games played one after the other），传统上在星期日，通常为相同的两个队。
>
> ②cinch 表示“确保，稳保”（to make something certain to happen）, 比如：They cinched a place in the play-off.（他们稳稳当当地进入了季后赛。）这里的cinch it for them是指“确保他们能赢得比赛” ，it指to win the game.
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> Cards（卡斯队）是美国圣路易市的卡迪纳尔棒球队的简称；Giants（巨人队）是美国纽约市的著名棒球队。

“As long as McGraw can buy every good ball player in the league there’s nothing to it.”

> <font color=red>“It’s a gift,” Bill said. “As long as McGraw can buy every good ball player in the league there’s nothing to it.”</font>
>
> “这是白送的，”比尔说。“只要麦克劳在球队俱乐部联合会中能收买每一个好球员，就没什么问题。”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①gift 指“不费力就得到的东西”，比如：The third goal was an absolute gift.（第三个进球简直不费吹灰之力。）
>
> ②there's nothing to it 表示“做某事没有困难，很容易”，常用语口语中，比如：Anyone can use a computer. There’s nothing to it!（人人都会用电脑，很简单的！）
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> McGraw即美国球星“约翰·麦克劳”（1875-1934），1902-1932年担任巨人队教练。

“He can’t buy them all,” Nick said.

“He buys all the ones he wants,” Bill said.

“Or he makes them discontented so they have to trade them to him.”

“Like Heinie Zim,” Nick agreed. “That bonehead will do him a lot of good.”

Bill stood up.“He can hit,” Nick offered.

The heat from the fire was baking his legs.

“He’s a sweet fielder, too,” Bill said. “But he loses ball games.”

“Maybe that’s what McGraw wants him for,” Nick suggested.

“Maybe,” Bill agreed.“There’s always more to it than we know about,” Nick said.

“Of course. But we’ve got pretty good dope for being so far away.”

“Like how much better you can pick them if you don’t see the horses.” “That’s it.”

> <font color=red>“Of course. But we’ve got pretty good dope for being so far away.”</font>
>
> “Like how much better you can pick them if you don’t see the horses.”
>
> “那当然。不过我们虽然隔得那么远，精彩的内幕消息倒不少。”
>
> “就像你虽然没有看见那些赛马，反而选马眼力更强。”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①pretty good dope “精彩的内幕消息”；the dope on sb/sth指“有关某人或某事的内幕消息”，比如：What’s the dope on the new guy?（有什么关于这个新来的家伙的内部消息？）
>
> ②for being so far away “我们虽然隔得那么远”；for在这里理解为“就…而言”，一般表示令人惊讶的语气，比如：She looks young for her age.（就她的年龄而言，她看上去算是年轻的。）

Bill reached down the whisky bottle. His big hand went all the way around it.

He poured the whisky into the glassNick held out.

“How much water?” “Just the same.”

He sat down on the floor beside Nick’s chair.

“It’s good when the fall storms come, isn’t it?” Nick said. “It’s swell.”

“It’s the best time of year,” Nick said.

“Wouldn’t it be hell to be in town?” Bill said.

“I’d like to see the World Series,” Nick said.

“Well, they’re always in New York or Philadelphia now,” Bill said.

“That doesn’t do us any good.” “I wonder if the Cards will ever win a pennant?”

“Not in our lifetime,” Bill said. “Gee, they’d go crazy,” Nick said.

“Do you remember when they got going that once before they had the train wreck?”

“Boy!” Nick said, remembering.

Bill reached over to the table under the window for the book that lay there, face down, where he had put it when he went to the door.

He held his glass in one hand and the book in the other, leaning back against Nick’s chair.

“What are you reading?” “Richard Feverel.” “I couldn’t get into it.”

“It’s all right,” Bill said. “It ain’t a badbook, Wemedge.”

“What else have you got I haven’t read?” Nick asked. “Did you read the Forest Lovers?”

“Yup. That’s the one where they go to bed every night with the naked sword between them.”

“That’s a good book, Wemedge.”

“It’s a swell book. What I couldn’t ever understand was what good the sword would do.

It would have to stay edge up all the time because if it went over flat you could roll right over it and it wouldn’t make any trouble.”

> <font color=red>"It would have to stay edge up all the time because if it went over flat you could roll right over it and it wouldn’t make any trouble."</font>
>
> “我始终搞不懂的是这把剑有什么用处。它得一直剑锋朝上，因为如果翻到了，你就能径直滚过去，不会出什么乱子。”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①stay edge up “一直剑锋朝上”；edge指剑的“锋刃处”，a knife with a sharp edge就是“刀刃锋利的小刀”；
>
> ②go over flat “翻倒”；go over指“侧翻”，flat作副词，表示“平直地，平坦地”，比如：That night I lay flat on my back and stared up at the ceiling.（那一夜，我仰面平躺，眼睛直直地盯着天花板。）
>
> *这里Nick谈论的是前面提到的*Forest Lovers*里的情节，两个情人睡在一张床上，但中间立着一把锋刃朝上的剑。

“It’s a symbol,” Bill said.“Sure” said Nick, “but it isn’t practical.”

“Did you ever read Fortitude?” “It’s fine,” Nick said.

“That’s a real book. That’s where his old man is after him all the time.Have you got any more by Walpole?”

“The Dark Forest,” Bill said. “It’s about Russia.”

“What does he know about Russia?”Nick asked.

“I don’t know. You can’t ever tell about those guys.

Maybe he was there when he was aboy. He’s got a lot of dope on it.”

“I’d like to meet him,” Nick said.

“I’d like to meet Chesterton,” Bill said.

“I wish he was here now,” Nick said.“We’d take him fishing to the ’Voix tomorrow.”

“I wonder if he’d like to go fishing,” Bill said.

“Sure,” said Nick. “He must be about the best guy there is. Do you remember the Flying Inn?”

“‘If an angel out of heaven gives you something else to drink.

Thank him for his kind intentions; Go and pour them down the sink.’”

“That’s right,” said Nick. “I guess he’s a better guy than Walpole.”

“Oh, he’s a better guy, all right,” Bill said.

"But Walpole’s a better writer." "I don’t know," Nick said.

“Chesterton’s a classic.” “Walpole’s a classic, too,” Bill insisted.

“I wish we had them both here,” Nick said. “We’d take them both fishing to the ’Voix tomorrow.”

“Let’s get drunk,” Bill said.“All right,” Nick agreed.

“My old man won’t care,” Bill said.

“Are you sure?” said Nick.“I know it,” Bill said.

“I’m a little drunk now,” Nick said. “You aren’t drunk,” Bill said.

He got up from the floor and reached for the whisky bottle.

Nick held out his glass. His eyes fixed on it while Bill poured.

Bill poured the glass half full of whisky.

“Put in your own water,” he said. “There’s just one more shot.”

“Got any more?” Nick asked.“There’s plenty more but dad only likes me to drink what’s open.”

“Sure,” said Nick.“He says opening bottles is what makes drunkards,” Bill explained.

“That’s right,” said Nick. He was impressed.

He had never thought of that before.

He had always thought it was solitary drinking that made drunkards.

> ==solitary[ˈsɑːləteri] adj. 单个的;单独的;独处的 n. 单独监禁;隐士==
>
> adj. 独自的, 单独的 (done alone; without other people)
>
> 原文：He had always thought it was solitarydrinking that made drunkards.
>
> 他一向总是认为只有独自喝闷酒才会成为酒鬼呢。
>
> 💧solitary还有“唯一的，仅有的 ”的意思，比如：There was not a solitary shred of evidence (= none at all) .
>
> 一丁点证据都没有。

“How is your dad?” he asked respectfully.

“He’s all right,” Bill said. “He gets a little wild sometimes.”

“He’s a swell guy,” Nick said. He poured water into his glass out of the pitcher.

It mixed slowly with the whisky. There was more whisky than water.

“You bet your life he is,” Bill said. “My old man’s all right,” Nick said. “You’re damn right he is,” said Bill.

“He claims he’s never taken a drink in his life,” Nick said, as though announcing a scientific fact.

“Well, he’s a doctor. My old man’s apainter. That’s different.”

“He’s missed a lot,” Nick said sadly.

“You can’t tell.” Bill said. “Everything’s got its compensations.”

> ==compensation[ˌkɑːmpenˈseɪʃn] n. 补偿费，赔偿金;补偿;报酬==
>
> n. 补偿，使坏的情况变好的事物（things that make a bad situation better）
>
> 原文：Everything’s got its compensations.
>
> 万事有失必有所得。
>
> 💧compensation还有“赔偿金”的意思，比如：He received one year's salary ascompensation for loss of office.
>
> 他得到一年的工资作为失业赔偿金。

“He says he’s missed a lot himself,” Nick confessed.

> ==confess[kənˈfes] vt.&vi. 坦白，招认;承认;忏悔==

“Well, dad’s had a tough time,” Bill said. “It all evens up,” Nick said.

They sat looking into the fire and thinking of this profound truth.

“I’ll get a chunk from the back porch,” Nick said.

He had noticed while looking into the fire that the fire was dying down.

Also he wished to show he could hold his liquor and be practical.

Even if his father had never toucheda drop Bill was not going to get him drunk before he himself was drunk.

“Bring one of the big beech chunks,” Bill said. He was also being consciously practical.

### 背景知识

**💧****美国职业棒球大联盟**

**Major League Basebal（缩写：MLB）**

我们今天的内容中提到了Nick和Bill围着炉火聊到了美国职业棒球锦标赛（“I’d like to see the World Series,” Nick said. “Well, they’re always in New York or Philadelphia now,” Bill said.）今天我们就一起来了解一下美国职业棒球赛吧～

美国职业棒球大联盟（MLB），是目前世界上最高水准的职业棒球赛事。他共有30支球队，每个球队都在自己的城市有自己的球场。有些历史悠久的球队，球场也同样拥有独特的人文底蕴。球场的周边往往会形成繁华的商业区域，不仅仅是本地球迷享受休闲生活的好去处，也是国外旅游者乐于体验美国文化风韵的地标。

常规的赛季，在每年的4-9月份，遵循着规定的交叉赛程，每支球队要和联盟中大多数的球队交手，162场比赛里有81场在自己的球场（主场 home court），另外81场要去到对手的场地（客场 away ground）。每个对手的系列赛在3-4场左右。

随着常规赛事的推进，MLB会组织球迷根据球员上半段的表现进行网络票选，将自己喜欢的球员选出来组成2支全明星队伍，在8月份常规赛季中期，进行对决。大牌明星球员云集，让你一次看个尽兴。入选全明星赛，对球员来说也是极大的荣誉。

而精彩绝伦的季后赛则是常规赛季中战绩最佳队伍的终极对决。通常在金秋十月进行。也被称为“经典十月”（Classic October），近年由于季后赛环节经常有抢七出现，世界大赛巅峰争冠赛也会被拖进十一月初。但即使初冬的寒风也不会影响到比赛的精彩程度和球迷的激情。

棒球是对身体的条件要求并不太高的运动，更多的是靠智慧和意志。比如打者的选球，捕手的配球，投手的自信程度等等。MLB是一个世界的熔炉，MLB的球员有来自美国本土普通中产的孩子甚至哈佛大学的名校毕业生，也有来自拉美棒球训练营的充满梦想的小球员，古巴的职业球员，日本职业棒球的明星球员等等。

### 课文理解

今天的故事《三日狂风》（*The Three-Day Blow*）是《了却一段情》（*The End of Something*）的续篇。Nick来到山顶上Bill的小屋里（The road came out of the orchard on to the top of the hill. There was the cottage...）而故事开篇，作者就交待了当时的环境——正好是秋天的第一场风暴，为之后的故事发展埋下了伏笔——

💧**Clue 1**: There is the first of the autumn storms.



**Evidence 1**: The big trees swayed far over in the wind as he watched. It was the first of the autumn storms.

那些大树在远方的高处在风中摇摆着。这是秋天的头一场风暴。



**Evidence 2**: The wind was blowing straight down the lake. They could see the surf along Ten Mile point.

“She’s blowing,” Nick said.

“She’ll blow like that for three days,” Bill said.

大风正直扫湖面。他们看得见那十里岬沿岸的浪花。

“在刮风呢。”尼克说。

“这样刮要连刮三天。”比尔说。



Nick和Bill俩人开始有一搭没一搭地聊起天来，从棒球锦标赛到各种书籍和作家，其中提到的许多书本正好也是当时海明威和他的朋友Bill Smith俩人正在读的，主要是英国作家的小说作品。这一段对于许多读者来说会显得无比枯燥，俩人的谈话似乎不着边际，什么都扯上一点，没个看透。但其实海明威写这一段的用意，是渲染俩人之间此刻隐藏的尴尬和紧张的氛围。



在《了却一段情里》，Nick和女朋友分手后并不好过，在河边的树林里，他把Bill呵斥走了（"Oh, go away, Bill! Go away for a while."）而现在俩人都没开口提这件事。有趣的是，Bill一直在不停地让Nick喝酒——



💧**Clue 2**: Bill keeps on getting Nick into more drinks.



**Evidence 1**: “I’m a little drunk now,” Nick said. “You aren’t drunk,” Bill said.

He got up from the floor and reached for the whisky bottle. Nick held out his glass. His eyes fixed on it while Bill poured.

“我现在就有点醉了。”尼克说。“你没醉。”比尔说。

他从地板上站起身，伸手去拿那瓶威士忌。尼克将酒杯伸过来。比尔斟酒时，他两眼直盯着酒杯。



**Evidence 2**: “He’s a swell guy,” Nick said. He poured water into his glass out of the pitcher. It mixed slowly with the whisky. There was more whisky than water.

“他人倒是不坏。”尼克说。他从壶里往自己杯里倒水。水慢慢地同威士忌混在一起了。威士忌比水多。



**Evidence 3**: “I’ll get a chunk from the back porch,” Nick said....Also he wished to show he could hold his liquor and be practical. Even if his father had never touched a drop Bill was not going to get him drunk before he himself was drunk.

“我到后门廊去拿块柴火。”尼克说。他紧盯着炉火时注意到火快熄灭了。同时他也希望表示自己酒量大，头脑还管用。尽管他父亲一生滴酒不沾，但是比尔自己还没醉就休想灌倒他。



在这后，作者还描述了一个细节，Bill也装出了一副自己还没喝醉并且头脑清醒的样子来（“Bring one of the big beech chunks,” Bill said. He was also being consciously practical.）但俩人是否真的完全不受酒精作用的影响呢？在这之后他们对话的焦点又会发生什么转变？在明天故事的下半篇里也会有精彩上演哦~

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****美国的飓风**

 **Hurricane in America**

我们今天的故事发生在秋季的大风天气，这场大风刮了三天。（It was the first of the autumn storms...The wind was blowing straight down the lake...“She’s blowing,” Nick said. “She’ll blow like that for three days,” Bill said.) 今天我们就来一起了解一下美国多发的飓风吧～

“飓风”这个词源自加勒比海语的恶魔Hurican一词，也有说他其实是玛雅人神话中创世众神的其中一位，就是旋风与雷暴之神Hurakan. 美国中南部有很大的平原，当冷气流与暖气流的锋面向与的时候，地面没有足够高的山坡阻挡，所以，锋面的冲击容易扩大成为飓风。从这方面不难看出，美国之所以频繁出现飓风，主要与它的气候条件和地形有非常大的关系。

按世界气象组织定义：热带气旋中心持续风速达到12级，即每秒32.7米或以上，称为台风或飓风。通常人们将发生在东北太平洋和大西洋上的这种热带气旋称为飓风。（而在国际日期变更线以西的海洋上生成的热带气旋则称之为台风，例如中国）飓风依强度分为1至5级，级数越高表明最高持续风速越高，造成的破坏可能越大。

美国人为何谈飓风色变？翻看美国的历史，就会发现上面洒满了与飓风斗争的血与泪。 一般来说，每年的6月至11月是美国的飓风季节，其中8、9月份飓风最为集中。目前，世界气象组织采用了6张飓风命名表，每6年循环一次，而每张表上的名字按照首字母次序排列。如果某些飓风带来的破坏太大，它的名字可能会弃用，被踢出表格。

2017年，在休斯顿，飓风“哈维”过境带来大面积洪水，灾民紧急撤离。

飓风“艾尔玛”登陆美国后引发强风暴雨，佛罗里达州共有630万人收到撤离令，房屋车辆受损严重，还出现大面积停电。在佛罗里达州冬泉市，飓风过后路面塌陷，一辆面包车坠入坑内。

2012年，飓风“桑迪”横扫美国东海岸，带来狂风暴雨、暴雪及洪水灾害，毁坏大量建筑，百余人丧生，数十万人无家可归。在纽约，飓风“桑迪”带来大雨，洪水灌入地下停车场。

2005年，在路易斯安那州新奥尔良，街道被淹没。超级飓风“卡特里娜”登陆新奥尔良，使之成为一座“水城”，而政府的救援不力，更使之成为一座“炼狱”。

## Chapter 5.2

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/4b021333de336dae6f6854327fe010ab-sz_2665103.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmhigh)

The Three-Day Blow

Nick came in with the log through the kitchen and in passing knocked a pan off the kitchen table.

He laid the log down and picked up the pan.

It had contained dried apricots, soaking in water.

He carefully picked up all the apricots off the floor, some of them had gone under the stove, and put them back in the pan.

He dipped some more water onto them from the pail by the table.

He felt quite proud of himself. He had been thoroughly practical.

He came in carrying the log and Bill got up from the chair and helped him put it on the fire.

“That’s a swell log,” Nick said.

“I’d been saving it for the bad weather,” Bill said.

“A log like that will burn all night.” “There’ll be coals left to start the fire in the morning,” Nick said.

“That’s right,” Bill agreed. They were conducting the conversation on a high plane.

> <font color=red>They were conducting the conversation on a high plane.</font>
>
> 他们谈话的水平可是很高的。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①conduct a (the) conversation “进行谈话”；conduct表示“进行，开展”还可以和investigation（调查）、experiment（实验）、interview（面试）等搭配，比如：The interview was conducted in English.（这次面试是用英语进行的。）
>
> ②on a high plane “在很高的水平”；plane在这里指“（思想、谈话的）水平，程度，标准”（a level or standard of thought, conversation etc）, 比如：The two newspapers are on completely different intellectual planes.（两份报纸的文化层次完全不同。） 

“Let’s have another drink,” Nick said.

“I think there’s another bottle open in the locker,” Bill said.

He kneeled down in the corner in front of the locker and brought out asquare-faced bottle.

“It’s Scotch,” he said.“I’ll get some more water,” Nick said.

He went out into the kitchen again. He filled the pitcher with the dipper dipping cold spring water from the pail.

On his way back to the living room he passed a mirror in the dining room and looked in it.

His face looked strange. He smiled at the face in the mirror and it grinned back at him.

He winked at it and went on. It was not his face but it didn’t make any difference. Bill had poured out the drinks.

“That’s an awfully big shot,” Nick said.

“Not for us, Wemedge,” Bill said.

“What’ll we drink to?” Nick asked, holding up the glass.

“Let’s drink to fishing,” Bill said.

“All right,” Nick said. “Gentlemen, I give you fishing.” “All fishing,” Bill said. “Everywhere.”

“Fishing,” Nick said. “That’s what we drink to.” “It’s better than baseball,” Bill said.

“There isn’t any comparison,” said Nick. “How did we ever get talking about baseball?”

“It was a mistake,” Bill said. “Baseball is a game for louts. ”They drank all that was in their glasses.

“Now let’s drink to Chesterton.” “And Walpole,” Nick interposed.

> ==interpose英 [ˌɪntəˈpəʊz] 美 [ˌɪntərˈpoʊz] vt. 介入，插入 vi. 插话，插嘴==
>
> v. 插话（to add a question or remark into a conversation）
>
> 原文：“Now let’s drink to Chesterton.” “And Walpole,” Nick interposed.
>
> “现在咱们为切斯特顿干杯。” “还有沃尔波尔呢，”尼克插嘴说。
>
> 💧interpose作动词还有“干预”的意思，比如：Police had to interpose themselves between the two rival groups.
>
> 警方不得不对这两个对立团体进行干预。

Nick poured out the liquor. Bill poured in the water.

They looked at each other. They felt very fine.

“Gentlemen,” Bill said, “I give you Chesterton and Walpole.” “Exactly, gentlemen,” Nick said.

They drank. Bill filled up the glasses. They sat down in the big chairs in front of the fire.

“You were very wise, Wemedge,” Bill said. “What do you mean?” asked Nick.

“To bust off that Marge business,” Bill said. “I guess so,” said Nick.

“It was the only thing to do. If you hadn’t, by now you’d be back home working trying to get enough money to get married.”

> <font color=red>"If you hadn’t, by now you’d be back home working trying to get enough money to get married."</font>
>
> “只有这么办了。要是你没断，这会儿就得赶回家干活，想法攒足钱结婚啦。”
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> 这句话运用了混合虚拟语气（虚拟语气和陈述语气混合在一起），If you hadn't表示对过去的虚拟，指的是Nick和Marge分手这件事（《了却一段情》里的故事），也就是If you hadn't busted off that Marge business（bust off表示“了断”）；by now you'd be back home...是一般现在时，用的是陈述语气（如果使用虚拟语气，应为you'd have been back home）.

Nick said nothing. “Once a man’s married he’s absolutely bitched,” Bill went on.

“He hasn’t got anything more. Nothing. Not a damn thing.

He’s done for. You’ve seen the guys that get married.”

Nick said nothing.“You can tell them,” Bill said.

“They get this sort of fat married look. They’re done for.” “Sure,” said Nick.

> <font color=red>“You can tell them,” Bill said. “They get this sort of fat married look. They’re done for.”</font>
>
> “你一看他们就知道。”比尔说。“他们都带着这种结过婚的傻样儿。他们玩儿完了。”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①tell 在这里是“看出，认出”（to know something or be able to recognize something because of certain signs that show this）的意思，比如：The moment Kramer walked in, I could tell that things were not going well.（克雷默一进来，我就看出情况不妙。）
>
> ②this sort of fat married look “这种结过婚的傻样儿”；fat在俚语里是“肤浅的，愚蠢的”（empty, stupid）的意思。

“It was probably bad busting it off,” Bill said.

“But you always fall for somebody else and then it’s all right. Fall for them but don’t let them ruin you.”

> <font color=red>“But you always fall for somebody else and then it’s all right.”</font>
>
> “不过你总是会爱上别的人，这一来就没事了。”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> fall for sb 表示“爱上某人”（to be strongly attracted to sb）, 比如：He was fantastically handsome – I just fell for him right away.（他帅极了–我对他简直就是一见钟情。）
>
> 另外fall for a lie/trick还可以表示“被骗”，比如：It was just a line to get you out here, and you fell for it!（那只是一个让你到这儿来的谎言，你被骗了！） 

“Yes,” said Nick.“If you’d have married her you would have had to marry the whole family.

Remember her mother and that guy she married.”Nick nodded.

“Imagine having them around the house all the time and going to Sunday dinners at their house, and having them over to dinner and her telling Marge all the time what to do and how to act.”

Nick sat quiet.“You came out of it damned well,” Bill said.

“Now she can marry somebody of her own sort and settle down and be happy.

You can’t mix oil and water and you can’t mix that sort of thing any more than if I’d marry Ida that works for Strattons. She’d probably like it, too.”

Nick said nothing. The liquor had all died out of him and left him alone.

Bill wasn’t there. He wasn’t sitting infront of the fire or going fishing tomorrow with Bill and his dad or anything.

He wasn’t drunk. It was all gone. All he knew was that he had once had Marjorie and that he had lost her.

She was gone and he had sent her away.

That was all that mattered. He might never see her again.

Probably he never would. It was all gone, finished.

“Let’s have another drink,” Nick said.

Bill poured it out. Nick splashed in alittle water.

“If you’d gone on that way we wouldn’t be here now,” Bill said.

That was true. His original plan had been to go down home and get a job.

Then he had planned to stay in Charlevoix all winter so he could be near Marge.

Now he did not know what he was going to do.

“Probably we wouldn’t even be going fishing tomorrow,” Bill said. “You had the right dope, all right.” “Icouldn’t help it,” Nick said.

“I know. That’s the way it works out,” Bill said.

“All of a sudden everything was over,” Nick said.

"I don’t know why it was. I couldn’t help it.

Just like when the three-day blows come now and rip all the leaves off the trees.”

“Well, it’s over. That’s the point,” Billsaid. “It was my fault,” Nick said.

“It doesn’t make any difference whose fault it was,” Bill said.

“No, I suppose not,” Nick said.

The big thing was that Marjorie was gone and that probably he would never see her again.

He had talked to her about how they would go to Italy together and the fun they would have.

Places they would be together. It was all gone now.

“So long as it’s over that’s all that matters,” Bill said.

“I tell you, Wemedge, I was worried while it was going on.

You played it right. I understand her mother is sore as hell.

She told a lot of people you were engaged.”

> <font color=red>“You played it right. I understand her mother is sore as hell. She told a lot of people you were engaged.”</font>
>
> “你做得对。我听说她母亲气得要命。她告诉好多人说你们订了婚。”
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①played it right “做得对”；play指“（以某种方式）行事，表现”，比如play it carefully/cool就是指“小心行事”：If you like him, play it cool, or you might scare him off.（你要是喜欢他，就别露声色，否则可能会把他吓跑。）
>
> ②sore as hell “气得要命”；sore 常见义是“（身体某个部位）疼痛的”（painful）, 这里表示“生气的，恼火的”，比如：Mac’s still sore because I didn’t invite him.（马克还在因为我没邀请他而生气呢。） as hell在这里表示程度“极度，非常”。

“We weren’t engaged,” Nick said. “Itwas all around that you were.”

“I can’t help it,” Nick said. “We weren’t.” “Weren’t you going to get married?” Bill asked.

“Yes. But we weren’t engaged,” Nick said.

“What’s the difference?” Bill asked judicially.

> ==judicially英 [dʒʊ'dɪʃəlɪ] 美 [dʒʊ'dɪʃəlɪ] adv. 依法判决地，公平地==

“I don’t know. There’s a difference.”

“I don’t see it,” said Bill.

“All right,” said Nick. “Let’s get drunk.”

“All right,” Bill said. “Let’s get really drunk.”

“Let’s get drunk and then go swimming,” Nick said. He drank off his glass.

“I’m sorry as hell about her but whatcould I do?” he said.

“You know what her mother was like!” “She was terrible,” Bill said.

“All of a sudden it was over,” Nick said. “I oughtn’t to talk about it.”

“You aren’t,” Bill said. “I talked about it and now I’m through. We won’t ever speak about it again.

You don’t want to think about it. You might get back into it again.”

Nick had not thought about that. It had seemed so absolute.

That was a thought. That made him feel better.

“Sure,” he said. “There’s always thatdanger.”

He felt happy now. There was not anything that was irrevocable.

> <font color=red>irrevocable英 [ɪˈrevəkəbl] 美 [ɪˈrɛvəkəbəl] adj. 不可更改的，不可撤回的</font>
>
> adj. 不可挽回的（incapable of being retracted or revoked）
>
> 原文：There was not anything that wasirrevocable.
>
> 决没有什么无可挽回的事。
>
> 💧irrevocable作形容词还有“不可改变的”的意思，比如：He said the decision wasirrevocable. 
>
> 他说这项决定是不可改变的。

He might go into town Saturday night. Today was Thursday.

“There’s always a chance,” he said.

“You’ll have to watch yourself,” Bill said. “I’ll watch myself,” he said.

He felt happy. Nothing was finished.Nothing was ever lost.

He would go into town on Saturday.

He felt lighter, as he had felt before Bill started to talk about it. There was always a way out.

“Let’s take the guns and go down tothe point and look for your dad,” Nick said. “All right.”

Bill took down the two shotguns from the rack on the wall.

He opened a box of shells. Nick puton his Mackinaw coat and his shoes.

His shoes were stiff from the drying.He was still quite drunk but his head was clear.

“How do you feel?” Nick asked.

“Swell. I’ve just got a good edge on.” Bill was buttoning up his sweater.

> <font color=red>“Swell. I’ve just got a good edge on.” Bill was buttoning up his sweater.</font>
>
> “不赖。我只是刚有点醉意罢了。”比尔正扣上毛衣的纽扣。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> I’ve just got a good edge on “我只是刚有点醉意罢了”；on edge 有“紧张，不安”的意思（being tense, nervous, and unable to relax）, 比如： My nerves were constantly on edge.（我的神经处于不断紧张中。）因此这里的got a good edge on可以理解为“精神感觉紧张的”，因为在这之前Bill和Nick的谈话几乎快到争吵的份上了，也可以延伸为“有醉意的”（Bill为自己态度不佳的找的说辞）。

“There’s no use getting drunk.” “No. We ought to get outdoors.”

They stepped out the door. The wind was blowing a gale.

“The birds will lie right down in the grass with this,” Nick said.

They struck down toward the orchard.

“I saw a woodcock this morning,” Bill said. “Maybe we’ll jump him,” Nick said.

“You can’t shoot in this wind,” Bill said.

Outside now the Marge business was no longer so tragic.

It was not even very important. The wind blew everything like that away.

“It’s coming right off the big lake,” Nick said. Against the wind they heard the thud of a shotgun.

“That’s dad,” Bill said. “He’s down inthe swamp.”

“Let’s cut down that way,” Nick said.

“Let’s cut across the lower meadow and see if we jump anything,” Bill said. “All right,” Nick said.

None of it was important now. The wind blew it out of his head.

Still he could always go into town Saturday night. It was a good thing to have in reserve.

### 背景知识

**💧****Hunting in America**

**美国狩猎文化** 

我们今天的内容中有这样的场景：Nick和Bill聊天过后，拿着抢去找Bill正在狩猎的父亲。（“Let’s take the guns and go down to the point and look for your dad,” Nick said. “All right.” Bill took down the two shotguns from the rack on the wall. He opened a box of shells...) 我们今天一起来了解一下美国的狩猎文化吧～

美国狩猎文化起源于欧洲移民（immigrant）最初抵达北美洲，以野外打猎方式寻求温饱。发展到如今，“狩猎”在美国已成为带有平民化的休闲运动。上至总统（罗斯福总统就是著名的“狩猎人”）下至百姓，大家都能同等享受狩猎带来的乐趣。

在美国狩猎合法并不意味着可任意狩猎，而是有着很严格的法律限制：需在规定的时间、地点里打猎指定种类和数量的野兽，如若违法狩猎，将受到严重的处罚（罚款甚至牢狱之灾都有可能）。另一方面，从科学角度证实，狩猎有助于自然界的生态平衡，只要合法狩猎，环保人士也很少上诉狩猎行为。

猎人必须把猎物带回，或食用其肉，或使用其皮毛。到猎场滥杀，置猎物横尸野地，肆意浪费野生资源，不管有无猎证都属非法；但所有渔猎所获，从皮肉肢体到内脏都只能自家或送亲友享用，有任何商业行为谋利，属重罪非法。

美国对于申购打猎执照资格的控管，各州有松有紧，申购了打猎执照之后，除了可以按相关规定猎野兔、松鼠等小动物之外，其他如飞鸟、水禽、及各种大型猎物（Big Game），都还须加购许可证、贴章与猎签。

猎棕熊则是在北美州算危险性最高的狩猎，一般在阿拉斯加雇用有执照向导追猎，狩猎方式有徒步追踪，驾雪地摩托车追猎，也可乘小飞机或船寻猎。该州的滨海区域巨型棕熊，可重达千磅，高达3米，是美国与国际顶尖猎人的梦幻猎物（Dream Game）.

外国人到美国狩猎，目前问题的是很难把猎枪带进美国。一般必须有熟悉打猎的亲友带领，使用他们的猎枪猎具；或寻人安排聘专业向导或到猎场，借用或租用他们的猎枪实现到美国的打猎梦。

美国狩猎地点Top5推荐：

\1. Appleton, Wisconsin,威斯康星州的阿普尔顿，Boone和Crockett俱乐部将其授予美国白尾鹿打猎最好的地点。

\2. Vassalboro, Maine，缅因州Vassalboro在国家南部提供一流的火鸡射击场所。

\3. Lake Umbagog, New Hampshire,新罕布什尔州的Umbagog湖是狩猎鸭，鹅，乌鸦，wood鹬，熊，白尾鹿，驼鹿和土狼的一个主要场所。

\4. Wilson Hill, New York，纽约威尔逊山提供水禽狩猎，也可以进行鹿和小型狩猎。如果你喜欢打雉鸡，那个地区在秋天有很多。

\5. West Virginia's Charleston-Beckley corridor，西弗吉尼亚州的查尔斯顿- 贝克利走廊，在弓和步枪狩猎季节可以猎到熊。在那里，还可以猎到最好的鹿和松鼠。

### 课文理解

Nick和Bill继续喝酒的过程中，Bill终于主动提起Nick和女友分手的话题，并且表示了自己对Nick的支持和赞同。Bill有强烈的对婚姻的反对和厌恶，在他看来，婚姻足以摧毁一个男人——

💧**Clue 1**: Bill thinks that marriage ruins a man.

**Evidence 1**: “You were very wise, Wemedge,” Bill said.

“What do you mean?” asked Nick.

“To bust off that Marge business,” Bill said.

“你非常聪明，威米奇。”比尔说。

“你什么意思？”尼克说。

“把跟玛吉的那段关系了断啦。”比尔说。



**Evidence 2**:  “Once a man’s married he’s absolutely bitched,” Bill went on. “He hasn’t got anything more. Nothing. Not a damn thing. He’s done for. You’ve seen the guys that get married.”

“男人一旦结了婚就彻底完蛋啦。”比尔继续说。“他什么都没有了。一无所有。屁也没有。他玩儿完了。你见过结了婚的男人嘛。”



对于Bill的这番慷慨陈词，Nick虽然嘴上应和，但独自一人的时候依然对和Marge分手感到伤痛和后悔——



💧**Clue 2**: Nick is painful about his break-up with Marge.



**Evidence 1**: It was all gone. All he knew was that he had once had Marjorie and that he had lost her. She was gone and he had sent her away. That was all that mattered.

这一切全过去了。他只知道自己从前跟玛乔丽好过，后来失去了她。她走了，是他打发她走的。这是一切的关键。



**Evidence 2**: His original plan had been to go down home and get a job. Then he had planned to stay in Charlevoix all winter so he could be near Marge. Now he did not know what he was going to do.

他原来的计划是回家去找份活儿。后来计划整个冬天都留在夏勒伏瓦，这样可以亲近玛吉。现在他可不知道自己该做什么了。



但是作者并没有让故事以Nick的无措和伤感结尾，而是安排了一个转折。在Bill的提醒下，他想到了自己总会再遇见喜欢的女孩。（“There’s always a chance,” he said. “You’ll have to watch yourself,” Bill said. “I’ll watch myself,” he said. He felt happy. Nothing was finished.）



Nick的心境转移也和这三天的大风形成了呼应（None of it was important now. The wind blew it out of his head.）狂风似乎把他对这件事情的残念都刮走了，他也突然地兴奋了起来。这个结尾其实也留下了一个矛盾，甚至可以说是悖论。Nick一方面主动和Marge分手后无法摆脱空虚和痛苦，另一方面又盲目地期待着也许还有新的感情机会。这也可以说是一种非常不成熟的感情观。

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****Fishing in Different Countries**

**各国钓鱼趣味文化**



我们今天的内容中Nick和Bill在闲聊中提到了他们喜欢的娱乐方式：钓鱼，并以钓鱼祝酒。（“What’ll we drink to?” Nick asked, holding up the glass. “Let’s drink to fishing,” Bill said. “All right,” Nick said. “Gentlemen, I give you fishing.” “All fishing,” Bill said. “Everywhere.”）其实钓鱼在世界各国有着各种有趣的方式～

\1. 德国－－钓鱼要考证

在德国如果想要去钓鱼，必须到专门的培训学校学习，通过考试之后会颁发一本有效期为五年的钓鱼执照。凡是是去钓鱼必须带着钓鱼执照，持证上岗，否则被抓到的话要受到处罚的。不过，这个规定只是针对德国人，对于外国游客却不需要，但是也要注意文明垂钓。

\2. 丹麦－－钓鱼带尺子

丹麦位于北欧，地处北海与波罗的海之间，是一个半岛国家，因为它有广阔的海岸线，海产资源非常丰富，是世界四大渔业国之一。在丹麦，人们到海边钓鱼，除了带通常的钓鱼工具外，工具袋中还有一把尺子，原因是丹麦政府发布了一条法令，凡是身长不满22 cm的鱼，一律禁止捕捞。

\3. 新西兰－－钓鱼放风筝

号称“钓鱼天堂”的新西兰流行风筝钓鱼法。风筝钓鱼最大的优势就是风筝可以把钓线带到几百米开外，而岸边甩钩高手也只能甩几十米远。原理是，风筝把附有诱饵和浮子的钓线送几百米外的水域。钓线会随着风筝的升降，在水中上下起落。一旦有鱼上钩，钓线因受到鱼的牵引，便会从风筝的夹子上滑落下来，浮子则漂浮在海水中。然后钓鱼人捡起鱼线，就能把钓在钩上的鱼拉上岸。

\4. 日本－－钓鱼不摘钩

日本是世界钓鱼大国，全国约有3100多万钓鱼爱好者。日本人钓鱼很少从鱼的嘴里取下渔钩，这是为防止不小心手被渔钩划破或被锋利的鱼鳍刺伤，尤其是为预防身上长刺的有毒鱼。此外，从鱼口中取钩不仅麻烦，而且还贻误垂钓时间。因此，他们钓到鱼后，会立即用剪子剪断引线。这就要求他们在钓鱼前要准备很多绑好子线的钓钩，麻利换上钓钩后接着开始钓鱼。日本人办事历来既讲安全又讲效率，钓鱼自然也不例外。

\5. 韩国－－钓鱼搭炉子

韩国济州岛沿岸海阔水深，鱼儿很多，岸边筑有长长的防波大堤，是垂钓的好去处。每当太阳西斜时，会有许多举家而来的垂钓者。丈夫忙着投竿钓鱼，妻子与孩子们则找块平坦地方铺上塑料布，支起专用小炉子等鱼下锅。垂钓者一般五分钟左右就可钓上鱼来，一家人围坐在一起，吃着烧好的鲜鱼和带来的食品，喝着啤酒或饮料，其惬意不言而喻。

虽然钓鱼方法各式各样，但是这些钓鱼人有一个共同点，就是穿着上都喜欢穿一件钓鱼马甲。这种马甲有许多大小不一的口袋，钓鱼的渔具本就多，一般钓鱼都不会另外背包，马甲的多口袋可以防止手机、钱包、证件、水壶小物件和各种鱼线、鱼饵、渔具盒存放、拿去都非常方便。马甲上的D型挂环、环形织带等可以挂剪刀、鱼钩、鱼漂等，专业的还有设置鱼竿放置槽。

## Chapter 6

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/7dc9ffc1b1c8323d4dd7149684f81f1f-sz_1258776.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

Mr. And Mrs. Elliot

Mr. and Mrs. Elliot tried very hard to have a baby.

They tried as often as Mrs. Elliot could stand it.

They tried in Boston after they were married and they tried coming over on the boat.

They did not try very often on the boat because Mrs. Elliot was quite sick.

She was sick and when she was sick she was sick as Southern women are sick.

That is women from the Southern part of the United States.

Like all Southern women Mrs. Elliot disintegrated very quickly under sea sickness, travelling at night, and getting up too early in the morning.

> ==disintegrate英 [dɪsˈɪntɪgreɪt] 美 [dɪsˈɪntɪˌɡret] vt.&vi. 使碎裂；瓦解==
>
> <font color=red>Like all Southern women Mrs. Elliot disintegrated very quickly under sea sickness, travelling at night, and getting up too early in the morning.</font>
>
> 跟所有的南方女人一样，艾略特太太一晕船便马上垮下，这是由于夜里开船、早晨起得太早之故。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> disintegrate 从integrate变形而来，integrate是“使合并，融入”的意思，加上否定前缀dis-后表示“分裂，解体”，比如：The plane just disintegrated in mid-air.（飞机就在半空中解体了。） 这里disintegrate引申为“瓦解，崩溃”（break down）. 

Many of the people on the boat took her for Elliot’s mother.

> <font color=red>Many of the people on the boat took her for Elliot’s mother.</font>
>
> 船上许多乘客以为她是艾略特的母亲。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> take sb for “把某人误认为……”；比如：Of course I won’t tell anyone! What do you take me for ? (= what sort of person do you think I am? ) （我当然不会告诉任何人！你当我是什么人了？）
>
> *这里别人之所以会把Mrs. Elliot当成Mr. Elliot的母亲，是因为他们俩的年龄差：Mrs. Elliot已经有40岁（In reality she was forty years old）而Mr. Elliot只有25岁（He was twenty-five years old）.

Other people who knew they were married believed she was going to have a baby.

In reality she was forty years old. Her years had been precipitated suddenly when she started travelling.

> ==precipitate英 [prɪˈsɪpɪteɪt] 美 [prɪˈsɪpɪˌtet] vt. 造成…仓促发生；使…陷入 adj. 鲁莽的；草率的；仓促的 n. 沉淀物；析出物质==

She had seemed much younger, in fact she had seemed not to have any age at all, when Elliot had married her after several weeks of making love to her after knowing her for a long time in her tea shop before he had kissed her one evening.

> <font color=red>Her years had been precipitated suddenly when she started travelling. She had seemed much younger, in fact she had seemed not to have any age at all...</font>
>
> 她一开始旅游，便一下子见老了。她曾看上去年轻得多。事实上，艾略特娶她时，她年轻得好像根本看不出年岁似的…
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①precipitate 有“加速，促成”（to make something serious happen suddenly or more quickly than was expected）的意思，相当于hasten.  比如：The riot was precipitated when four black men were arrested.（这场骚乱是因为四名黑人男子的被捕而突然引发的。）
>
> ②not to have any age at all “看出年岁似的”；age在这里不是指“年龄”，而是指“衰老”（the state of being age），或者是“陈旧”（the state of being old）, 比如：Some of the furniture was showing signs of age.（有些家具已显陈旧。）

Hubert Elliot was taking postgraduate work in law at Harvardwhen he was married.

He was a poet with an income of nearly ten thousand dollars a year.He wrote very long poems very rapidly.

He was twenty-five years old and had never gone to bed with a woman until he married Mrs. Elliot.

He wanted to keep himself pure so that he could bring to his wife the same purity of mind and body that he expected of her.

> ==purity英 [ˈpjʊərəti] 美 [ˈpjʊrəti] n. 纯净，纯正，纯粹==

He called it to himself living straight.

> <font color=red>He called it to himself living straight.</font>
>
> 他自称这是“过规矩的生活”。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> straight 可以表示“诚实地，坦诚地”（in an honest direct way）, 比如：I hope, for your sake, you’re playing it straight (= being honest ) .（为了你自己，我希望你说实话。）
>
> *这里的“规矩生活”指Mr. Elliot一直保持童身，并且向他所有的交往对象都如此坦诚。

He had been in love with various girls before he kissed Mrs. Elliot and always told them sooner or later that he had led a clean life.

Nearly all the girls lost interest in him. He was shocked and really horrified at the way girls would become engaged to and marry men whom they must know had dragged themselves through the gutter.

> ==gutter英 [ˈgʌtə(r)] 美 [ˈɡʌtɚ] n. 排水沟；排水槽；恶劣环境 vi. (烛光)摇曳不定==
>
> n. 排水沟（ the edge of a road next to the pavement, where rain water collects and flows away.）
>
> 原文：He was shocked and really horrified at the way girls would become engaged to and marry men whom they must know had dragged themselves through the gutter.
>
> 另一方面，这些姑娘明明知道有些汉子乌七八糟，却愿意跟他们订婚以至结合，这使他愕然，甚至觉得不堪。
>
> 💧这里用穿行于排水沟来形容这些男子们行为不检点，放纵不羁。
>
> 💧gutter还可以作动词，意思是“（火焰）忽明忽暗，摇曳不定 ”，比如：The flamesguttered.
>
> 火苗摇曳不定。

He once tried to warn a girl he knew against a man of whom he had almost proof that he had been a rotter at college and a very unpleasant incident had resulted.

Mrs. Elliot’s name was Cornelia. She had taught him to call her Calutina, which was her family nickname in the South.

His mother cried when he brought Cornelia home after their marriage but brightened very much when she learned they were going to live abroad.

Cornelia had said, “You dear sweet boy,” and held him closer than ever when he had told her how he had kept himself clean for her.

Cornelia was pure too. “Kiss me again like that,” she said.

Hubert explained to her that he had learned that way of kissing from hearing a fellow tell a story once.

He was delighted with his experiment and they developed it as far as possible.

Sometimes when they had been kissing together a long time, Cornelia would ask him to tell her again that he had kept himself really straight for her.

The declaration always set her off again. At first Hubert had no idea of marrying Cornelia. He had never thought of her that way.

She had been such a good friend ofhis, and then one day in the little back room of the shop they had been dancing to the gramophone while her girl friend was in the front of the shop and she had looked up into his eyes and he had kissed her.

He could never remember just when it was decided that they were to be married.

But they were married. They spent the night of the day they were married in a Boston hotel.

They were both disappointed but finally Cornelia went to sleep.

Hubert could not sleep and several times went out and walked up and down the corridor of the hotel in his new Jaeger bathrobe that he had bought for his wedding trip.

As he walked he saw all the pairs of shoes, small shoes and big shoes, outside the doors of the hotel rooms.

This set his heart to pounding and he hurried back to his own room but Cornelia was asleep.

He did not like to waken her and soon everything was quite all right and he slept peacefully.

The next day they called on his mother and the next day they sailed for Europe.

It was possible to try to have a baby but Cornelia could not attempt it very often although they wanted a baby more than anything else in the world.

They landed at Cherbourg and came to Paris. They tried to have a baby in Paris.

Then they decided to go to Dijon where there was summer school and where a number of people who crossed on the boat with them had gone.

They found there was nothing to do in Dijon.

Hubert, however, was writing a great number of poems and Cornelia typed them for him.

They were all very long poems. He was very severe about mistakes and would make her re-do an entirepage if there was one mistake.

She cried a good deal and they tried several times to have a baby before they left Dijon.

They came to Paris and most of their friends from the boat came back too.

They were tired of Dijon and anyway would now be able to say that after leaving Harvard or Columbia or Wabash they had studied at the University of Dijon down in the Côte d’Or.

Many of them would have preferred to go to Languedoc, Montpellier or Perpignan if there are universities there.

But all those places are too far away. Dijon is only four and a half hours from Paris and there is a diner on the train.

So they all sat around the Café du Dome, avoiding the Rotonde across the street because it is always so full of foreigners, for a few days andthen the Elliots rented a château in Touraine through an advertisement in the New York Herald.

Elliot had a number of friends by now all of whom admired his poetry and Mrs. Elliot had prevailed upon him to send over to Boston for her girl friend who had been in the tea shop.

> ==prevail英 [prɪˈveɪl] 美 [prɪˈvel] vi. 盛行；获胜；战胜==
>
> v. 劝说（to persuade sb to do sth）
>
> 原文：Mrs. Elliot had prevailed upon him to send over to Boston for her girl friend who had been in the tea shop.
>
> 艾略特太太还说服他，邀请以前她在某室里的女伴从波士顿来作客。
>
> 💧prevail on/upon sb to do sth 意思是“劝说 某人做某事”，比如：I'm sure he could beprevailed upon to give a talk.
>
> 我相信能说服他来做一次报告。
>
> 💧prevail作动词还有“战胜”的意思，常与against/over搭配，比如：Justice will prevail over tyranny.
>
> 正义必将战胜暴虐。

Mrs. Elliot became much brighter after her girl friend came and they had many good cries together.

The girl friend was several years older than Cornelia and called her Honey.

She too came from a very old Southern family.

The three of them, with several of Elliot’s friends who called him Hubie, went down to the château in Touraine.

They found Touraine to be a very flat hot country very much like Kansas.

Elliot had nearly enough poems for a book now.

He was going to bring it out in Boston and had already sent his check to, and made a contract with, a publisher.

In a short time the friends began to drift back to Paris.

Touraine had not turned out the way it looked when it started.

Soon all the friends had gone off with a rich young and unmarried poet to a seaside resort near Trouville.

There they were all very happy. Elliot kept on at the château in Touraine because he had taken it for all summer.

He and Mrs. Elliot tried very hard to have a baby in the big hot bedroomon the big, hard bed.

Mrs. Elliot was learning the touch system on the typewriter, but she found that while it increased the speed it made more mistakes.

The girl friend was now typing practically all of the manuscripts.

She was very neat and efficient andseemed to enjoy it.

Elliot had taken to drinking white wine and lived apart in his own room.

He wrote a great deal of poetry during the night and in the morning looked very exhausted.

Mrs. Elliot and the girl friend now slept together in the big medieval bed. They had many a good cry together.

> ==medieval英 [ˌmediˈi:vl] 美 [ˌmidiˈivəl] adj. 中世纪的==

In the evening they all sat at dinner together in the garden under a plane tree and the hot evening windblew and Elliot drank white wine and Mrs. Elliot and the girl friend made conversation and they were all quite happy.

### 背景知识

**💧****Medieval Furniture**

**中世纪风格家具**

我们今天的内容中提到了艾略特夫人和女伴同睡一张中世纪的大床。（Mrs. Elliot and the girl friend now slept together in the big medieval bed. ）那么中世纪风格的家具都是什么样子的呢？

中世纪是欧洲历史上的一个时代，由西罗马帝国灭亡（公元476年）直到文艺复兴时期（公元1453年）。这一千年的历史中形成了融合希伯来文化、日耳曼文化、古希腊、古罗马文化为一体的基督教文明。

人们通常将这个时期的艺术，分为三个形式：即拜占庭艺术、仿罗马式艺术和哥特式艺术。中世纪前期的家具风格以拜占庭式和罗马式为主流。到了12世纪后半叶，中世纪的代表哥特式家具风靡整个欧洲大陆，人们的视野被引向天空，垂直耸立的哥特式风格被广泛地引入到建筑和家具设计中。

\1. 拜占庭式家具（Byzantine Style Furniture）

受到基督教影响，拜占庭家具的装饰图案常用象征基督教的十字架符号，或在花冠藤蔓之间夹杂着天使、圣徒以及各种鸟兽、果实和叶饰图案。由于当时崇尚奢华生活，拜占庭家具装饰形式与过去相比更为华美。

家具在雕刻和镶嵌装饰上十分精细，常常将象牙雕刻的板面用于椅子、小箱、圣骨箱、门等重要的装饰部位，或作为镶嵌形式来点缀家具。在贮藏家具中大多以木材为主（solid wood furniture）形式上精心制作，同时，金、银、青铜饰件也常见于家具的装饰表现上。

拜占庭家具还融入了波斯、伊斯兰、甚至中国的影响，其特征为制作精巧的轴柱、X框架的座椅、圆形或半圆形餐桌、篷盖式睡床、可开合的橱柜以及精心装饰的衣箱。此外，由于丝织业的兴盛，家具的衬垫装饰和室内壁挂以及帷幔等饰物得到了很快的发展，部分丝织品以动物图案为装饰，明显地表露出波斯王朝的特异风格。

\2. 罗马式家具（Romanesque Furniture）

木材是罗马式家具的主要用材，除了松木等低档木材以外，常用的有胡桃木、橡木、欧洲椴木与栗木。此外，铜、铁、象牙、珍珠母等也常用于罗马式家具中。中世纪的整个欧洲家具制作技术发展较慢，家具连接主要靠榫卯接合、钉接合以及铁件的加固作用。罗马式家具方正、笨重，结构简洁，几乎所有支撑构件采用垂直的车木构件，橱柜采用中欧流行的拱顶形。

罗马式家具可以说是罗马式建筑的缩写，其主要标志是采用古罗马建筑的拱券和檐帽、柱子等作为家具构件的表面装饰手法，家具粗犷。但由于罗马文化的优秀遗产大部分在战火中焚毁，此时的家具无论从造型上还是从制作工艺上看明显带有北方条顿民族的粗野形态。

\3. 哥特式家具（Gothic Furniture）

哥特式艺术，始于12世纪的法国，盛行于13世纪，至14世纪末期，其风格逐渐大众化和自然化，成为国际哥特风格。在这一时期木材仍然是制作家具的主要用材。整个欧洲以橡木为主，法国、西班牙和意大利也用胡桃木，欧洲中部和黑海地区用金高松木等软质木材。也有坐具采用金属制作，使用时表面铺上软垫和织物。锁、合页等装饰五金用铁制作，采用敲打、透雕工艺。

哥特式家具从造型、装饰题材到制作工艺直接受到哥特式建筑风潮的影响。家具造型以垂直线条强调垂直庄重的形态，采用尖顶、尖拱、卷叶拱、棂花格、束柱以及浮雕等装饰，给人以刚直、挺拔、严谨的感受。

### 课文理解

今天的故事以一对夫妇为主角，男方是哈佛的高材生，年仅25岁，而女方则已40岁。小说开篇即交待俩人一直想要生一个孩子，但始终没有成功，接下来的情节都围绕着这条主线展开。首先Mr. Elliot在婚前一直保持童身，因为在他看来，只要维持自己的纯洁，就能够获得一段完美的婚姻关系——

💧**Clue 1**: Mr. Elliot thinks that keeping himself sexually pure will be the basis of a perfect relationship.



**Evidence 1**: He wanted to keep himself pure so that he could bring to his wife the same purity of mind and body that he expected of her.

他要保持童身，这样能将纯洁的心灵和身体给予妻子，而他对她也有着同样的期望。



**Evidence 2**:  Cornelia had said, “You dear sweet boy,” and held him closer than ever when he had told her how he had kept himself clean for her. Cornelia was pure too.

他告诉妻子，自己为了她而保持洁身自好，科妮莉娅便称他“亲爱的小宝贝”，还把他搂得格外紧。科妮莉娅也是纯洁的。



但是Mr. Elliot并没有获得期望的完美婚姻生活，他甚至连在和妻子结婚的时候都不是完全自主情愿的（At first Hubert had no idea of marrying Cornelia. He had never thought of her that way...He could never remember just when it was decided that they were to be married. But they were married.）而Mrs. Elliot在这段关系中也并不快乐——



💧**Clue 2**: Mrs. Elliot is also unhappy with her marriage.



**Evidence 1**: Hubert, however, was writing a great number of poems and Cornelia typed them for him. They were all very long poems. He was very severe about mistakes and would make her re-do an entire page if there was one mistake.

幸而休伯特正在写诗，写了好多，科妮莉娅在帮他打字。那些诗全都很长。他又很严格，绝不允许打错，要是有一个差错，就要她把整整一页重打。她哭过好几次，在离开第戎前，他俩几次三番试着怀上孩子。



**Evidence 2**: Elliot had taken to drinking white wine and lived apart in his own room. He wrote a great deal of poetry during the night and in the morning looked very exhausted. Mrs. Elliot and the girl friend now slept together in the big medieval bed. They had many a good cry together.

此时，艾略特喝上了白葡萄酒，独自住在另一间房中。他熬夜写了好多诗，早晨显得精疲力竭。艾略特太太和女友现在同睡在那只中世纪的大床上。她俩抱住了哭过好几回。



这篇小说在表面上探讨的是“不孕不育”（sterility）的话题，但也有人认为，这恰恰象征着“迷惘的一代”精神贫瘠的状态——竭力寻找满足感但无从获得（They search for an undefined sense of fulfillment, but never find it）. 也有人认为，Elliot夫妇的名字其实是在向美国诗人T. S. Elliot致敬，他创作的《荒原》（The Waste Land）是当时展现西方一代人精神上幻灭的经典之作。

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****Why Do Some People Feel Sick on Boat or Car？**

**为什么有些人会晕船和晕车呢？**



我们今天的内容中Eliot晕船的情节的描写。（They did not try very often on the boat because Mrs. Elliot was quite sick. She was sick and when she was sick she was sick as Southern women are sick. ）我们今天就来科普一下为什么有些人会晕船和晕车又有哪些小妙招能克服晕船和晕车吧～

从医学上说，晕车、晕船和晕机统称为晕动病，这个病虽不属疑难杂症，但是由于症状令人非常难受，晕车除了和人体个体差异有关系以外，主要和人体的前庭平衡器官这个平衡系统有关系。



许多人想不到这与人的耳朵有关。一般来说，人产生眩晕感主要是因为内耳、眼睛、小脑处于不正常状态造成的。至于晕车，耳部前庭神经功能紊乱是它产生的主因。人的耳朵生理构造分为外耳、中耳、内耳。其中内耳嵌在骨头里，在内耳中有一套调节人体平衡功能的器官，医学术语称为“前庭器官”。前庭是维持人体平衡的一个很重要的器官，它可以感受到人体头位、体位的变化，可以随时调整人身体的姿势，达到身体平衡。



当人们坐船或坐车时，身体经常会产生突然的变向运动，或者在竖直方向上突然变化，就会使前庭器变得不稳定，与此同时，人们眼睛看到情景也对大脑产生刺激，于是，眼睛耳朵向大脑发出不一样的指令，大脑就感到不对了，这时，大脑会发出警告，让人们感觉晕乎乎的，并且想通过呕吐来缓解这种状态的不一致。



此外，如果运行中有一些异常感觉以及运动过程中的一些特殊情况往往会加强晕车的表现，比如在车里觉得不舒服，或者周围的空气不好，或者在运行过程中经常遇到一些复杂的交通情况，都会对前庭器产生一些频繁的刺激。



那么晕车该如何预防呢？

\1. 不要在乘车、船、飞机前吃得太饱，也不要挨饿，尽可能提早吃些易消化食物，不要吃油腻食品。

\2. 应找颠簸不那么厉害的座位，如前两三排座位，眼望前方。

\3. 尽量打开窗门吸取新鲜空气。

\4. 乘船尽量要选较大的船，避免乘小船。

\5. 如有需要，准备一些如苯海拉明片等抗晕动药品，最迟应在乘车前30分钟服用。

\6. 可以听听收音机或和别人聊天、玩耍以分散注意力。

\7. 回忆美好的时光和高兴的往事有利抑制晕动病的症状。



推荐几个的实用小偏方：



\1. 嚼块生姜

生姜的辛辣味道能抑制恶心呕吐的感觉。需要提醒的是，姜会让血液变得稀薄，如果你在服用降血压的药物，一定要事先咨询医生。



\2. 带个橘子

乘车前1小时左右,将新鲜橘皮表面朝外,向内对折,然后对准两鼻孔两手指挤压,皮中便会喷射也带芳香味的油雾。可吸入10余次,乘车途中也照此法随时吸闻。



\3. 按手腕

如果感到胃部不适，恶心想吐，可用大拇指在手腕内侧折痕下方5厘米处的内关穴，按压几分钟，晕车症状就能减轻。



\4. 涂风油精

乘车途中，将风油精搽于太阳穴或风池穴。亦可滴两滴风油精于肚脐眼处，并用伤湿止痛膏敷盖。



\5. 盯住车外一点

适宜轻微的头晕眼花和呕吐。如果眼睛盯住车辆内部的物体，大脑就会收到“没有移动”的信号，使内耳和大脑不同步，进而出现头晕。此时可以盯住车外一个固定不动的点 (如远处的高楼)，这样能让内耳和大脑保持同步，缓解头晕。

## Chapter 7

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/4c50233959bc386fdec25f1e0ba09e35-sz_1249744.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

Cat in the Rain

There were only two Americans stopping at the hotel.

They did not know any of the people they passed on the stairs on their way to and from their room.

Their room was on the second floor facing the sea.

It also faced the public garden and war monument.

There were big palms and green benches in the public garden.

In the good weather there was always an artist with his easel.

Artists liked the way the palms grew and the bright colors of the hotels facing the sea.

Italians came from a long way off to look up at the war monument.

It was made of bronze and glistened in the rain. It was raining.

> ==glisten英 [ˈglɪsn] 美 [ˈɡlɪsən] vi. 闪光；闪亮==

The rain dripped from the palm trees. Water stood in pools on the gravel paths.

> ==gravel英 [ˈgrævl] 美 [ˈɡrævəl] n. 砾石，砂砾，石子 vt. 铺碎石；使气恼，搅扰==

The sea broke into a long line in the rain and slipped back down the beach to come up and break again in a long line in the rain.

> <font color=red>The sea broke into a long line in the rain and slipped back down the beach to come up and break again in a long line in the rain. </font>
>
> 在雨中， 海水依着长长的浪线冲过来， 又顺着海滩滑回去，再过一会儿，又依着长长的浪线冲过来。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①The sea broke into a long line 这里形容海浪冲击成一条长线，这里的break表示“冲击，冲破”的意思（to crash into a shore and change into foam)，比如：The sea was trying to break the ship into pieces, and we had very little time. 
>
> 海浪似乎极力地想把船击成粉碎，我们只有很少的时间了。
>
> Alfred Tennyson（阿尔弗雷德丁尼生）有一首著名诗歌*Break，Break，Break*（《冲击，冲击，冲击》）就以大海一个又一个的浪潮冲击山岩的景象，象征痛失友人的打击就像心中被无情的浪潮冲击一样。
>
> ②slipped back down the beach 海涛沿着沙滩退去，slip back 在这里是“逆流”的意思。slip back还有“倒退，衰退”的意思，比如：The White House has been pushing Democrats to back the measure, arguing that if the plan is defeated, the economy could slip back into recession. 
>
> 白宫敦促民主党人支持这项政策，认为如果该计划不能在国会通过，那么美国经济将再次陷入衰退。
>
> ③to come up 扑上沙滩，come up 在这里有“上升”的意思，指海浪升起。比如：It will be so great watching the sun come up.
>
> 看着太阳升起将会很美妙。

The motor cars were gone from the square by the war monument.

Across the square in the doorway of the cafe a waiter stood looking out at the empty square.

The American wife stood at the window looking out.

Outside right under their window a cat was crouched under one of the dripping green tables.

The cat was trying to make herself so compact that she would not be dripped on.

> ==compact英 [kəmˈpækt] 美 [ˈkɑ:mˈpækt] adj. 小巧便携；紧密的；矮小结实 n. 粉饼盒；小型汽车；协定 vt. 压紧，压实==
>
> <font color=red>Outside right under their window a cat was crouched under one of the dripping green tables. The cat was trying to make herself so compact that she would not be dripped on.</font>
>
> 窗户的正下方有一只猫，蜷缩在一个滴水的绿色桌子下面。那猫萎缩成一团，生怕被淋着。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ① right under their window 窗户的正下方，right在这里作副词，表示（位置或地点）准确地，精确地（emphasize the precise place, position, or time of something），right under ... 表示“...的正下方”，比如：The back of a car appeared right in front of him.
>
> 汽车尾部正对着他。
>
> ②a cat was crouched 一只猫蜷缩着，crouched在这里作形容词，表示“蜷缩的”，crouch作动词，意为“蹲伏，蜷伏”（your legs are bent under you so that you are close to the ground and leaning forward slightly），比如：We were crouching in the bushes.
>
> 我们那时正蹲伏在灌木丛中。
>
> ③one of the dripping green tables 一个滴水的绿色桌子，dripping在这里作形容词，表示“湿淋淋的”，比如：Her face was dripping with sweat.
>
> 她脸上汗水淋淋。
>
> ④make herself so compact 蜷缩成一团，这里的compact用作形容词，表示“小巧紧凑的”（small and neatly constructed），形容小猫蜷缩成一团的样子。
>
> ⑤be dripped on 被淋着，drip作动词的原意是“（液体）滴下”，比如：Water was dripping down the walls.
>
> 水从墙上滴落下来。
>
> 这里指被雨水淋到。

"I'm going down and get that kitty," the American wife said.

"I'll do it," her husband offered from the bed.

"No, I'll get it. The poor kitty is out trying to keep dry under the table."

The husband went on reading, lying propped up with the two pillows at the foot of the bed.

> <font color=red>The husband went on reading, lying propped up with the two pillows at the foot of the bed.</font>
>
> 丈夫继续看书，他肩后垫着两只枕头，躺在床脚那一头。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①propped up with the two pillows 用两个枕头垫起来，prop up表示“支撑，支持”，比如：Bubble prices were not allowed to adjust quickly but were to some extent propped up by government interventions. 
>
> 虚高的价格不能过快的调整而是通过政府的干涉来达到某种程度的支撑。
>
> ②at the foot of the bed 在床脚那一头，at the foot of还可以指在山脚下，比如：Our first camp was at the foot of one of them, beside a three mile-wide lake. 
>
> 我们第一个营地在一座火山脚下，营地边上有一个三英里宽的湖泊。

"Don't get wet," he said.The wife went downstairs and the hotel owner stood up and bowed to her as she passed the office.

His desk was at the far end of the office. He was an old man and very tall.

"Il piove," the wife said. She liked the hotelkeeper.

"Si, si, Signora, brutto tempo. It is very bad weather."

He stood behind his desk in the far end of the dim room.

The wife liked him. She liked the way he wanted to serve her.

She liked the way he felt about being a hotel-keeper. She liked his old, heavy face and big hands.

Liking him she opened the door and looked out. It was raining harder.

A man in a rubber cape was crossing the empty square to the cafe.

The cat would be around to the right. Perhaps she could go along to the eaves.

> ==eave英 [i:v] 美 [i:v] n. 屋檐==

As she stood in the doorway an umbrella opened behind her. It was the maid who looked after their room.

"You must not get wet," she smiled, speaking Italian. Of course, the hotel-keeper had sent her.

With the maid holding the umbrella over her, she walked along the gravel path until she was under their window.

The table was there, washed bright green in the rain, but the cat was gone.

She was suddenly disappointed. The maid looked up at her.

"Ha perduto qualque cosa, Signora?" "There was a cat," said the American girl.

"A cat?""Si, il gatto.""A cat?" the maid laughed. "A cat in the rain?"

"Yes," she said, "under the table." Then, "Oh, I wanted it so much. I wanted a kitty."When she talked English the maid's face tightened.

"Come, Signora," she said. "We must get back inside. You will be wet."

"I suppose so," said the American girl.

They went back along the gravel path and passed in the door.

The maid stayed outside to close the umbrella.

As the American girl passed the office, the padrone bowed from his desk.

Something felt very small and tight inside the girl.

> <font color=red>Something felt very small and tight inside the girl.</font>
>
> 一阵莫名其妙的不适与紧张在心头掠过。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> 可以将这句话理解为"The girl felt something small and tight inside her heart." 例句：As he began sprinting down the runway, something felt wonderfully different, yet familiar. 
>
> 他沿着跑道起跑冲刺，那感觉奇特无比，妙不可言，而又似曾相识。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> very small and tight 不适与紧张，这里的small作形容词，表示“羞愧的”，比如：This may just be another of her schemes to make me look small.
>
> 这也许就是她要让我羞愧的又一个诡计。

The padrone made her feel very small and at the same time really important.

She had a momentary feeling of being of supreme importance.

> ==momentary英 [ˈməʊməntri] 美 [ˈmoʊmənteri] adj. 短暂的，片刻的==

She went on up the stairs. She opened the door of the room. George was on the bed reading.

"Did you get the cat?" he asked, putting the book down.

"It was gone.""Wonder where it wentto," he said, resting his eyes from reading.

She sat down on the bed."I wanted it so much," she said.

"I don't know why I wanted it so much. I wanted that poor kitty. It isn't any fun to be a poor kitty out in the rain."

George was reading again.She wentover and sat in front of the mirror of the dressing table looking at herself with the hand glass.

She studied her profile, first one side and then the other.

> ==profile英 [ˈprəʊfaɪl] 美 [ˈproʊfaɪl] n. 侧面，侧影；简介；外形，轮廓==
>
> n. 形象（the general impression that sb/sth gives to the public and the amount of attention they receive）
>
> 原文：She studied her profile, first one side and then the other.
>
> 她欣赏自己的形象，从这一边，到另一边，再转向后脑和脖颈。
>
> 💧profile作名词还有“简介”的意思，比如：A newspaper published profiles of the candidates' wives.
>
> 一家报纸刊登了几位候选人夫人的简介。
>
> 💧a high/low profile 表示“高 / 低姿态”，比如：I advised her to keep a low profile for the next few days (= not to attract attention) .
>
> 我建议她未来几天保持低姿态。

Then she studied the back of her head and her neck.

"Don't you think it would be a good idea if I let my hair grow out?" she asked, looking at her profile again.

George looked up and saw the back of her neck, clipped close like a boy's.

> ==clipped==
>
> v. 修剪（to cut sth with scissors or shears , in order to make it shorter or neater; to remove sth from somewhere by cutting it off）
>
> 原文：George looked up and saw the back of her neck, clipped close like a boy's.
>
> 乔治抬起头看了看她脖子后面，头发修剪得像个男孩儿。
>
> 💧clip作动词还有“碰撞”的意思，比如：The carclipped the kerb as it turned.
>
> 汽车转弯时撞上了路缘。

"I like it the way it is.""I get so tired of it," she said. "I get so tired of looking like a boy."

George shifted his position in the bed. He hadn't looked away from her since she started to speak.

"You look pretty darn nice," he said.

> <font color=red>"You look pretty darn nice," he said.</font>
>
> “你看起来很漂亮。”他说道。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> look pretty darn nice 看起来很漂亮，darn作副词，表示“极其，非常”（used as a mild swear word, instead of saying damn , to mean ‘extremely’ or ‘very’）pretty darn意为“相当地”，比如：They’ve got a resume that looks pretty darn good. 
>
> 他们的行业履历看上去相当完美。

She laid the mirror down on the dresser and went over to the window and looked out. It was getting dark.

"I want to pull my hair back tight and smooth and make a big knot at the back that I can feel," she said.

"I want to have a kitty to sit on my lap and purr when I stroke her."

"Yeah?" George said from the bed.

"And I want to eat at a table with my own silver and I want candles.

And I want it to be spring and I want to brush my hair out in front of a mirror and I want a kitty and I want some new clothes."

"Oh, shut up and get something to read," George said. He was reading again.

His wife was looking out of the window. It was quite dark now and still raining in the palm trees.

"Anyway, I want a cat," she said, "I want a cat. I want a cat now.

If I can't have long hair or any fun, Ican have a cat."

George was not listening. He was reading his book.

His wife looked out of the window where the light had come on in the square.

Someone knocked at the door.

"Avanti," George said. He looked upfrom his book. In the doorway stoodthe maid.

She held a big tortoise-shell cat pressed tight against her and swung down against her body.

> <font color=red>She held a big tortoise-shell cat pressed tight against her and swung down against her body.</font>
>
> 她抱着一只龟壳花纹的大猫，那猫紧紧地缩在她的怀里，尾巴还在摇摆。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> swung down against her body 尾巴还在摇摆；swing down表示“摇摆”，这里指的是猫的尾巴在摇摆，比如：That would mean if I joined the bob and I swing down with the bob that you should get that same period. 
>
> 那就意味着，如果我也挂上摆锤，和摆锤一起振荡，你们会得到相同的周期。
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> tortoise-shell cat 玳瑁猫，龟甲纹毛猫（a cat having black and cream and yellowish markings)名字来源于海龟的一种——玳瑁，因其皮毛颜色与海龟玳瑁非常相似，故称为玳瑁猫。玳瑁猫的名称是由“玳瑁色猫”简化而来的，因此玳瑁猫并不是猫的一个品种，只是对一种颜色的猫的统称，是黑、黄、白三种颜色混杂的猫。

"Excuse me," she said, "the padrone asked me to bring this for the Signora."

### 背景知识

**💧****The Monuments around the World**

**世界上令人惊叹的纪念碑**

我们今天的内容中描写到一对美国夫妇住的酒店房间正对着战争纪念碑，许多意大利人远道而来就是为了看这座战争纪念碑。（Their room was on the second floor facing the sea. It also faced the public garden and war monument...Italians came from a long way off to look up at the war monument. It was made of bronze and glistened in the rain.)



纪念碑是为了纪念一个人或重要的事件而建立的一种结构，或者是作为他们纪念历史时期或文化遗产的一部分，或者仅仅是历史建筑的一个例子。每一种文化纪念碑都是具有多种含义的象征，它可以代表一个时代、一个地区、一个信仰、一个文化、一个国家或一个城市。每一种建筑都讲述着自己的故事，今天我们来感受一下世界上一些恢弘的纪念碑吧～



\1. 印度泰姬陵（Taj Mahal）

泰姬陵是印度最受欢迎的旅游景点，被誉为“印度明珠”。1631年由莫卧儿皇帝沙贾汗修建，以纪念他的妻子去世后。该纪念碑位于阿格拉，每年吸引了阿格拉两倍的人口。1983年，泰姬陵被宣布为世界遗产，它代表了莫卧儿建筑成就的高峰，被评选为“世界新七大奇迹”。这栋建筑至今仍然像当初建造时那样宏伟，被认为是世界上最完美的建筑作品之一。



\2. 里约热内卢基督像（Cristo Redentor）

也叫巴西基督像，是一座装饰艺术风格的大型耶稣基督雕像，位于巴西的里约热内卢基督山上，是该市的标志，也是世界最闻名的纪念雕塑之一。落成于1931年，总高38米，体积庞大，有1145吨重，左右手的指间距达到了23米。雕像中的耶稣基督身着长袍，双臂平举，深情地俯瞰山下里约热内卢市的美丽全景，预示着博爱的精神和对独立的赞许。耶稣像面向着碧波荡漾的大西洋，张开着的双臂从远处望去，就像一个巨大的十字架，显得庄重、威严。



\3. 美国拉什莫尔山国家纪念公园（Mount Rushmore National Memorial）

俗称美国总统山、美国总统公园，拉什莫尔山国家纪念碑是史诗般的比例独特的地标。20世纪30年代，雕刻在南达科他州的花岗岩中，纪念碑描绘了一些国家历史上伟大的总统的面孔：乔治·华盛顿，托马斯·杰斐逊，西奥多·罗斯福和亚伯拉罕·林肯，这四位总统被认为代表了美国建国150年来的历史。



\4. 雅典卫城（Acropolis）

雅典卫城是希腊最杰出的古建筑群，是综合性的公共建筑，为宗教政治的中心地，也是世界上最著名的纪念碑之一。被称为雅典的“阿克罗波利斯”，原意为“高处的城市”或“高丘上的城邦”。它是古希腊文化中最重要的参考点，也是雅典城本身的象征，它代表了公元前5世纪艺术发展的顶峰。在佩里克尔的黄金时代，古希腊文明以一种理想的方式出现在山上，一些建筑杰作被竖立在它的地面上。



\5.  柬埔寨吴哥城（Angkor Thom）

吴哥城是一个有城墙的城市，是安科里王朝的最后一个首都。在1181年，贾瓦里曼七世从巴普修和菲利亚卡斯等现存的建筑开始，在他们周围建造了一个宏伟的封闭城市，加上了外墙、护城河和吴哥窟的一些最伟大的寺庙，其中包括他的国家庙宇巴戎，位于城市中心。城门有五个入口，每一个都有一个基点，还有通往皇宫的胜利大门。每扇门都有四个巨大的脸。南门经常是旅游的第一站。



\6. 阿拉伯克尔白圣殿（Kaaba temple）

克尔白圣殿是一个位于沙特阿拉伯麦加的长剑状建筑，是伊斯兰教最神圣的地方，最古老，也是世界上最著名的文化纪念碑。《可兰经》指出，卡巴是由亚伯拉罕和他的儿子以实玛利在阿拉伯半岛定居后建造的。这座建筑周围建了一座清真寺，无论在哪里，全世界的穆斯林都在祈祷时面对着卡巴。

### 课文理解

《雨中的猫》（Cat in the Rain）讲述了一对美国夫妇在意大利旅行，一天在旅馆里，妻子看到窗外的大雨里有一只猫蜷缩在绿色的桌子下，感觉可怜，想把那只猫救上来。但等到她走到窗下，却发现猫已经不见了。回到房间后，妻子无比失落，不断向丈夫哀诉。最后，旅馆的老板派侍女送上来了一只玳瑁猫。这对夫妇的对话和行为表现都暗藏了有意思的小细节，比如他们俩之间其实早已缺乏热情、貌合神离——

💧**Clue 1**: There is passion lacking between the couple.



**Evidence 1**: "I'm going down and get that kitty," the American wife said.

"I'll do it," her husband offered from the bed.

"No, I'll get it. The poor kitty is out trying to keep dry under the table."

The husband went on reading, lying propped up with the two pillows at the foot of the bed.

"Don't get wet," he said.

“我要下去捉那只小猫。”美国太太说。

“我来去捉吧。”她丈夫从床上说。

“不，我去捉。外边那只小猫正躲在桌子底下避雨呢。”

丈夫继续看书，他肩后垫着两只枕头，躺在床脚那一头。

“别淋湿了。”他说。



**Evidence 2**: "It was gone."

"Wonder where it went to," he said, resting his eyes from reading. She sat down on the bed.

"I wanted it so much," she said. "I don't know why I wanted it so much. I wanted that poor kitty. It isn't any fun to be a poor kitty out in the rain."

George was reading again.

“跑掉了。”

“不知跑到哪里去了。”他说。眼睛移开书，休息一下。她在床上坐下。

“我太想要那只猫了。”她说，“我不知道我为什么那么想要那只猫。我要那只可怜的小猫。做一只待在外面雨里的可怜的小猫，可不是什么乐事啊。”

乔治又在看书了。



第一个细节是当妻子提出要下去救猫的时候，丈夫只是礼貌性地提出要下去，随后便继续看书不为所动了。第二个细节是妻子回来后哀叹自己多么想要那只猫，丈夫敷衍地回答后就充耳不闻了。这两个细节都说明了这对夫妇彼此之间的冷淡疏离——丈夫欠缺对妻子的关心，妻子也毅然不顾地单独行动。



妻子又继续喋喋不休地哭诉，她不仅想要猫，她还想把自己的头发重新留长好扎个发髻，直到最后已经语无伦次了（"Anyway, I want a cat," she said, "I want a cat. I want a cat now. If I can't have long hair or any fun, I can have a cat."）这里实际上暗示了妻子对猫的渴望、以及对自己外型的不满，其实都是她内心对自己在婚姻中的女性地位和身份的焦虑外显——



💧**Clue 2**: The wife is anxious about her status and identity in the marriage.



**Evidence 1**: "Don't you think it would be a good idea if I let my hair grow out?" she asked, looking at her profile again.

George looked up and saw the back of her neck, clipped close like a boy's.

"I like it the way it is."

"I get so tired of it," she said. "I get so tired of looking like a boy."

“我把头发留起来，你不觉得很好吗？”她问道，又端详起自己的侧影来。

乔治抬起头，看她的后边的头颈。头发剪得短短的，真像一个男孩。

“我喜欢你现在这样子。”

“我可烦透这样子了。”她说，“看上去像个男孩，我真烦透了。”



**Evidence 2**: She laid the mirror down on the dresser and went over to the window and looked out. It was getting dark.

"I want to pull my hair back tight and smooth and make a big knot at the back that I can feel," she said. "I want to have a kitty to sit on my lap and purr when I stroke her."

她把镜子放在梳妆台上，走到窗边，向外望去。天渐渐黑了。

“我要把头发向后光滑地梳起扎紧，在后脑勺扎个我可以摸到的大发髻。”她说，“我要让一只小猫坐在我腿上，我一抚摸它，它就会呜呜叫。”



20世纪初的20年代，美国社会中的女性地位正在发生巨大的变化。比如女性开始留短发，打扮穿着更加中性，这些都代表了女性对开放和独立自由的渴望。这位妻子也追随了当时的浪潮，但她表现出了相反的焦虑和不安；或者说，她在重新找回女性在家庭当中的传统角色。对猫的渴望也是对孩子的渴望——成为母亲；留长头发就更不必说了，这是长久以来对女性特质的一个刻板印象。



最后小说的结尾也很有意味，旅馆的老板派侍女送来了一只猫。而在这之前，旅馆老板对这位妻子殷勤有加，这也激发了她的好感（The wife liked him. She liked the way he wanted to serve her. ）然而故事就这样戛然而止了（"Excuse me," she said, "the padrone asked me to bring this for the Signora."）剩下的是给读者无限的想象空间。

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****All Kinds of Cats**

**各个种类的猫**

我们今天的故事是围绕雨中之猫展开的。（Outside right under their window a cat was crouched under one of the dripping green tables. The cat was trying to make herself so compact that she would not be dripped on.）在今天的彩蛋中我们就来看一看都有哪些种类的猫，一起来云吸猫吧～



\1. 英国短毛猫（British Shorthair）

体形圆胖，四肢粗短发达，毛短而密，头大脸圆，温柔平静，对人友善，极易饲养。大而圆的眼睛根据被毛不同而呈现各种颜色。作为一个古老的猫品种，其历史可追溯至古罗马时期的家猫，由于拥有悠久的育种历史，可以称得上是猫家族中的典范。更重要的是，有了广泛的配种历史后，这种猫拥有了更健康的身体和更温驯的性格。



\2. 美国短毛猫（American Shorthair）

又称美洲短毛虎纹猫，美国短毛猫素以体格魁梧，骨骼粗壮，肌肉发达，生性聪明，性格温顺著称，是短毛猫中的大体型猫。是由美国人把欧洲猫与美洲大陆的土种猫加以改良而育成，是家猫中的传统品种。1971年，其被选为美国最好的猫种之一。



\3. 波斯猫（Persian cat）

以阿富汗的土种长毛猫和土耳其的安哥拉长毛猫为基础，在英国经过100多年的选种繁殖，于1860年诞生的一个品种。波斯猫是最常见的长毛猫，波斯猫有一张讨人喜爱的面庞，长而华丽的背毛，优雅的举止，故有“猫中王子”、“王妃”之称，是世界上爱猫者最喜欢的纯种猫之一，占有极其重要的地位。



\4.  斯芬克斯猫（Sphynx cat）

亦称加拿大无毛猫（Canadian Hairless），是加拿大安大略省多伦多市养猫爱好者在1966年从一窝几乎是无毛的猫仔中，经过近交选育，特意为对猫毛过敏的爱猫者培育成的。这种猫是自然的基因突变产生的宠物猫，除了在耳、口、鼻、尾前锻、脚等部位有些又薄又软的胎毛外，其它全身部分均无毛，皮肤多皱有弹性。加拿大无毛猫性情温顺，独立性强，无攻击性，能与其它猫狗相处。



\5. 布偶猫（Ragdoll）

又称布拉多尔，发源于美国，是一种杂交品种宠物猫。是现存体型最大、体重最重的猫之一。头呈楔形，眼大而圆，被毛丰厚，四肢较长且富有肉感，尾长，身体柔软，毛色有重点色、手套色或双色等等。布偶猫较为温顺好静，对人友善。其美丽优雅又非常类似于狗的性格（Puppy cat），而又被称为"仙女猫"，"小狗猫"。特殊的外貌和温和的性格是布偶猫最大的特点之一。



\6. 暹罗猫（Siamese cat）

世界著名的短毛猫，也是短毛猫的代表品种。种族原产于暹罗（今泰国），故名暹罗猫。在200多年前，这种珍贵的猫仅在泰国的皇宫和大寺院中饲养，是足不出户的贵族。暹罗猫能够较好适应主人当地的气候，且性格刚烈好动，机智灵活，好奇心特强，善解人意。



\7. 加菲猫（Garfield）

有着浑圆的眼睛，大而圆的头部，两眼间距较阔，脖子短而粗，鼻子很短，因为鼻节较短泪腺发达容易流眼泪，性格温顺，十分亲人。

## Chapter 8

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/f1ba415f526680f178c08d5b26495a64-sz_697675.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

A Day's Wait

He came into the room to shut the windows while we were still in bed and I saw he looked ill.

He was shivering, his face was white, and he walked slowly as though it ached to move.

> ==shiver英 [ˈʃɪvə(r)] 美 [ˈʃɪvɚ] vi. 颤抖，哆嗦，发抖；碎裂 n. 颤抖；寒战；碎片 vt. 打碎==

"What's the matter, Schatz?" "I've got a headache."

"You better go back to bed." "No, I'm all right."

"You go to bed. I'll see you when I'm dressed.”

But when I came downstairs he was dressed, sitting by the fire, looking a very sick and miserable boy of nine years.

When I put my hand on his forehead I knew he had a fever.

"You go up to bed," I said, "you're sick." "I'm all right," he said.

When the doctor came he took the boy's temperature.

"What is it?"I asked him. "One hundred and two."

Downstairs, the doctor left three different medicines in different colored capsules with instructions for giving them.

> ==capsule英 [ˈkæpsju:l] 美 [ˈkæpsul] n. 胶囊；小容器；太空舱；蒴果==

One was to bring down the fever, another a purgative, the third to overcome an acid condition.

> ==purgative英 [ˈpɜ:gətɪv] 美 [ˈpɜ:rgətɪv] adj. 净化的，清洗的；通便的 n. 泻剂==
>
> ==acid英 [ˈæsɪd] 美 [ˈæsɪd] n. 酸；迷幻药 adj. 酸的；尖酸的==
>
> <font color=red>One was to bring down the fever, another a purgative, the third to overcome an acid condition.</font>
>
> 一种是退热的，另一种是泻药，第三种是控制酸的。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> 三个分句可以理解为并列的成分，后面两个分句的谓语动词与第一个相同，可省略。原句为：One was to bring down the fever, another was a purgative, and the third was to overcome an acid condition. 
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ① bring down the fever 退烧，bring down表示“降低”，比如：We must bring down the cost of doing business. 
>
> 我们必须在从事商业的过程中降低成本。
>
> ②another a purgative 另一种是泻药，purgative是“泻药”的意思，to administer/prescribe a purgative 用/开泻药；
>
> ③overcome an acid condition 控制酸，acid condition指“酸性环境”。

The germs of influenza can only exist in an acid condition, he explained.

> ==influenza英 [ˌɪnfluˈenzə] 美 [ˌɪnflʊ'enzə] n. 流行性感冒，同flu==

He seemed to know all about influenza and said there was nothing to worry about if the fever did not go above one hundred and four degrees.

This was a light epidemic of flu and there was no danger if you avoided pneumonia.

> ==epidemic英 [ˌepɪˈdemɪk] 美 [ˌɛpɪˈdɛmɪk] n. 流行病；流行；蔓延，猖獗 adj. 流行性的；盛行的==
>
> n.  流行病（a large number of cases of a particular disease happening at the same time in a particular community）
>
> 原文：This was a light epidemic of flu and there was no danger if you avoided pneumonia.
>
> 这是轻度流感，假如不并发肺炎就没有危险。
>
> 💧epidemic作名词还有“泛滥”的意思，比如：Drug experts say it could spell the end of the crack epidemic. 
>
> 禁毒专家说它可能会结束强效可卡因吸食泛滥的局面。

Back in the room I wrote the boy's temperature down and made a note of the time to give the various capsules.

"Do you want me to read to you?" "All right. If you want to," said the boy.

His face was very white and there were dark areas under his eyes.

He lay still in bed and seemed very detached from what was going on.

> <font color=red>He lay still in bed and seemed verydetached from what was going on.</font>
>
> 他躺在床上一动也不动，似乎超然物外。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①lay still in bed躺在床上一动也不动，still在这里作副词，表示“静止地”（without moving or making a sound），比如：He sat still as a statue. 他像一座雕像似的坐着一动不动。
>
> ②detached from what was going on 超然物外，detached作形容词，是“超然的”（not personally involved in something or has no emotional interest in it）的意思，比如：Hawthorne has a lively description of marital problems in America based on moral criticism, and expresses his very detached attitude to that. 
>
> 霍桑习惯以道德批判的方式去反映美国错综复杂的婚姻家庭问题，并表现出超然的生活态度。

I read aloud from Howard Pyle's Book of Pirates; but I could see he was not following what I was reading.

"How do you feel, Schatz?"I asked him.

"Just the same, so far." he said.

I sat at the foot of the bed and read to myself while I waited for it to be time to give another capsule.

It would have been natural for him to go to sleep, but when I looked up he was looking at the foot of the bed, looking very strangely.

"Why don't you try to go to sleep? I'll wake you up for the medicine."

"I'd rather stay awake."After a while he said to me, "You don't have to stay here with me, Papa, if it bothers you."

"It doesn't bother me." "No, I mean you don't have to stay if it's going to bother you."

I thought perhaps he was a little light-headed and after giving him the prescribed capsule at eleven o'clock I went out for a while.

> ==prescribe英 [prɪˈskraɪb] 美 [prɪˈskraɪb] vt. 开药；开处方；规定；指定==
>
> v. 开（药）（If a doctor prescribes medicine or treatment for you, he or she tells you what medicine or treatment to have.）
>
> 原文：I thought perhaps he was a little light-headed and after giving him the prescribedcapsule at eleven o'clock I went out for a while.
>
> 我以为他也许有点头晕，到了十一点我给他吃了医生开的药丸后就到外面去了一会儿。
>
> 💧prescribe作动词还有“规定“的意思，比如：The syllabus prescribes precisely which books should be studied.
>
> 教学大纲明确规定了哪些是必读的书。
>
> <font color=red>I thought perhaps he was a little light-headed and after giving him the prescribed capsule at eleven o'clock I went out for a while.</font>
>
> 我以为他也许有点头晕，到了十一点我给他吃了医生开的药丸后就到外面去了一会儿。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①a little light-headed 有点头晕，light-headed意为“头晕的”（not completely in control of your thoughts or movements; slightly faint），比如：After four glasses of wine he began to feel light-headed.
>
> 他四杯酒下肚后开始感到头晕目眩起来。
>
> ②the prescribed capsule 医生开的药丸，prescribe做动词有“开药方”的意思，比如：Our doctor diagnosed a throat infection and prescribed antibiotic and junior aspirin.
>
> 我们的医生诊断是喉部感染，并且开了一些抗生素和小剂量阿司匹林。

It was a bright, cold day, the ground covered with a sleet that had frozen so that it seemed as if all the bare trees, the bushes, the cut brush and all the grass and the bare ground had been varnished with ice.

> ==varnish英 [ˈvɑ:nɪʃ] 美 [ˈvɑ:rnɪʃ] n. 清漆 vt. 给…涂上清漆==
>
> <font color=red>It was a bright, cold day, the ground covered with a sleet that had frozen so that it seemed as if all the bare trees, the bushes, the cut brush and all the grass and the bare ground had been varnished with ice.</font>
>
> 那天天气晴朗寒冷，地面上盖着一层雨夹雪都结成冰了，因此看上去所有光秃秃的树木，灌木，修剪过的灌木，全部草地和空地上面都涂上层冰。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> had been varnished with ice 都涂上层冰，varnish的原义是“在...上涂清漆”，这里varnish... with ice 指涂上层冰。

I took the young Irish setter for a little walk up the road and along a frozen creek,

but it was difficult to stand or walk on the glassy surface and the red dog slipped and slithered and fell twice, hard, once dropping my gun and having it slide over the ice.

> ==slither英 [ˈslɪðə(r)] 美 [ˈslɪðɚ] vi. 滑动；蜿蜒地滑行==
>
> <font color=red>I took the young Irish setter for a little walkup the road and along a frozen creek, but it was difficult to stand or walk on the glassy surface and the red dog slipped and slitheredand fell twice, hard, once dropping my gun and having it slide over the ice.</font>
>
> 我带了一条爱尔兰长毛小猎狗顺那条路，沿着一条结冰的小溪散散步，但在光滑的路面上站也好，走也好，都不容易，那条红毛狗跳一下滑倒了，我也重重摔了两交，有一次我的枪都掉下来，在冰上滑掉了。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①up the road 顺着、沿着道路 , 比如：Without looking at either Manuel or the boy she turned to her companion and they went on up the road together. 
>
> 没有看曼纽尔也没有看那个男孩，她转向她的同伴，他们一起沿着路继续走去。
>
> ②slipped and slithered 跳一下滑倒了，having it slide over the ice （枪）在冰上滑掉了（it指my gun, 我的枪），这句话出现了三个表示“滑”的单词：slip，slitter，slide. 他们有什么区别呢？
>
> slip：指走或跑时"失足，滑倒"。含有不由自主及突然的意思.  
>
> 例句：I slipped on the snow and sprained my ankle.我在雪地上滑倒,扭伤了脚踝。
>
> slide：指在光滑的平面上"平稳地滑动"。 
>
> 例句：The children are sliding on the ice.孩子们在滑冰。 
>
> slither指"摇晃地，跌跌撞撞地滑动"
>
> 例句：We slithered all the way here in the heavy snow.在大雪中我们一路连跌带滑地来到这儿. 
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> Irish setter 爱尔兰长毛猎犬：被称作“莫德犬”或“红犬”，在加衣里克曾一度闻名。这种充满活力的、灵敏的犬种很乐意进行体育活动。爱尔兰长毛猎犬是一种精力旺盛、性格外向的犬种。

We flushed a covey of quail under a high clay bank with overhanging brush and killed two as they went out of sight over the top of the bank.

> <font color=red>We flushed a covey of quail under a high clay bank with overhanging brush and killed two as they went out of sight over the top of the bank.</font>
>
> 一群鹌鹑躲在悬垂着灌木的高高土堤下，被我们惊起了，它们从土堤顶上飞开时我打死了两只。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①flushed a covey of quail 惊起一群鹌鹑，flush在这里作动词，表示“把(人或动物)驱赶出”（If you flush people or animals out of a place where they are hiding, you find or capture them by forcing them to come out of that place.），比如：They flushed them out of their hiding places.
>
> 他们把他们从藏身之处赶了出来。
>
> ②a covey of 表示“一群”（A covey of grouse or partridges is a small group of them.）比如：They let me stumble about on the trails for a time before my clumsiness flushed a covey of doves from their rest. 
>
> 我笨拙的动作惊飞了一群窝里的鸽子，之后他们又任凭我在藤蔓上绊了一脚。
>
> ③they went out of sight 它们飞开时， out of sight 意为“看不见，在视野之外”，比如：The hares raced away out of sight. 
>
> 野兔飞奔而去，很快就看不见了

Some of the covey 55 lit the trees, but most of them scattered into brush piles and it was necessary to jump on the ice-coated mounds of brush several times before they would flush.

> ==mound英 [maʊnd] 美 [maʊnd] n. 土墩，土冈，土丘；一堆 vt. 成堆，堆积==

Coming out while you were poised unsteadily on the icy, springy brush they made difficult shooting and killed two, missed five, and started back pleased to have found a coveyclose to the house and happy there were so many left to find on anotherday.

> ==springy英 [ˈsprɪŋi] 美 [ˈsprɪŋi] adj. 有弹力[性]的==

At the house they said the boy had refused to let anyone come into the room.

"You can't come in," he said. "You mustn't get what I have."

I went up to him and found him in exactly the position I had left him, white faced, but with the tops of his cheeks flushed by the fever, staring still, as he had stared, at the foot of the bed.

I took his temperature."What is it?"

"Something like a hundred," I said. It was one hundred and two and four tenth.

"It was a hundred and two," he said.

"Who said so?" "The doctor."

"Your temperature is all right," I said. "It's nothing to worry about."

"I don't worry," he said, "but I can't keep from thinking."

"Don't think," I said. "Just take it easy."

"I'm taking it easy," he said and looked straight ahead.

He was evidently holding tight onto himself about something.

> <font color=red>“I'm taking it easy,” he said and looked straight ahead. He was evidently holding tight onto himself about something.</font>
>
> “我不急，”他说着一直朝前看。显然他心里藏着什么事情。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①I'm taking it easy 我不急，take it easy意为“放轻松，不紧张”，比如：Take it easy. Don't be so sensitive. 
>
> 放松点，别这么敏感。
>
> ②holding tight onto himself about something心里藏着什么事情，hold tight onto oneself 控制自己不做某事，这里形容小男孩压抑着自己感情的状态。

"Take this with water." "Do you think it will do any good?"

"Of course it will."I sat down and opened the Pirate book and commenced to read, but I could see he was not following, so I stopped.

"About what time do you think I'm going to die?" he asked.

"What?" "About how long will it be before I die?"

"You aren't going to die. What's the matter with you?"

"Oh, yes, I am. I heard him say a hundred and two."

"People don't die with a fever of onehundred and two. That's a silly way to talk."

"I know they do. At school in Francethe boys told me you can't live with forty-four degrees. I've got a hundred and two."

He had been waiting to die all day, ever since nine o'clock in the morning.

"You poor Schatz," I said. "Poor old Schatz. It's like miles and kilometers. You aren't going to die.

That's a different thermometer. On that thermometer thirty-seven is normal. On this kind it's ninety-eight."

> ==thermometer英 [θəˈmɒmɪtə(r)] 美 [θərˈmɑ:mɪtə(r)] n. 温度计；体温表==

"Are you sure?" "Absolutely," I said. "It's like miles and kilometers.

You know, like how many kilometerswe make when we do seventy in the car?"

"Oh," he said.But his gaze at the foot of his bed relaxed slowly.

The hold over himself relaxed too, finally, and the next day it was very slack and he cried very easily at little things that were of no importance.

> ==slack英 [slæk] 美 [slæk] adj. 松散的；萧条的；懈怠的 vi. 偷懒；松懈；磨洋工 adv. 松弛地 n. 松弛；裤子(复数)；煤渣==

### 背景知识

**💧****Celsius and Fahrenheit Scales**

**摄氏度和华氏度**

我们今天的内容中出现了两种不同的体温计，一种是以摄氏度量化，一种以华氏度。（It's like miles and kilometers. You aren't going to die. That's a different thermometer. On that thermometer thirty-seven is normal. On this kind it's ninety-eight. 这好比英里和公里。你不会死的。那是两种体温表啊。那种表上三十七度算正常。这种表要九十八度才算正常。）那么摄氏度和华氏度有哪些差别呢？



\1. 所代表的含义不同：

摄氏度：是指在1标准大气压下，纯净的冰水混合物的温度为0度，水的沸点为100度，其间平均分为100份，每一等份为1度，记作1℃。

华氏度：是指在标准大气压下，冰的熔点为32℉，水的沸点为212℉，中间有180等分，每等分为华氏1度，记作“1℉”。



\2. 适用范围不同：

摄氏度：包括我国在内的世界上绝大多数国家都使用摄氏度。

华氏度：世界上仅有5个国家使用华氏度，包括巴哈马、伯利兹、英属开曼群岛、帕劳、美利坚合众国及其他附属领土（波多黎各、关岛、美属维京群岛）。

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/61ebf20cdc1d9e1d48a6f54987b3f2e2-sz_264299.png?x-oss-process=image/resize,w_1080/auto-orient,1/crop,x_0,y_77,w_540,h_360)



\3. 代表符号不同：

摄氏度：用符号℃。是以其发明者安德斯·摄尔修斯（Anders Celsius，1701-1744）的姓氏的第一个字母“C”来表示。

华氏度：符号℉。是以其发明者德国人华伦海特（Gabriel D. Fahrenheit，1686—1736）命名的。



💧**Howard Pyle and Book of Pirates**

**霍华德•派尔和他的《海贼王》**

文章中提到爸爸给儿子读霍华德•派尔的《海贼王》。（I read aloud from Howard Pyle's*Book of Pirates*; but I could see he was not following what I was reading.）我们一起来了解一下吧～



\1. 霍华德•派尔（Howard Pyle）

美国著名插画家、作家，是难得一见的在文字写作和绘画方面皆造诣不凡的大师级人物。霍华德·派尔少年时代就表现出超人的绘画才能，为—些杂志定期绘制插图，此外他在写作方面也很有天赋，因之前接到许多民闾故事和传说，也就促成后来他创作了一系列骑士和英雄人物的历险记，主要作品有《海贼王》《罗宾汉奇遇记》《银手奥托》《骑士麦尔斯》等，大多取材于中世纪的神话或殖民地时期历史，再现了那个时代的社会风貌。霍华德·派尔的作品在英文领域—直有着良好的口碑，被列为世界名著，《海贼王》《骑士麦尔斯》等被列入欧美青少年必读书目。



\2. *Book of Pirates*

《海贼王》

这本书以独特的视角描述了一些历史上著名的海盗故事，从布兰德船长的幽灵到杰克巴里斯特的财宝，一幕幕或是妙趣横生或是惊心动魄，使人尤如身临其境。一大批极富盛名的海盗头子，包括著名的黑胡子爱德华·提奇、基德船长、黑色准男爵罗伯茨等都是这段时间海盗史上的传奇人物，使读者可以更真实地了解海盗的生存世界，真正走进那段血雨腥风的旷世传奇。 

### 课文理解

《一天的等待》（*A Day's Wait*）里的主人公是一个小男孩，他感染了流感，发着高烧（102华氏度，大约接近39摄氏度）。虽然这个故事在表面上似乎只是简单的小男孩因为不知道摄氏度和华氏度的差别，而误以为自己很快就要死了，但其实里面有很多暗藏的细节。首先是父亲和小男孩之间的言语交流鲜少，并且父亲也疏于察看儿子的心里状态。所以当他知道原来儿子误会了温度计算标准而陷入沮丧的时候很是惊讶——

💧**Clue 1**: The father doesn't tend much to the boy's inner feelings.



**Evidence 1**: After a while he said to me, 'You don't have to stay here with me, Papa, if it bothers you.'

'It doesn't bother me.'

'No, I mean you don't have to stay if it's going to bother you.'

I thought perhaps he was a little light-headed and after giving him the prescribed capsule at eleven o'clock I went out for a while.

过了一会儿，他对我说：“要是你心烦就不用在这儿陪我，爸爸。”

“我没心烦。”

“不，我是说如果叫你心烦的话，就不用在这儿陪。”

我以为他也许有点头晕，到了十一点我给他吃了医生开的药丸后就到外面去了一会儿。



**Evidence 2**: 'About what time do you think I'm going to die?' he asked.

'What?'

'About how long will it be before I die?'

'You aren't going to die. What's the matter with you?'

'Oh, yes, I am. I heard him say a hundred and two.'

'People don't die with a fever of one hundred and two. That's a silly way to talk.'

“你看我几时会死？”他问。

“什么？”

“我还能活多久才死？”

“你不会死的。你怎么啦？”

“哦，是的，我要死了。我听见他说一百零二度的。”

“发烧到一百零二度可死不了。你这么说可真傻。”



内心冲突是这篇小说的一大特点，人物之间没有外在的争斗或冲突，矛盾都隐藏在内心活动里。比如这里就是小男孩在不小心听到医生告诉父亲自己的体温后什么话也没说，而是暗自陷在悲观沮丧里。这样再回头看一开始小男孩对父亲说的话（让他如果觉得心烦就不用在床边陪着他），我们就能明白事出何因了。



这也解释了他之后表现出来的敏感，甚至可以说过度反应：他不让任何人走进他的房间，因为他觉得自己感染了流感就要死了，这是一个致命可怕的病，所以他不让家人进去看他。（At the house they said the boy had refused to let anyone come into the room. 'You can't come in,' he said. 'You mustn't get what I have.'）



虽然后来父亲给他解释清楚了其间的误会，但小男孩的心态是否真的重新恢复如初了呢？作者留下来了一个模棱两可的结尾——



💧**Clue 2**: The impact on the boy is ambiguous.



**Evidence 1**: 'Are you sure?'

'Absolutely,' I said. 'It's like miles and kilometers. You know, like how many kilometers we make when we do seventy in the car?'

'Oh,' he said.

“这话当真？”

“绝对错不了，”我说，“好比英里和公里。你知道我们开车时车速七十英里合多少公里吗？”

“哦。”他说。



**Evidence 2**: The hold over himself relaxed too, finally, and the next day it was very slack and he cried very easily at little things that were of no importance.

他内心的紧张终于松弛下来了。第二天一点也不紧张而来，为了一点小事，动不动就哭了。



最后一句提到：he cried very easily at little things that were of no importance，这里会让读者非常矛盾？前面不是说他不再那么紧张了吗？那么这里的“他动不动就为一点小事哭”是尽管他恢复好了，但他本来的性格就如此，还是指因为这一次的经历让他变得敏感多疑，所以总是很容易被惹哭？



结合作者自己在战场上的经历，以及目睹战事中的伤痛病死，这里可以猜测作者想表达的主旨是即便是很小的伤害或恐惧，都可以对一个人的性格造成影响，或者因此而永远烙上心理伤疤。

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****How to Describe Diseases**

**生病的英文表达方法**



我们今天的内容当中描述了Schatz患流感的情景。（He seemed to know all about influenza and said there was nothing to worry about if the fever did not go above one hundred and four degrees. This was a light epidemic of flu and there was no danger if you avoided pneumonia.）接下来我们一起来看一下生病该如何用英语表达吧～



\1. have：表示“生病”，后常跟表示疾病的名词，是最通俗的说法，多用于口语。

例句：As I remember, my brother and sister both had severe asthmatic attacks in the childhood.
