我记得，我弟弟和妹妹小时候都得过严重的哮喘病。



\2. take/catch:均可表示“生病”，且含有“感染”之意。美国人多用take，英国人多用catch。

例句：Mary takes cold easily. 玛丽易患感冒。

Towards the end of the year, his son caught scarlet fever. 快到年底的时候他儿子得了腥红热。



\3. suffer from: 常用来表示“患病”，后接疾病名词，多用于医生与病人的交谈之中。

例句：Is there anybody in your family who has suffered from the same eye disease as you? 你家中还有没有人得过跟你一样的眼病?



\4. (be) ill with: 如表示“患......病”的时候后面须跟with，多见于英式英语。

例句：The patient is ill with influenza. 病人患流行性感冒。



\5. be vulnerable to: 一般常用来表示“易患......病”。

例句：Fibres from the macular region of the retina are particularly vulnerable to inflammation. 视网膜斑区的纤维特别易患炎症。



\6. expose...to (be exposed to): 以为“使......易患......病”，“易患......病”。

例句： An attack of fever weakens a child and exposes it to all kinds of infections. 发烧使患儿虚弱，易患各种感染。

When having cold, children are exposed to pneumonia. 孩子感冒时易患肺炎。



\7. be seized with: 一般表示“突然患......病”。

例句：The patient was seized with apoplexy yesterday afernoon.病人昨天下午忽患中风。



\8. be attacked with: 基本意是“为......疾病所侵袭”，常译成“患......病”。

例句：Attacked with acute myocardial inraction, the patient was surveilled for a week in hospital. 病人患急性心肌梗塞后，在医院里监护了一个星期。



\9. be afflicted with: 其基本意为“为......病所折磨”，常用来表达“患......病”，其特征是，不仅表示患病的开始，还表示患病过程中所受之苦，特别是精神上的痛苦。

例句：For many years Harold was afflicted with edematous laryngitis. 哈德罗患水肿性喉炎多年了。



\10. be infected with: 意为“被......所感染”，“被......所侵袭”，可译成“患......病”。

例句：On necropsy the patient was found to have been infected with tuberculosis as well. 尸检发现病人还患过结核病。

## Chapter 9.1

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/add280ef01fe447f561eaee8008c226a-sz_1375522.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

Big Two-Hearted River

The train went on up the track out of sight, around one of the hills of burnt timber.

Nick sat down on the bundle of canvas and bedding the baggage man had pitched out of the door of the baggage car.

There was no town, nothing but the rails and the burned-over coun-try.

The thirteen saloons that had lined the one street of Seney had not left a trace.

The foundations of the Mansion House hotel stuck up above the ground.

The stone was chipped and split by the fire.

It was all that was left of the town of Seney.

Even the surface had been burned off the ground.

Nick looked at the burned-over stretch of hillside, where he had expected to find the scattered houses of the town and then walked down the railroad track to the bridge over the river.

The river was there. It swirled against the log spiles of the bridge.

Nick looked down into the clear, brown water, colored from the pebbly bottom, and watched the trout keeping themselves steady in the current with wavering fins.

As he watched them they changed their positions by quick angles, only to hold steady in the fast water again.

Nick watched them a long time.

He watched them holding themselves with their noses into the current, many trout in deep, fast moving water, slightly distorted as he watched far down through the glassy convex surface of the pool,

its surface pushing and swelling smooth against the resistance of thelog-driven piles of the bridge.

> ==resistance英 [rɪˈzɪstəns] 美 [rɪˈzɪstəns] n. 抵制；抵抗(力)；阻力，电阻==
>
> <font color=red>He watched them holding themselves with their noses into the current, many trout in deep, fast moving water, slightly distorted as he watched far down through the glassy convex surface of the pool, its surface pushing and swelling smooth against the resistance of the log-driven piles of the bridge.</font>
>
> 他看它们把鼻子探进激流，稳定了身子，这许多在飞速流动的深水中的鳟鱼显得稍微有些变形，因为他是穿过水潭那凸透镜般的水面一直望到深处的，水潭表面的流水拍打在阻住去路的圆木桩组成的桥墩上，滑溜地激起波浪。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> 这里many trout...surface of the pool 和 its surface...of the bridge两句都是独立主格结构。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①slightly distorted 稍微有些变形，distort 意为“变形”（to change the shape, appearance or sound of sth so that it is strange or not clear），比如：a fairground mirror that distorts your shape
>
> 露天游乐场的哈哈镜
>
> distort 作动词还有“歪曲”的意思，比如：The media distorts reality; categorises people as all good or all bad.
>
> 媒体会歪曲事实，将人说得不是完美无缺就是一无是处。
>
> ②log-driven piles of the bridge 圆木桩组成的桥墩，这里log－driven 意为“由原木组成的”，－driven 是“由...... 组成”的意思（influenced or caused by a particular thing），比如：a character-driven movie
>
> 以人物为主的电影
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> trout 鲑鳟鱼，是一个笼统的概念，它不是特指某一种鱼，而是鲑鱼和鳟鱼的统称。鲑鳟鱼类以其只能在低温水域中繁衍生长，正常生长的上限水温很低，没有明显的下限温度，因此被称为冷水鱼。鲑鳟鱼鱼体呈流线型，口大而斜，牙锥状，体背小圆鳞，背鳍和腹鳍各一个，尾鳍稍凹入或叉形。

At the bottom of the pool were the big trout. Nick did not see them at first.

Then he saw them at the bottom of the pool, big trout looking to hold themselves on the gravel bottom in a varying mist of gravel and sand, raised in spurts by the current.

> ==spurt英 [spɜ:t] 美 [spɜ:rt] vt.&vi. 喷出；迸出 vi. 迅速行进；冲刺 n. 喷出；涌出；迸发；激增==
>
> n. (喷射出的)一股 （A spurt of liquid is a stream of it which comes out of something very forcefully.）
>
> 原文：... big trout looking to hold themselves on the gravel bottom in a varying mist of gravel and sand, raised in spurts by the current.
>
> 这些大鳟鱼指望在潭底的砾石层上稳住身子，正处在流水激起的一股股象游移不定的迷雾般的砾石和沙子中。
>
> 💧spurt 做动词还有“冲刺”的意思，比如：Shespurted past me to get to the line first.
>
> 她冲刺超过我，率先抵达终点线。
>
> <font color=red>Then he saw them at the bottom of the pool, big trout looking to hold themselves onthe gravel bottom in a varying mist of gravel and sand, raised in spurts by the current.</font>
>
> 后来他才看见它们在潭底，这些大鳟鱼指望在潭底的砾石层上稳住身子，正处在流水激起的一股股象游移不定的迷雾般的砾石和沙子中。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> 这句话有三个分句，第一个小句的主语是he，第二个的主语是big trout，两小句中间没有连词，且第二个小句之后跟的是非谓语动词looking，所以第二个小句是独立主格结构，big trout 是逻辑主语
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①looking to hold themselves on 指望在......上稳住身子，look to 在这里是“指望”的意思，比如：He runs the team because he commands their respect. The kids really look to him.
>
> 他管理这个团队，因为他博得了孩子们的尊敬。孩子们确实指望他。
>
> ②hold...on 意为“稳住”，比如：I told him how we had fought to hold on to the company 
>
> 我给他讲了我们是如何极力争取保住公司的。

Nick looked down into the pool from the bridge. It was a hot day.

A kingfisher flew up the stream.

> ==upstream英 [ˌʌpˈstri:m] 美 [ˈʌpˈstrim] adv. 向上游；逆流地 adj. 上游的；逆流的==

It was a long time since Nick had looked into a stream and seen trout.

They were very satisfactory.

As the shadow of the kingfisher moved up the stream, a big trout shot upstream in a long angle, only his shadow marking the angle,

then lost his shadow as he came through the surface of the water, caught the sun, and then, as he went back into the stream under thesurface,

his shadow seemed to float down the stream with the current, unresisting, to his post under the bridge where he tightened facing upinto the current.

> <font color=red>As the shadow of the kingfisher moved up the stream, a big trout shot upstream in a long angle, only his shadow marking the angle, then lost his shadow as he came through the surface of the water, caught the sun, and then, as he went back into the stream under the surface, his shadow seemed to float down the stream with the current, unresisting, to his post under the bridge where he tightened facing up into the current.</font>
>
> 随着那翠鸟在水面上的影子朝上游掠去，一条大鳟鱼朝上游窜去，构成一道长长的弧线，不过仅仅是它在水中的身影勾勒出了这道弧线，跟着它跃出水面，被阳光照着，这就失去了身影，跟着，它穿过水面回到水里，它的身影仿佛随着水流一路飘去，毫无阻碍地直漂到它在桥底下常待的地方，在那里绷紧着身子，脸冲着流水。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①shot upstream in a long angle 朝上游窜去，构成一道长长的弧线，这里shoot作动词，表示”窜，冲”的意思（to move suddenly or quickly in one direction; to make sb/sth move in this way），比如：Flames were shooting up through the roof.
>
> 火不断从房顶蹿上来。
>
> ②upstream 作副词，表示“向上游”（along a river, in the opposite direction to the way in which the water flows）比如：The water rose high enough for them to continue upstream.
>
> 水位涨得够高了，他们可以继续向上游航行。
>
> ③catch the sun 意为“被阳光照着”，比如：White-tailed deer in these Wisconsin woods search out a south-facing slope to catch the morning sun. 
>
> 威斯康星州森林里的白尾鹿找寻一面朝南的斜坡来以便上午去晒太阳。

Nick’s heart tightened as the trout moved. He felt all the old feeling.

He turned and looked down the stream.

It stretched away, pebbly-bottomed with shallows and big boulders and a deep pool as it curved away around the foot of a bluff.

> <font color=red>It stretched away, pebbly-bottomed with shallows and big boulders and a deep pool as it curved away around the foot of a bluff.</font>
>
> 河流一路伸展开去，卵石打底，有些浅滩和大片石，在它流到一处峭壁脚下拐弯的地方，有个深水潭。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①stretch away 表示“向远处伸展”，比如：The desert stretched away into the distance. 
>
> 沙漠一直延伸到远方；
>
> ②curved away around the foot of a bluff 流到一处峭壁脚下拐弯的地方，curve原义是“呈曲线变化”，这里curve away 是“拐弯”的意思，比如：The smiley-shaped bow shocks curve away from the stellar winds of the central massive stars. 
>
> 笑口状的弓形激波因躲开来自中心巨型恒星的星风而发生弯曲。

Nick walked back up the ties to where his pack lay in the cinders beside the railway track. He was happy.

He adjusted the pack harness around the bundle, pulling straps tight, slung the pack on his back, got his arms through the shoulder straps and took some of the pull off his shoulders by leaning his forehead against the wide band of the tump-line.

Still, it was too heavy. It was much too heavy.

He had his leather rod-case in his hand and leaning forward to keep the weight of the pack high on his shoulders he walked along the road that paralleled the railway track, leaving the burned town behind in the heat,

and then turned off around a hill with a high, fire-scarred hill on either side onto a road that went back into the country.

He walked along the road feeling the ache from the pull of the heavy pack.

The road climbed steadily. It was hard work walking up-hill.

His muscles ached and the day was hot, but Nick felt happy.

He felt he had left everything behind, the need for thinking, the need to write, other needs. It was all back of him.

From the time he had gotten down off the train and the baggage man had thrown his pack out of the open car door things had been different.

Seney was burned, the country was burned over and changed, but it did not matter.

It could not all be burned. He knew that.

He hiked along the road, sweating in the sun, climbing to cross the range of hills that separated the railway from the pine plains.

The road ran on, dipping occasionally, but always climbing.

> <font color=red>The road ran on, dipping occasionally, but always climbing.</font>
>
> 大路一直往前，偶尔有段下坡路，但始终是在向高处攀登。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> dipping occasionally 偶尔有段下坡路，dip作动词在这里是“下坡”的意思（ If an area of land, a road, or a path dips, it goes down quite suddenly to a lower level. ），比如：The road dipped and rose again as it neared the top of Parker Mountain.
>
> 快到帕克山山顶的时候，山路突降，继而又突升。

Nick went on up. Finally the road after going parallel to the burnt hillside reached the top.

Nick leaned back against a stump and slipped out of the pack harness.

> ==stump英 [stʌmp] 美 [stʌmp] n. 树桩；残肢；残余部分；柱 vt. 难住；出局；在…作巡回演说 vi. 重重地走；作巡回政治演说==
>
> n. 树桩 (the bottom part of a tree left in the ground after the rest has fallen or been cut down)
>
> 原文：Nick leaned back against a stump and slipped out of the pack harness.
>
> 尼克倒身靠在一截树桩上，从背带圈中溜出身子。
>
> 💧stump作名词时还有“巡回演说”的意思，比如：The presidential candidates are on thestump today.
>
> 总统候选人今天在作巡回演说。

Ahead of him, as far as he could see, was the pine plain.

The burned country stopped off at the left with the range of hills.

On ahead islands of dark pine treesrose out of the plain.

Far off to the left was the line of the river.

Nick followed it with his eye and caught glints of the water in the sun.

There was nothing but the pine plain ahead of him, until the far blue hills that marked the Lake Superior height of land.

He could hardly see them, faint and far away in the heat-light over the plain. If he looked too steadily they were gone.

But if he only half-looked they were there, the far-off hills of the height of land.

> <font color=red>But if he only half-looked they were there,the far-off hills of the height of land.</font>
>
> 可若是随便一望，这抹高地上的远山就明明在那儿。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①half－looked 表示“随便一望”；
>
> ②the far-off hills 远山，far-of是“遥远的”的意思（If you describe something as far off, you mean that it is a long distance from you or from a particular place. ），比如：This iteration of Orion is intended for trips to Mars or far-off asteroids. 
>
> 猎户座的迭代是为了打算远行到火星或遥远的小行星。

Nick sat down against the charred stump and smoked a cigarette.

His pack balanced on the top of the stump, harness holding ready, a hollow molded in it from his back.

Nick sat smoking, looking out over the country. He did not need to get his map out.

He knew where he was from the position of the river.

As he smoked, his legs stretched out in front of him, he noticed a grasshopper walk along the ground and up onto his woolen sock.

The grasshopper was black. As he had walked along the road, climbing, he had started many grasshoppers from the dust.

They were all black. They were not the big grasshoppers with yellow and black or red and black wings whirring out from their black wing sheathing as they fly up.

> ==sheath英 [ʃi:θ] 美 [ʃiθ] n. 套；鞘；护套；紧身连衣裙==

These were just ordinary hoppers, but all a sooty black in color.

Nick had wondered about them as he walked, without really thinking about them.

Now, as he watched the black hopper that was nibbling at the woolof his sock with its fourway lip, he realized that they had all turned black from living in the burned-over land.

He realized that the fire must have come the year before, but the grasshoppers were all black now.

He wondered how long they would stay that way.

Carefully he reached his hand downand took hold of the hopper by the wings.

He turned him up, all his legs walking in the air, and looked at his jointed belly.

Yes, it was black too, iridescent where the back and head were dusty.

“Go on, hopper,” Nick said, speaking out loud for the first time. “Fly away somewhere.”

He tossed the grasshopper up into the air and watched him sail away to a charcoal stump across the road.

Nick stood up. He leaned his back against the weight of his pack where it rested upright on the stumpand got his arms through the shoulder straps.

He stood with the pack on his back on the brow of the hill looking out across the country toward the distant river and then struck down the hillside away from the road.

Underfoot the ground was good walking.

Two hundred yards down the hillside the fire line stopped.

Then it was sweet fern, growing ankle high, to walk through, and clumps of jack pines; a long undulating country with frequent rises and descents, sandy underfoot and the country alive again.

> ==undulating英 ['ʌndjəˌletɪŋ] 美 ['ʌndjəˌletɪŋ] adj. 起伏的==
>
> ==descent英 [dɪˈsent] 美 [dɪˈsɛnt] n. 下降；坡道；堕落；出身，血统==

Nick kept his direction by the sun.

He knew where he wanted to strike the river and he kept on through thepine plain, mounting small rises to see other rises ahead of him

and sometimes from the top of a rise a great solid island of pines off to his right or his left.

He broke off some sprigs of the heathery sweet fern, and put them under his pack straps.

The chafing crushed it and he smelled it as he walked.

He was tired and very hot, walking across the uneven, shadeless pine plain.

At any time he knew he could strikethe river by turning off to his left.

It could not be more than a mile away.

But he kept on toward the north to hit the river as far upstream as he could go in one day’s walking.

For some time as he walked Nick had been in sight of one of the big islands of pine standing out above the rolling high ground he was crossing.

He dipped down and then as he came slowly up to the crest of the bridge he turned and made toward the pine trees.

There was no underbrush in the island of pine trees.

The trunks of the trees went straightup or slanted toward each other.

The trunks were straight and brown without branches.

The branches were high above. Some interlocked to make a solid shadow on the brown forest floor.

Around the grove of trees was a bare space. It was brown and soft underfoot as Nick walked on it.

This was the over-lapping of the pine needle floor, extending out beyond the width of the high branches.

The trees had grown tall and the branches moved high, leaving in thesun this bare space they had once covered with shadow.

Sharp at the edge of this extension of the forest floor commenced the sweet fern.

Nick slipped off his pack and lay down in the shade.

He lay on his back and looked up into the pine trees.

His neck and back and the small of his back rested as he stretched.

The earth felt good against his back. He looked up at the sky, through the branches, and then shuthis eyes.

He opened them and looked up again. There was a wind high up in the branches.

He shut his eyes again and went to sleep.

### 背景知识

**💧****The Wilderness Therapy**

**荒野疗法**

我们今天的内容中Nick在参加大战后，身心受到损伤，回到密执安州北部少年时代常去的钓鱼之地。后来在海明威的回忆录（memoir）《不固定的圣节》（*A Moveable Feast*）中“饥饿是有益的磨练”一节中写道：“该故事写的是战后还乡的事，但全篇中没有一字提到战争。”



Nick回到家乡想要缓解自己的战争创伤，然而家乡已是一片荒野（There was no town, nothing but the rails and the burned-over coun-try. The thirteen saloons that had lined the one street of Seney had not left a trace...It was all that was left of the town of Seney. Even the surface had been burned off the ground.）。在心理学当中，有一种治疗法就是荒野疗法，我们今天一起来了解一下吧～



美国人所说的荒野是指“没有为人类驯服,人类只是访客并不会常驻的地区”，它可能是森林，也可能是草原、湿地或是荒漠。荒野是美国文化的重要组成部分，在美国人心中，荒野意味着自由，也暗含着冒险。



荒野疗法是一种通过在远足途中传授生活经验和社交技巧来帮助内心有困扰的年轻人的方法，主要针对情感和行为问题，最短需要1周，最长不超过3个月，每次参与者不少于10人。



荒野环境通常比较恶劣，这使得每位参与者会选择优选处理好自己问题，同时意识到团队合作的重要性。与拓展训练类似，荒野疗愈目标之一是树立参与者的信心，拓展身体和心理极限，帮助参与者掌握生存技巧和建立防御机制。



此外，荒野区别于熟悉的城市环境，所以能轻易帮助参与者从不愉快的过往中解放出来。最单纯原始的荒野环境，也会是人类内心最依赖的环境，荒野疗法师会运用冒险和恐惧的力量，唤醒参与者与自然之间最原始的链接。



还有，简单地徒步穿越荒野，这使得大脑思维也变得简单，再加上荒野疗法师擅长运用自然隐喻，有效促进参与者内省，所以荒野疗愈会是一种行之有效的心理干预方法。



作为神经科临床治疗方法，医院患者是荒野治疗的主要受众，适应症包括药物滥用、青少年暴力和抑郁问题等等。不只是精神疾病，针对摄食障碍、身体残障和癌症等身体疾病，荒野疗愈也有很多成功案例。



作为教育方法，美国学校通过荒野疗愈来传授自然知识，提高学生风险控制能力和领导能力。对于网络成瘾和青少年犯罪等问题，荒野治疗通常是传统监禁的有效补充。除了治疗和教育之外，更多荒野治疗形态是与团队拓展训练结合在一起，帮助个人成长。



史蒂夫·卡迪萨诺（Steve Cartisano）因颇具争议的荒野治疗项目而出名，他创立了“挑战者基金会”（Challenger Foundation）和美国、南美地区其他一些项目。有一次卡迪萨诺被指控因疏忽而杀人，因为在他监管下的两个少年死于远程旅行。虽然荒野疗法可以达到预期效果，但是运用不道德的方法，有时甚至是残忍的方法来帮助苦苦挣扎的年轻人，这遭到了强烈指责。

### 课文理解

《大双心河》（*Big Two-Hearted River*）的背景是Nick从一战的欧洲战场返回，他故地重游，想要以此治疗战争留给自己的创伤。今天的内容里，就有多处环境描写暗示了战争带来的摧毁性结果——

💧**Clue 1**: The implication of war influences.



**Evidence 1**: The train went on up the track out of sight, around one of the hills of burnt timber...There was no town, nothing but the rails and the burned-over coun-try... The thirteen saloons that had lined the one street of Seney had not left a trace.

火车沿着轨道向前行驶，绕过一座满是烧焦树木的小山，就不见了踪影…没有村镇，什么也没有，只有铁轨和被火烧过的土地。赛妠镇唯一的一条街道边上曾经有过十三家酒馆，现在都已经荡然无存。



**Evidence 2**: The stone was chipped and split by the fire. It was all that was left of the town of Seney. Even the surface had been burned off the ground.

基石被火烧碎，开裂了。塞纳镇就剩下这些了。连土地的表层也被烧毁了。



小说一开篇，作者就描绘了村镇在战争侵袭后一片凋零的模样。不仅如此，还有对自然环境所遭受的破坏的描写，比如土地的表层也被“烧毁”了。burnt, burned-over以及had been burned off的重复出现和强调，也增添了整个环境氛围的压抑和沉重感。



Nick之所以回到这个地方，我们可以从下文的描述里看出，他其实是想重新疗愈自己所受的创伤。比如有一个细节提到他其实还是会不时地被某些景象触动而联系到自己的遭遇——



💧**Clue 2**: Nick is trying to restore his inner peace.



**Evidence 1**: ...as he went back into the stream under the surface, his shadow seemed to float down the stream with the current, unresisting, to his post under the bridge where he tightened facing up into the current.

Nick’s heart tightened as the trout moved. He felt all the old feeling.

它穿过水面回到水里，它的身影仿佛随着水流一路飘去，毫无阻碍地直漂到它在桥底下常待的地方，在那里绷紧着身子，脸冲着流水。

看着鳟鱼的动作，尼克的心抽紧了。旧时的感受全部涌上心头。



**Evidence 2**: It was hard work walking up-hill. His muscles ached and the day was hot, but Nick felt happy. He felt he had left everything behind, the need for thinking, the need to write, other needs. It was all back of him.

登山真是一件难事。尼克肌肉发痛，天气又热，但他感到很开心。他感到已把一切都抛在脑后了，不需要思索，不需要写作，不需要做其他事情。一切都被抛在脑后了。



为什么说看到鳟鱼Nick就联想到了自己的遭遇呢？上文里描写了鳟鱼在激流中努力稳住身子来抵抗流水的冲刷（big trout looking to hold themselves on the gravel bottom in a varying mist of gravel and sand, raised in spurts by the current），这里象征着像Nick这样的退伍士兵其实也无时不刻不在抵抗战争带来的“痛苦”的激流，避免让自己的精神世界扭曲变形。这种挣扎和努力他十分有同感。



接着他开始登山。这是一个体力活，他虽然感觉吃力，但心情十分愉悦。这里“向上”的动作也在暗示着他在努力挣脱现在所处的情感黑洞，而向积极的方向努力。走累了之后他卸下背包在树荫底下休息（Nick slipped off his pack and lay down in the shade.）最后他就这么睡着了（He shut his eyes again and went to sleep.）

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****How to Determine the Direction When We Get Lost in the Wild**

**在野外迷路时如何确定方向？**



我们今天的内容中有这样的场景，在荒野里Nick凭借太阳确定自己的方向（Nick kept his direction by the sun.）。现在野外生存越来越受都市人群的欢迎，喧嚣的闹市根本感受不到大自然的安宁，而旅游观光又弥补不了人们内心的空虚，所以就用工作之余难得的假期走入大自然去挑战自我，但是有挑战就有困难和危险，走入荒野一片茫然，没有人烟、没有道路，极易迷失方向陷入进退两难的困境，所以这个时候会用科学的方法辨别方向至关重要，下面就来讲讲在野外如何辨别方向吧～



\1. 利用指南针（ compass）判断方向

这是最方便的方法。磁针的北极指向地理的北极。



\2. 利用太阳判断方向

我国大部分地区在北回归线以北，正午太阳位于天顶偏向南方，对着太阳，前面是南，背面是北，左面是东，右面是西。太阳东升西落，早晨起来，面向太阳，前面是东，后面是西，左面是北，右面是南；傍晚对着太阳，前面是西，背后是东，左面是南，右面是北。如果是南半球太阳会是在朝北的方向东升西落。



\3. 利用手表判断方向

必须是指针式的手表。把当前的时间除以2,把所得的商数对准太阳.表盘上12所对的方向就是北方。如果是上午10点，把手表刻度盘上的“5”对准太阳，下午2点（14点）则把手表刻度盘上的“7”对准太阳，这时，手表刻度盘上的“12”指的就是北方。  



\4. 利用北极星（ Polaris ）判断方向

如果是晴朗的夜空可以观看北极星，北极星永远在地球的正北方。如果不知道哪颗星是北极星，可以先找到酷似勺子形状的北斗七星，在勺子最外沿的那颗星延伸五个星位对应的那颗亮星就是北极星。



\5. 利用木棍判断方向

在太阳的底下立一根木棍，把影子的末端摆一个记号，十五分钟后影子会移动，在移动后的末端再摆一个记号，连接两个记号形成一条线，这条线就是东西方向。



\5. 利用树木判断方向

通常情况下，北半球树木南面受到阳光照射的时间较长，枝叶长得茂密些；北面受到阳光照射较少，枝叶稀少些。树木的南面阳光照射比较充足，木质生长较快，形成的年轮宽些。因而，年轮较稀的一边是南方，年轮较紧密的一边是北方。 



\6. 利用积雪判断方向

丘陵上的积雪，南坡比北坡融化得快些。沟里的积雪，朝南的一面比朝北的一面融化得快些。　



\7. 利用青苔判断方向

青苔喜欢阴暗潮湿的环境。石头上的青苔往往生长在北面。　

## Chapter 9.2

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/e0f00a0d6ac01c574ead6c34e6de24ab-sz_1246735.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

Big Two-Hearted River

Nick woke stiff and cramped. The sun was nearly down.

> ==cramped英 [kræmpt] 美 [kræmpt] adj. 狭促的；拥挤的；密密麻麻的==
>
> adj. 麻痹的（sudden strong pain caused by a muscle suddenly contracting. You sometimes get cramps in a muscle after you have been making a physical effort over a long period of time. ）
>
> 原文：Nick woke stiff and cramped.
>
> 尼克醒过来，觉得身子僵硬、麻痹。
>
> 💧cramped作形容词，还有“拥挤的”意思，比如：
>
> There are hundreds of families living incramped conditions on the floor of the airport lounge.
>
> 数百个家庭住在机场候机室拥挤的地板上。

His pack was heavy and the straps painful as he lifted it on.

> <font color=red>His pack was heavy and the straps painful as he lifted it on.</font>
>
> 他的包裹很沉，背在背上，带子勒得很痛。
>
> **💧句式拆解**
>
> the straps painful 省略了谓语动词，应为the straps were painful；
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> the straps painful 带子勒得很痛，这里的形容词painful并不是真正用来修饰straps的，而是straps勒得Nick很痛，是来形容he的，这里用到了transferred epithet（移就）这个修辞手法，也就是把本来应该用来修饰甲事物性质或状态的词用来修饰乙事物，转了个弯来表示甲事物给人的感觉，常见的是把用来修饰人的词用来修饰物。比如：I spent sleepless nights on my project.
>
> 我在项目上度过了无眠之夜。

He leaned over with the pack on and picked up the leather rod-case and started out from the pine trees across the sweet fern swale, toward the river.

> <font color=red>He leaned over with the pack on and picked up the leather rod-case and started out from the pine trees across the sweet fern swale, toward the river.</font>
>
> 他背着包裹弯下身子，拎起皮钓竿袋，从松林出发，跨过香蕨木洼地，朝河走去。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> lean over 表示“弯下身子”，比如：Then he would lean over and give me a big kiss on the cheek and tell me to be a good boy. 
>
> 接着他会倾下身来在我的脸颊上给我一个大大的吻，并告诉我做一个好孩子。

He knew it could not be more than a mile.

He came down a hillside covered with stumps into a meadow.

At the edge of the meadow flowed the river.

Nick was glad to get to the river. He walked upstream through the meadow.

His trousers were soaked with the dew as he walked.

> <font color=red>His trousers were soaked with the dew as he walked.</font>
>
> 他走着走着，裤腿被露水弄得湿透了。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> were soaked with the dew 被露水弄得湿透了，be soaked with 表示“被...浸湿”（to make sb/sth completely wet），比如：Our clothes were soaked with sweat. 
>
> 我们的衣服给汗水湿透了。

After the hot day, the dew had come quickly and heavily.

The river made no sound. It was too fast and smooth.

At the edge of the meadow, before he mounted to a piece of high ground to make camp, Nick looked down the river at the trout rising.

They were rising to insects come from the swamp on the other side of the stream when the sun went down.

The trout jumped out of water to take them.

While Nick walked through the little stretch of meadow alongside the stream, trout had jumped high out of water.

> <font color=red>While Nick walked through the little stretch of meadow alongside the stream, trout had jumped high out of water.</font>
>
> 尼克穿过河边这一小段草场时，鳟鱼就在高高地跃出水面了。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> the little stretch of meadow 这一小段草场，stretch在这里是“一段”的意思（A stretch of road, water, or land is a length or area of it.）。比如：It's a very dangerous stretch of road.
>
> 这是一段非常危险的路。

Now as he looked down the river, the insects must be settling on the surface, for the trout were feeding steadily all down the stream.

As far down the long stretch as he could see, the trout were rising, making circles all down the surface of the water, as though it were starting to rain.

The ground rose, wooded and sandy, to overlook the meadow, the stretch of river and the swamp.

Nick dropped his pack and rod-caseand looked for a level piece of ground.

He was very hungry and he wanted to make his camp before he cooked.

Between two jack pines, the ground was quite level.

> <font color=red>Between two jack pines, the ground was quite level.</font>
>
> 在两棵短叶松之间，土地很平坦。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> quite level 十分平坦，这里level做形容词，表示“平坦的”（When something is level, it is completely flat with no part higher than any other. ）比如：The floor was level, but the ceiling sloped toward his head.
>
> 地面平平坦坦，但是天花板向他的头部倾斜。
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> jack pine 短叶松，是北美东部的一种松树，它也被称为灰松（grey pine）和威忌州松（scrub pine）.

He took the ax out of the pack and chopped out two projecting roots.

> ==projecting英 [prə'dʒektɪŋ] 美 [prə'dʒektɪŋ] adj. 伸出的==
>
> adj. 突出的（extending out above or beyond a surface or boundary）
>
> 原文：He took the ax out of the pack and chopped out two projecting roots.
>
> 他从包裹里拿出斧子，砍掉两个撅出的根条。
>
> 💧project作动词时有“突出”的意思，比如：a narrow ledge that projected out from the bank of the river.
>
> 河岸边突出来的一块狭长的岩脊

That leveled a piece of ground large enough to sleep on.

He smoothed out the sandy soil with his hand and pulled all the sweet fern bushes by their roots.

> <font color=red>He smoothed out the sandy soil with his hand and pulled all the sweet fern bushes by their roots.</font>
>
> 他伸手抹平沙地，把所有的香蕨木连根拔掉。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①smoothed out the sandy soil 抹平沙地，smooth out 在这里是“抹平”的意思，比如：He smoothed out the paper and then began to write on it.
>
> 他先把纸抹平，然后开始在上面写字。
>
> smooth out 还有“解决”（If you smooth out a problem or difficulty, you solve it, especially by talking to the people concerned.）的意思，比如：Baker was smoothing out differences with European allies.
>
> 贝克尔正在解决与欧洲盟友的分歧。
>
> ②pulled all the sweet fern bushes by their roots. 把所有的香蕨木连根拔掉，by their roots表示“连根拔起”，比如：Buildings had their roofs blown off, and trees were ripped out by their roots. 
>
> 建筑物的屋顶被掀翻，树木也被连根拔起。

His hands smelled good from the sweet fern. He smoothed the uprooted earth.

He did not want anything making lumps under the blankets.

When he had the ground smooth, he spread his three blankets.

One he folded double, next to the ground. The other two he spread ontop.

With the ax he slit off a bright slab of pine from one of the stumps and split it into pegs for the tent.

He wanted them long and solid to hold in the ground.

With the tent unpacked and spread on the ground, the pack, leaning against a jackpine, looked much smaller.

Nick tied the rope that served the tent for a ridge-pole to the trunk of one of the pine trees and pulled thetent up off the ground with the other end of the rope and tied it to the other pine.

The tent hung on the rope like a canvas blanket on a clothesline.

Nick poked a pole he had cut up under the back peak of the canvas and then made it a tent by pegging out the sides.

He pegged the sides out taut and drove the pegs deep, hitting them down into the ground with the flat ofthe ax until the rope loops were buried and the canvas was drum tight.

> <font color=red>He pegged the sides out taut and drove the pegs deep, hitting them down into the ground with the flat of the ax until the rope loops were buried and the canvas was drum tight.</font>
>
> 他用木钉把四边绷得紧紧的，用斧子平坦的一面把它们深深地敲进地面，直到绳圈被埋进泥里，帆布帐篷绷得象铜鼓一般紧。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①pegged the sides out 用木钉把四边绷住，peg out 指的是“用木桩在地上标出界限”，比如：To peg out a mining claim of yourself.
>
> 用界桩标出属于自己的采矿地段。
>
> taut 在这里作形容词，表示“拉紧的”，用来修饰the sides.
>
> peg out 还可以表示“累倒”（If someone pegs out, they are too exhausted to carry on with what they have been doing.），比如：I nipped round the corner for a quick beer and nearly pegged out on the spot.
>
> 我匆匆转过街角去痛快地喝杯啤酒，差点儿当场累趴下。
>
> ②drove the pegs deep 把它们深深地敲，这里用pep的名词形式，表示“销钉”，比如：He builds furniture using wooden pegs instead of nails.
>
> 他用木钉而不是铁钉制作家具。
>
> ③drum tight 像鼓一样紧，在这里相当于（as）tight as a drum，是一个习语。比如：They rushed the child to hospital when his abdomen became tight as a drum due to the swelling.
>
> 当孩子的腹部因为肿胀变得像鼓一样紧时，他们赶紧把他送到医院。
>
> （as）tight as a drum 还有“密不透风、滴水不漏”的意思，比如：The suit is tight as a drum to keep inclement weather conditions out, but the lack of ventilation turns it into something of a sauna while you wear it.
>
> 这套西装紧得像个鼓，可以抵御恶劣的天气条件，但由于缺乏通风，穿上它就像在蒸桑拿。

Across the open mouth of the tent Nick fixed cheesecloth to keep out mosquitoes.

He crawled inside under the mosquito bar with various things from the pack to put at the head of the bed under the slant of the canvas.

Inside the tent the light came through the brown canvas.

It smelled pleasantly of canvas. Already there was something mysterious and homelike.

Nick was happy as he crawled inside the tent. He had not been unhappy all day.

This was different though. Now things were done.

There had been this to do. Now it was done. It had been a hard trip.

He was very tired. That was done. He had made his camp.

He was settled. Nothing could touchhim. It was a good place to camp.

He was there, in the good place. Hewas in his home where he had made it. Now he was hungry.

He came out, crawling under the cheesecloth. It was quite dark outside. It was lighter in the tent.

Nick went over to the pack and found, with his fingers, a long nail ina paper sack of nails, in the bottom of the pack.

He drove it into the pine tree, holding it close and hitting it gently with the flat of the ax.

He hung the pack up on the nail. Allhis supplies were in the pack.

They were off the ground and sheltered now.

Nick was hungry. He did not believe he had ever been hungrier.

He opened and emptied a can of pork and beans and a can of spaghetti into the frying pan.

> ==spaghetti英 [spəˈgeti] 美 [spəˈɡɛti] n. 意大利粉，意大利面条==

"I've got a right to eat this kind of stuff, if I'm willing to carry it," Nick said.

His voice sounded strange in the darkening woods. He did not speak again.

He started a fire with some chunks of pine he got with the ax from a stump.

> <font color=red>He started a fire with some chunks of pine he got with the ax from a stump.</font>
>
> 他用斧子从一个树桩上砍下几大片松木，生了一堆火。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> start a fire 表示“生火”，比如：Dry twigs are good to start a fire with. 
>
> 干燥的细树枝用来生火很好。

Over the fire he stuck a wire grill, pushing the four legs down into the ground with his boot.

Nick put the frying pan on the grill over the flames.

He was hungrier. The beans and spaghetti warmed.

Nick stirred them and mixed them together.

They began to bubble, making little bubbles that rose with difficulty to the surface.

There was a good smell. Nick got out a bottle of tomato catchup and cut four slices of bread.

> ==catchup英 ['kætʃəp] 美 ['kætʃəp] n. 调味酱（如蕃茄酱之类）==

The little bubbles were coming faster now.

Nick sat down beside the fire and lifted the frying pan off.

He poured about half the contents out into the tin plate.

It spread slowly on the plate. Nick knew it was too hot.

He poured on some tomato catchup. He knew the beans and spaghetti were still too hot.

He looked at the fire, then at the tent, he was not going to spoil it all by burning his tongue.

For years he had never enjoyed fried bananas because he had never been able to wait for them to cool.

His tongue was very sensitive. He was very hungry.

Across the river in the swamp, in the almost dark, he saw a mist rising. He looked at the tent once more.

All right. He took a full spoonful from the plate.

"Chrise," Nick said, "Geezus Chrise," he said happily.

He ate the whole plateful before he remembered the bread.

Nick finished the second plateful with the bread, mopping the plate shiny.

He had not eaten since a cup of coffee and a ham sandwich in the station restaurant at St. Ignace.

It had been a very fine experience. He had been that hungry before, but had not been able to satisfy it.

He could have made camp hours before if he had wanted to.

There were plenty of good places tocamp on the river. But this was good.

Nick tucked two big chips of pine under the grill.

The fire flared up. He had forgotten to get water for the coffee.

Out of the pack he got a folding canvas bucket and walked down thehill, across the edge of the meadow,to the stream.

The other bank was in the white mist.

The grass was wet and cold as he knelt on the bank and dipped the canvas bucket into the stream.

It bellied and pulled hard in the current. The water was ice cold.

Nick rinsed the bucket and carried itfull up to the camp.

Up away from the stream it was not so cold.

Nick drove another big nail and hung up the bucket full of water.

He dipped the coffee pot half full, put some more chips under the grill onto the fire and put the pot on.

He could not remember which way he made coffee.

He could remember an argument about it with Hopkins, but not which side he had taken.

He decided to bring it to a boil. He remembered now that was Hopkins’s way.

He had once argued about everything with Hopkins.

While he waited for the coffee to boil, he opened a small can of apricots. He liked to open cans.

He emptied the can of apricots out into a tin cup.

> ==apricot英 [ˈeɪprɪkɒt] 美 [ˈæprɪkɑ:t] n.&adj. 杏子；杏色(的)==

While he watched the coffee on the fire, he drank the juice syrup of the apricots, carefully at first to keep from spilling, then meditatively, sucking the apricots down.

> ==meditatively英 ['medɪtətɪvlɪ] 美 ['medəˌteɪtɪvlɪ] adv. 冥想地==

They were better than fresh apricots. The coffee boiled as he watched.

The lid came up and coffee and grounds ran down the side of the pot.

Nick took it off the grill. It was a triumph for Hopkins.

He put sugar in the empty apricot cup and poured some of the coffee out to cool.

It was too hot to pour and he used his hat to hold the handle of the coffee pot.

He would not let it steep in the pot at all. Not the first cup.

It should be straight Hopkins all the way. Hop deserved that.

He was a very serious coffee drinker. He was the most serious man Nick had ever known.

Not heavy, serious. That was a longtime ago. Hopkins spoke without moving his lips.

He had played polo. He made millions of dollars in Texas.

He had borrowed carfare to go to Chicago, when the wire came that his first big well had come in.

He could have wired for money. That would have been too slow.

They called Hop’s girl the Blonde Venus. Hop did not mind because she was not his real girl.

Hopkins said very confidently that none of them would make fun of hisreal girl.

He was right. Hopkins went away when the telegram came.

### 背景知识

**💧****Playing Polo**

**打马球**

我们今天的内容中Nick回想起Hopkins打马球的事情。（ He had played polo. ）我们今天一起来了解一下马球这项运动吧～

马球运动（Polo）指的是骑在马上，用马球杆击球入门的一种体育活动。马球在中国古代叫“击鞠”，发明始于汉代，兴盛于唐宋，在后来的几个世纪内流传到西方。它的名字则来自于印度，在印度当地，人们玩耍一种藏语中名叫pulu的木球。



后来，作为印度占领者的英国人将这个运动带回了大不列颠。很快，马球在英国军队中流行开来。Cachar地区首府Silchar成为现代马球的发源地。成立于1859年的Sichar俱乐部也成为世界上最古老的马球俱乐部。



1876年，詹姆斯·戈登·本纳特将马球传入美国。1878年举办了首届马球（军）团内锦标赛，这项运动迅速蔓延到世界其它国家和地区，特别是英联邦各国以及阿根廷。20世纪二三十年代是美国马球的“黄金时代”，出现了汤米·希区柯克、塞西尔·史密斯等著名选手。美国的马球运动主要在俱乐部进行。



马球曾在1908、1920、1924、1936年作为奥运会正式比赛项目 。英 、美、阿根廷、印度、中东等国今仍喜爱这项运动。



马球比赛两队对抗，每队4人，1号和2号为前锋，3号、4 号为后卫。运动员头戴马球帽，腿着皮制护膝，脚蹬棕色皮靴，身穿白色马裤和本队颜色的上衣。比赛以中线争球开始，运动员用球槌击球，每个人在场上不受位置限制。比赛过半或每攻进一球 （点球除外 ）双方交换场地。球进入两球门柱之间即得一分。



一场比赛为8小节，每节7分钟。节间休息 3分钟，半场间休息5分钟。马球场地长275米，宽 183米。马的身材和年龄不限 ，但需具备良好的速度、耐力和灵活性，特别是脾气温顺，否则易在激烈对抗中受惊、失控而引发事故。



马球运动有着一个古老而有趣的特别程序——作为一名观众，你有一项义务：踏草皮！当比赛第三巡结束的中场哨声吹响之后，坐在球场四周的球迷们便纷纷走上球场寻找那些翻起的草皮，尽情用力地踏实草皮，以使整个球场恢复平整。此刻，球场上一扫比赛紧张、激烈的气氛，取而代之的是球场上人们踏草皮的欢声笑语。



Polo衫原本称做网球衫（tennis shirt），原本是贵族打马球的时候所穿的服装，可能是因为舒适，他们喜欢穿着有领子的短袖衣服。久而久之就被人们称作是polo衫（polo shirt），后来广为大众喜爱，所以演变成一般的休闲服装。

### 课文理解

Nick醒来后，背起背包和钓竿袋开始向河边出发（He leaned over with the pack on and picked up the leather rod-case and started out from the pine trees across the sweet fern swale, toward the river.）他找了一片平地先搭起帐篷再做吃的东西。这一段是非常简单日常的描写，但从字里行间我们可以感受到Nick对这种安逸和简单的满足喜悦——

💧**Clue 1**: Nick is happy with the simple life there.



**Evidence 1**: Inside the tent the light came through the brown canvas. It smelled pleasantly of canvas. Already there was something mysterious and homelike. Nick was happy as he crawled inside the tent.

日光透过棕色帆布渗进帐篷。帆布气味很好闻，有一种神秘的气氛和家的样子。尼克爬进帐篷时，心里很开心。



**Evidence 2**: It was a good place to camp. He was there, in the good place. He was in his home where he had made it.

这是个扎营的好地方。他就在这儿，在这个好地方。他正在自己亲手建起的家里。



**Evidence 3**: He could have made camp hours before if he had wanted to. There were plenty of good places to camp on the river. But this was good.

他原本在几小时以前就可以扎营的，但是他不想那样做。这河边有的是宿营的好地点。这样就很好。



在这种简单的惬意中，作者用来描述Nick感受的词语也非常的简单但有力——good. 自己搭帐篷是好的，煮豆子和面条吃也是好的，这一切都让Nick十分满足。接着他开始准备自己煮咖啡。在这个过程中，他想起了自己的一位旧友，一个叫作Hopkins的人。他们曾经就如何煮咖啡发生过争执，但现在，他竟不自觉地开始按照Hopkins的方法煮咖啡了——



💧**Clue 2**: Nick reminisces about his old friend.



**Evidence 1**: He could remember an argument about it with Hopkins, but not which side he had taken. He decided to bring it to a boil. He remembered now that was Hopkins’s way.

他只记得曾为这事跟霍普金斯争论过，但是记不得自己赞成用哪种方法了。他决定让咖啡煮沸。他现在想起来了，这正是霍普金斯的方法。



**Evidence 2**: It should be straight Hopkins all the way. Hop deserved that. He was a very serious coffee drinker. He was the most serious man Nick had ever known.

就应该把霍普金斯的办法用到底。霍普金斯应该得到这样的待遇。他是个非常认真的喝咖啡的人。这是尼克所认识的最认真的人。



Nick通过这种方式来怀念过去的好友。从现在的情况推测，他们已经失联很久。在这之前的某一天，Hopkins突然收到电报说他的一口油井出油了（the wire came that his first big well had come in），也就是Hopkins成了一个暴发户。这里对Hopkins的描述也可以看作是作者对于与自然对立的金钱和物质主义的一个暗示。

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****Many Sauces**

**各种调味酱汁**

我们今天的内容当中有这样的情节：Nick拿出一瓶番茄酱，切了四片面包。（ Nick got out a bottle of tomato catchup and cut four slices of bread. ）接着他将番茄酱倒在食物上（ He poured on some tomato catchup. ），这里的 tomato catchup是指番茄酱，catchup同ketchup，我们今天就来一起看一下都有哪些调味酱汁吧～



\1. Ketchup 番茄蘸酱

Ketchup是番茄蘸酱，用来冷食，比如蘸薯条吃。其实除了食用的冷热这点不同外，ketchup和tomato sauce制作材料也不同。Ketchup配料中一般包括洋葱、玉米和醋。有些配料大家应该都没吃出来吧？美国人很喜欢用品牌来给东西命名，Ketchup是一个很有名的番茄酱牌子，于是大家都叫番茄酱叫ketchup了。



\2. Tomato Sauce 番茄酱

中文里同样被叫做番茄酱，但请大家不要把它和ketchup搞混，否则Tomato sauce可是要伤心的。因为人家它血统纯正，是法式经典菜肴5大基本酱汁之一。Tomato sauce其实是做热菜的酱汁，除了番茄，一般会有油、香草、蔬菜和肉糜，做意大利面的时候用上它，绝对棒！



\3. Mayonnaise 蛋黄酱

它就是大家经常吃的蛋黄酱，可以做沙拉调料（dressing），很百搭哦。蛋黄酱的主要成分是至少70%总重的植物油和蛋黄，配料是芥末酱（mustard）和柠檬汁，其实白醋也很好，当然盐和胡椒不能少。 



\4. Ranch 农场酱

Ranch一般翻译为农场酱，可以搭配新鲜蔬菜，它有着浓郁的洋葱和大蒜味，比蒜蓉酱（garlic sauce）更具有奶香味，层次也更丰富。它除了可以用来做色拉，也可以蘸薯条、鸡翅、玉米片吃。



\5. Sour Cream 酸奶油

酸奶油在墨西哥菜里运用的很多。它口感比蛋黄酱轻薄，口味略酸。不爱吃酸的人可以把酸奶油配合有芝士的食物一起吃，可以很好地综合掉腻的感觉。推荐吃法：一颗草莓蘸上红糖，再裹上酸奶油，就变成了极为受欢迎的甜品。



\6. Guacamole 鳄梨酱

Guacamole是南美洲阿兹特克文化里的传统酱料，用鳄梨（牛油果）、番茄、洋葱、香菜和辣椒粉（cayenne pepper）等制成，最流行的就是蘸着墨西哥玉米片（tortilla chips）吃，是一大派对美食。也可以加在面包或墨西哥卷饼里吃。词尾“mole”就是酱料的意思，这个词也随着文化而进入了西班牙语中。



\7. Béchamel/White sauce 白酱

Béchamel白酱常以White sauce之名出现在各式西餐中，是意大利面和焗菜必不可缺的酱汁。主要材料是黄油、牛奶和面粉，加上不同的食材就可以变化万千。比如加入Gruyère或Parmesan奶酪，就是芝士酱（mornay sauce）；加上奶油就是奶油酱（cream sauce）；加上蘑菇就是蘑菇酱（mushroom sauce）.



\8. Hummus 鹰嘴豆泥

鹰嘴豆泥既可以作为酱料，又可以作为开胃菜，常见于中东、阿拉伯菜肴。做法很简单，将鹰嘴豆磨成泥，加上芝麻酱、橄榄油和其他香料就完成了。很多阿拉伯人用皮塔饼（Pita）蘸著鹰嘴豆泥吃就是一顿饭了。

## Chapter 9.3

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/5dce27f887d2e83aa4a5ef68bc74bed8-sz_1700927.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmhigh)

Big Two-Hearted River

That was on the Black River. It took eight days for the telegram to reach him.

Hopkins gave away his 22 caliber Colt automatic pistol to Nick.

> <font color=red>Hopkins gave away his 22 caliber Colt automatic pistol to Nick.</font>
>
> 霍普金斯把他的二二口径的柯尔特牌自动手枪送给了尼克。
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> 22 caliber Colt automatic pistol 二二口径的柯尔特牌自动手枪，caliber指“口径”。柯尔特公司是美国第一家研发生产自动手枪的枪械制造商。在1880年代末至1900年代初，自动手枪已在欧洲兴起，但在美国，由于历史传统和西部枪械文化的影响，使得转轮手枪稳占枪械市场，自动手枪难有立足之地，此时柯尔特公司已看到自动手枪但发展趋势和市场前景，与美国著名发明家勃朗宁最早建立合作关系，获得英美制造权。从1900年开始推出了一系列柯尔特专利品牌的自动手枪，使柯尔特公司成为美国自动手枪领军者，从此从未被超越。

He gave his camera to Bill. It was to remember him always by.

They were all going fishing again next summer.

The Hop Head was rich. He would get a yacht and they would all cruise along the north shore of LakeSuperior.

> <font color=red>The Hop Head was rich. He would get a yacht and they would all cruise along the north shore of Lake Superior.</font>
>
> 这个吸毒鬼发了财。他要买一条游艇，大家一起沿着苏必利尔湖的北岸航行。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①hophead为美国俚语，意为“吸毒鬼”（a heroin or opium addict）。原文为Hop Head，作者故意把它分开写成两个字，并把首字母大写，看上去像Hopkins的名字。 
>
> ②cruise along the north shore of Lake Superior 沿着苏必利尔湖的北岸航行，cruise along 沿着......航行，比如：During your trip, you can cruise along the Seine and see the famous sights of Paris.
>
> 旅行期间，你可以乘船沿着塞纳河航行，观赏巴黎的名胜。

He was excited but serious. They said good-bye and all felt bad.

It broke up the trip. They never saw Hopkins again.

That was a long time ago on the Black River.

Nick drank the coffee, the coffee according to Hopkins.

The coffee was bitter. Nick laughed.It made a good ending to the story.

His mind was starting to work. He knew he could choke it because he was tired enough.

He spilled the coffee out of the pot and shook the grounds loose into the fire.

He lit a cigarette and went inside the tent.

He took off his shoes and trousers, sitting on the blankets, rolled the shoes up inside the trousers for a pillow and got in between the blankets.

Out through the front of the tent he watched the glow of the fire, when the night wind blew on it.

It was a quiet night. The swamp was perfectly quiet.

Nick stretched under the blanket comfortably.

A mosquito hummed close to his ear. Nick sat up and lit a match.

The mosquito was on the canvas, over his head. Nick moved the match quickly up to it.

The mosquito made a satisfactory hiss in the flame. The match went out.

Nick lay down again under the blanket. He turned on his side and shut his eyes.

He was sleepy. He felt sleep coming. He curled up under the blanket and went to sleep.

> <font color=red>He curled up under the blanket and went to sleep.</font>
>
> 他在毯子下蜷起身子，就入睡了。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> curl up 表示“蜷缩”（sit or lie in curved position），比如：In colder weather, your cat will curl up into a tight, heat-conserving ball.
>
> 在更冷的天气里，你的猫会蜷缩成紧紧的一团来保暖。

In the morning the sun was up and the tent was starting to get hot.

Nick crawled out under the mosquito netting stretched across the mouth of the tent, to look at the morning.

The grass was wet on his hands as he came out. He held his trousers and his shoes in his hands.

The sun was just up over the hill. There was the meadow, the river and the swamp.

There were birch trees in the green of the swamp on the other side of the river.

The river was clear and smoothly fast in the early morning.

Down about two hundred yards were three logs all the way across the stream.

They made the water smooth and deep above them.

As Nick watched, a mink crossed the river on the logs and went into the swamp.

Nick was excited. He was excited by the early morning and the river.

He was really too hurried to eat breakfast, but he knew he must.

He built a little fire and put on the coffee pot.

> <font color=red>He built a little fire and put on the coffee pot.</font>
>
> 他生了一小堆火，放上咖啡壶。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> build a fire 表示“生火”，比如：On winter nights, when I build a fire in the fireplace, the approaching and receding sound of trains comes down the chimney. 
>
> 在隆冬的夜晚，当我在壁炉里生火的时候，列车声便从烟囱中传入，先是渐行渐近，然后渐行渐远。

While the water was heating in the pot he took an empty bottle and went down over the edge of the high ground to the meadow.

The meadow was wet with dew and Nick wanted to catch grasshoppers for bait before the sun dried the grass.

> ==grasshopper英 [ˈgrɑ:shɒpə(r)] 美 [ˈgræshɑ:pə(r)] n. 蚱蜢；蝗虫==

He found plenty of good grasshoppers. They were at the base of the grass stems.

> ==stem英 [stem] 美 [stɛm] n. 茎；梗；柄；词干 vi. 起源于；来自 vt. 阻止；遏制；控制==
>
> n.  茎（The stem of a plant is the thin, upright part on which the flowers and leaves grow.）
>
> 原文：Sometimes they clung to a grass stem.
>
> 有时候它们依附在草茎上。
>
> 💧stem作动词时有“起源于”的意思，常与from搭配，比如：All my problems stem from drink.
>
> 我所有的问题都源于酗酒。

Sometimes they clung to a grass stem. They were cold and wet with the dew, and could not jump until the sun warmed them.

> <font color=red>Sometimes they clung to a grass stem.</font>
>
> 有时候它们依附在草茎上。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> clung to a grass stem 依附在草茎上，clung是cling的过去式，cling to 表示“依附”（to stick to sth），比如：The smell of smoke still clung to her clothes.
>
> 烟味仍附着在她的衣服上不散。
>
> cling to 还有“坚持”（to be unwilling to get rid of sth, or stop doing sth）的意思，比如：Throughout the trial she had clung to the belief that he was innocent.
>
> 在整个审判中，她都坚持相信他是清白的。

Nick picked them up, taking only the medium-sized brown ones, and put them into the bottle.

He turned over a log and just under the shelter of the edge were several hundred hoppers.

It was a grasshopper lodging house.Nick put about fifty of the medium browns into the bottle.

While he was picking up the hoppers the others warmed in the sun and commenced to hop away.

They flew when they hopped. At first they made one flight and stayed stiff when they landed, as though they were dead.

Nick knew that by the time he was through with breakfast they would be as lively as ever.

Without dew in the grass it would take him all day to catch a bottle full of good grasshoppers and he would have to crush many of them, slamming at them with his hat.

He washed his hands at the stream.He was excited to be near it.

Then he walked up to the tent. The hoppers were already jumping stiffly in the grass.

In the bottle, warmed by the sun, they were jumping in a mass. Nick put in a pine stick as a cork.

It plugged the mouth of the bottle enough, so the hoppers could not get out and left plenty of air passage.

He had rolled the log back and knew he could get grasshoppers there every morning.

Nick laid the bottle full of jumping grasshoppers against a pine trunk.

Rapidly he mixed some buckwheat flour with water and stirred it smooth, one cup of flour, one cup of water.

He put a handful of coffee in the pot and dipped a lump of grease out of a can and slid it sputtering across the hot skillet.

> ==sputter英 [ˈspʌtə(r)] 美 [ˈspʌtɚ] vi. 发出啪啪声，毕剥作响 n. 劈啪声；慌乱的说话方式==

On the smoking skillet he poured smoothly the buckwheat batter.

It spread like lava, the grease spitting sharply.

Around the edges the buckwheat cake began to firm, then brown, then crisp.

The surface was bubbling slowly to porousness. Nick pushed under the browned under surface with a fresh pine chip.

He shook the skillet sideways and the cake was loose on the surface. I won’t try and flop it, he thought.

He slid the chip of clean wood all the way under the cake, and flopped it over onto its face. It sputtered in the pan.

> ==flop英 [flɒp] 美 [flɑ:p] vi. 猛然坐下或躺下；摔落；失败 n. 惨败；失败之作；扑通声==

When it was cooked Nick regreasedthe skillet. He used all the batter.

It made another big flapjack and one smaller one.

Nick ate a big flapjack and a smaller one, covered with apple butter.

He put apple butter on the third cake, folded it over twice, wrapped it in oiled paper and put it in his shirt pocket.

He put the apple butter jar back in the pack and cut bread for two sandwiches.

In the pack he found a big onion. He sliced it in two and peeled the silky outer skin.

Then he cut one half into slices and made onion sandwiches.

He wrapped them in oiled paper and buttoned them in the other pocket of his khaki shirt.

He turned the skillet upside down on the grill, drank the coffee, sweetened and yellow brown with the condensed milk in it, and tidied up the camp. It was a good camp.

> ==condensed英 [kən'denst] 美 [kənˈdɛnst] adj. 精简的；浓缩的==

Nick took his fly rod out of the leather rod-case, jointed it, and shoved the rod-case back into the tent.

He put on the reel and threaded theline through the guides.

He had to hold it from hand to hand, as he threaded it, or it would slip back through its own weight.

It was a heavy, double tapered fly line.

Nick had paid eight dollars for it a long time ago.

It was made heavy to lift back in the air and come forward flat and heavyand straight to make it possible to cast a fly which has no weight.

Nick opened the aluminum leader box.

The leaders were coiled between the damp flannel pads.

Nick had wet the pads at the water cooler on the train up to St. Ignace.

In the damp pads the gut leaders had softened and Nick unrolled one and tied it by a loop at the end to the heavy fly line.

He fastened a hook on the end of the leader.

It was a small hook; very thin and springy.

Nick took it from his hook book, sitting with the rod across his lap.

He tested the knot and the spring ofthe rod by pulling the line taut.

It was a good feeling. He was careful not to let the hook bite into his finger.

He started down to the stream, holding his rod, the bottle of grasshoppers hung from his neck bya thong tied in half hitches around the neck of the bottle.

> ==hitch英 [hɪtʃ] 美 [hɪtʃ] vt.&vi. 搭便车；向上拉；攀爬；套住 n. 小故障；(某种)结==

His landing net hung by a hook from his belt.

Over his shoulder was a long flour sack tied at each corner into an ear.

The cord went over his shoulder. The sack flapped against his legs.

Nick felt awkward and professionally happy with all his equipment hanging from him.

The grasshopper bottle swung against his chest.

In his shirt the breast pockets bulged against him with the lunch and his fly book.

> ==bulge英 [bʌldʒ] 美 [bʌldʒ] vi. 鼓起；凸出；塞满 n. 凸起；鼓起部分；骤增；暴涨==
>
> v. 鼓胀（to stick out from sth in a round shape）
>
> 原文：In his shirt the breast pockets bulgedagainst him with the lunch and his fly book.
>
> 他衬衫口袋里塞满了午餐的吃食和放假蝇的小匣，饱鼓鼓地顶在他身上。
>
> 💧bulge作动词，还有“充满”的意思，比如：They returned home with the car bulging with boxes.
>
> 他们车里满载大包小盒，回到了家。

He stepped into the stream. It was a shock. His trousers clung tight to his legs.

His shoes felt the gravel. The water was a rising cold shock.

Rushing, the current sucked against his legs.

Where he stepped in, the water wasover his knees.

He waded with the current. The gravel slid under his shoes.

He looked down at the swirl of water below each leg and tipped up the bottle to get a grasshopper.

> ==wade英 [weɪd] 美 [wed] vi. 蹚，涉水；费力地阅读==
>
> <font color=red>He waded with the current. The gravel slid under his shoes. He looked down at the swirl of water below each leg and tipped up the bottle to get a grasshopper.</font>
>
> 他顺着流水涉水而行。砂砾在他鞋底擦过。他低头看看在每条腿下打旋的流水，倒转玻璃瓶，打算捉一只蚁蜢。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①waded with the current 涉水而行，wade with 表示“涉水”，还可以用wade across，比如：Rescuers had to wade across a river to reach them...
>
> 救援者必须蹚过一条河才能靠近他们。
>
> wade through 表示“费力阅读”，比如：I spent the whole day wading through the paperwork on my desk.
>
> 我一整天都在伏案处理文件。
>
> ②tipped up the bottle 倒转玻璃瓶，tip up表示“倒转”，比如： She reversed the sheet of paper. Tip the box up and empty it. 
>
> 她把这张纸翻了过来。把那盒子翻过来倒空。

The first grasshopper gave a jump in the neck of the bottle and went out into the water.

> <font color=red>The first grasshopper gave a jump in the neck of the bottle and went out into the water.</font>
>
> 第一只蚁蜢从瓶口一跃，跳到水里。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> give a jump 表示“一跃”；
>
> give sb a jump 表示“使某人吓了一跳”，比如：Good Heavens! You did give me a jump. 
>
> 天哪，你真吓了我一跳。

He was sucked under in the whirl by Nick’s right leg and came to the surface a little way down stream.

He floated rapidly, kicking. In a quick circle, breaking the smooth surface of the water, he disappeared. A trout had taken him.

### 背景知识

**💧****北美五大湖**

**Great Lakes**

*Big Two-Hearted River*（《大双心河》）这个短篇讲述的是Nick在参加大战后，身心受到损伤，回到密执安州北部少年时代常去的钓鱼之地。美国东北部的密执安州处于美国和加拿大交界处的五大湖地带。该州北部为一东西向的大半岛，北面以苏必利尔湖与加拿大为界，南面为密执安湖及休伦湖。我们今天的内容中也出现了Hopkins想要买游艇，带大家一起沿着苏必利尔湖的北岸航行。（He would get a yacht and they would all cruise along the north shore of Lake Superior. ）



北美五大湖是世界最大的淡水湖群，即北美洲的苏必利尔湖、密歇根湖、休伦湖、伊利湖和安大略湖五个相连湖泊的总称，有“北美大陆地中海”之称。我们今天就来了解一下美国著名的五大湖吧～

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/7f7c07b104a4ca4077cac1d058cefb92-sz_1830133.png)



\1. 苏必利尔湖（Lake Superior）



是北美洲五大湖最西北和最大的一个，也是世界面积最大的淡水湖，是世界第二大湖。湖东北面为加拿大，西南面为美国。湖面东西长616千米，南北最宽处257千米，有近200条河流注入湖中，以尼皮贡和圣路易斯河为最大。湖中主要岛屿有罗亚尔岛（美国国家公园之一)、阿波斯特尔群岛等等。



沿湖多林地，风景秀丽，人口稀少。苏必利尔湖水质清澈，湖面多风浪，湖区冬寒夏凉。季节性渔猎和旅游为当地娱乐业主要项目。还蕴藏有多种矿物。有很多天然港湾和人工港口。全年通航期为8个月。该湖1622年为法国探险家发现，湖名取自法语，意为“上湖”。



\2. 休伦湖（Lake Huron）

为北美五大湖中第二大湖，在五大湖中位置居中。它由西北向东南延伸，自北接纳了苏必利尔湖及密歇根湖，南经底特律旁边的圣克莱尔湖、底特律河流入伊利湖。湖区东北部多岛屿，其中包括世界上最大的湖岛马尼图林岛。岛上湖沼众多，更是形成了世界之最的湖中湖——马尼图林湖。湖区主要经济活动有伐木业和渔业。沿湖多游览区。4月初至12月末为通航季节。休伦湖是第一个为欧洲人所发现的湖泊，名源出休伦族印第安人。



\3. 密歇根湖（Lake Michigan）

也叫密执安湖，是北美五大湖中面积居第三位，唯一全部属于美国的湖泊。东北西南走向，湖北部与休伦湖相通，南北长517千米，最宽处190千米，湖岸线长2100千米。有约100条小河注入其中，北端多岛屿，以比弗岛为最大。

湖区气候温和，冬季虽港湾封冻，但湖面却极少全面绅冰，全年有轮渡往来。沿湖岸边有湖波冲蚀而成的悬崖，东南岸多有沙丘，尤以印第安纳国家湖滨区和州立公园的沙丘最为著名。东岸水果产区颇有名，以苹果、桃、梨为代表。北岸曲折多港湾，湖中多鳟鱼、鲑鱼，垂钓业兴旺。南端的芝加哥为重要的工业城市，并有加里、马斯基根等很多港口。



\4. 伊利湖（Lake Erie）

是北美五大湖的第四大湖，东、西、南面为美国，北面为加拿大。湖水面积25667平方千米。呈西南——东北走向，平均深度18米，最深64米，是五大湖中最浅的一个，蓄水量455立方千米。底特律河、休伦河等众多河流注入其中，湖水由东端经尼亚加拉河排出。岛屿集中在湖的西端，以加拿大的皮利岛为最大，岛上有加拿大皮利角国家公园。北岸多农业平原，周围人口密集，城市众多。



\5. 安大略湖（Lake Ontario）

是北美洲五大湖最东和最小的一个，名字来自易洛魁语skanadario，意思是“美丽之湖”。北为加拿大，南是美国，大致成椭圆形。有尼亚加拉、杰纳西等河流注入，经韦兰运河和尼亚加拉河与伊利湖连接。著名的尼亚加拉大瀑布上接伊利湖，下灌安大略湖，两湖落差99米。湖水由东端流入圣劳伦斯河。安大略湖北面为农业平原，工业集中在港口城市圣凯瑟琳、多伦多、金斯顿等。港湾每年12月至来年4月不通航。

### 课文理解

今天内容的开头接着昨天的故事，Nick回忆起过去的一个好友Hopkins，他因为油井而突然成为了暴发户。最后他承诺的很多约定还没兑现就离开了（The Hop Head was rich. He would get a yacht and they would all cruise along the north shore of Lake Superior. He was excited but serious. They said good-bye and all felt bad. It broke up the trip.）自此，Hopkins的朋友再没见到过他。Nick对于这些回忆并没有感觉痛苦，相反地，他对于一切的结束态度很平和，也非常自得于当下的状态——

💧**Clue 1**: Nick is content with the present.



**Evidence 1**: The coffee was bitter. Nick laughed. It made a good ending to the story. His mind was starting to work. He knew he could choke it because he was tired enough.

咖啡很苦。尼克笑笑。故事这样结束，倒是很不错。他的头脑开始转动起来了。他知道，他可以把这思路阻断，因为他太累了。



**Evidence 2**: The mosquito was on the canvas, over his head. Nick moved the match quickly up to it. The mosquito made a satisfactory hiss in the flame. The match went out. Nick lay down again under the blanket.

蚊子立在他头顶的帆布帐篷上。尼克点着火柴去烧蚊子。蚊子在火中发出嘶的一声，这声音听来叫人快慰。火柴熄了。尼克再次盖上毯子躺了下来。



一晚好眠后，Nick第二天的计划是去钓鱼。从一大早起他就开始准备：捉蚱蜢当鱼饵、烹饪食物等等。作者花了相当的笔墨描述这个准备过程，还写到了Nick如何仔细地端详他的钓竿，这些细节都说明了Nick是在非常慎重细致地准备开展钓鱼这项活动——



💧**Clue 2**: Nick prepares the fishing carefully.



**Evidence 1**: Nick took it from his hook book, sitting with the rod across his lap. He tested the knot and the spring of the rod by pulling the line taut. It was a good feeling. He was careful not to let the hook bite into his finger.

尼克坐在那里，钓竿横在膝上，从农钓钩匣中取出这个钓钩。他把钩线拉紧，看看这个结打得牢不牢，看看钓竿的弹性怎么样。这是一种很好的感觉。他非常小心，不让钓钩钩到手指。



**Evidence 2**: Nick felt awkward and professionally happy with all his equipment hanging from him. The grasshopper bottle swung against his chest. In his shirt the breast pockets bulged against him with the lunch and his fly book.

身上挂着这么些东西，尼克感到走路有些别扭，但是又觉得自己好像成了一个行家，心里很开心。那瓶蚱蜢摇晃着，打着他的前胸。衬衫口袋鼓鼓的，塞在里面的是他提前做好的午饭和盛着假蝇的小匣。



Nick做这些事情的时候，刻意地增加了仪式感。可以猜测，钓鱼也是他恢复战争创收并且重拾对生活的积极信心中的重要一步。

### 今日彩蛋

**💧****Various Special Cakes**

**国外各种特色“饼”**

我们今天的内容中有Nick自己用煎锅（skillet）烤荞麦饼（buckwheat cake）的情节（Rapidly he mixed some buckwheat flour with water and stirred it smooth, one cup of flour, one cup of water...On the smoking skillet he poured smoothly the buckwheat batter. It spread like lava, the grease spitting sharply. Around the edges the buckwheat cake began to firm, then brown, then crisp... 他迅速地用水和着一些荞麦面，搅得很均匀，用量是一杯面加一杯水......他把荞麦糊滑溜地倒进这冒烟的煎锅。它像岩浆般扩散开来，牛油清脆地卜卜发响。荞麦饼的四周变得硬起来，然后发黄，然后发脆......) 我们今天来一起看一下国外有哪些独具特色的“饼”吧～



\1. 松饼（Muffin）



平时我们爱吃的“松饼”，被翻译成英文叫做“muffin”，再翻译过来就变成了“英格兰松饼”、“杯状小松糕”、“马芬蛋糕”。所有以纸杯作为模具的蛋糕都被叫做纸杯蛋糕（cupcake）， muffin cupcake也属于其中一种，muffin的面糊中含有黄油、鸡蛋、糖、低粉和泡打粉，口感会比戚风蛋糕（Chiffon Cake）浓厚很多。



最常见的muffin有巧克力muffin、香蕉muffin、蔓越莓muffin、柠檬muffin，有些甚至可以做成咸的，例如蔬菜muffin、芝士蒜香muffin…



\2. 华夫饼（Waffle）

华夫饼不管做成圆的还是方的，它都是带格子的，香港人喜欢叫它格子饼。华夫饼由发酵的面糊，倒入一边带模具的烤盘中，再盖上另一边烤盘，加热烘烤几分钟制成。新鲜出炉的华夫饼是脆脆的，不同地方有不同的吃法。美国的华夫饼口感紧密，外表看上去比较薄，通常会混合山核桃、巧克力或浆果，配上黄油、枫糖浆、培根、糖粉、蜂蜜或其他果酱。美国人喜欢把它们当成早餐。



\3. 煎饼（Pancake）

一般来说，我们所说的松饼应该是Pancake，最正统的叫法是煎饼或者薄烤饼。煎饼是一种扁平的蛋糕，用淀粉制成，含有鸡蛋、牛奶和黄油，在热的平底锅（Pan）上用油或是黄油煎，因此得名Pancake。煎饼的厚度可以自己定，但一般都偏向于薄，最经典的煎饼最外层皮是金黄色，或是微焦带点棕色，内部柔软，多孔且富有弹性。



\4.  可丽饼（Crepe）

可丽饼是一种法式煎饼，又被叫做法式薄饼，以小麦粉为原材料，比英式煎饼更薄。在煎的时候，其他煎饼是两面都煎，而可丽饼只煎一面，煎成一大张饼后折成扇形。可丽饼在国内以甜口味为主，吃法多种多样，可以卷上各种奶油、水果、巧克力酱等等。在法国，可丽饼也可以是咸的，除了可以包裹奶油水果冰激凌，或撒上糖粉，还可以包裹鸡蛋、火腿、奶酪、蔬菜、鱼肉......



\5. 荷兰煎饼（Pannenkoeken）

是荷兰最普遍也最受欢迎的风味餐点,有点类似法国的可丽饼，又有点像意大利的披萨。将奶、蛋、和面粉稍微煎成饼后，放入已熏好的培根、火腿、奶酪，及切成薄片的苹果、葡萄干、香蕉等各式水果，最后淋上黑枫糖浆（maple syrup），又咸又甜，十分特别。



\6.  热香饼（Hotcakes）

在北美，煎饼又被叫做hotcakes，用发酵粉使煎饼发酵，因此会厚一些。配煎饼的酱汁和配料就多了，糖粉、果酱、冰淇淋、水果、坚果、蜂蜜…...  美式煎饼最常见的吃法是在原味的Pancake上淋上一层加拿大的枫糖浆，而且是加热后的枫糖浆，饼里的奶香味与蛋香味在枫糖浆的作用下越发清晰，层层递进。

## Chapter 9.4

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/74efefbb9de7f781202d4f98ddbd065a-sz_1246458.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmorient)

Big Two-Hearted River

Another hopper poked his face out of the bottle. His antenna wavered.

He was getting his front legs out of the bottle to jump.

Nick took him by the head and held him while he threaded the slim hookunder his chin, down through his thorax and into the last segments ofhis abdomen.

> ==segment英 [ˈsegmənt] 美 [ˈsɛɡmənt] n. 部分；片段；瓣；弓形，弦；段 vt.&vi. 分割，划分==
>
> n. 环节（a part of sth that is separate from the other parts or can be considered separately）
>
> 原文：Nick took him by the head and held him while he threaded the slim hook under his chin, down through his thorax and into the lastsegments of his abdomen.
>
> 尼克一把抓住它的头，捏着它，把细钓钩穿过它的下巴，一直刺透咽喉直到它肚子最下部的那几个环节。
>
> 💧segment作动词时，有“划分”的意思，比如：Market researchers often segment the population on the basis of age and social class.
>
> 市场研究人员常常按年龄和社会阶层划分人口。

The grasshopper took hold of the hook with his front feet, spitting tobacco juice on it. Nick dropped him into the water.

Holding the rod in his right hand he let out line against the pull of the grasshopper in the current.

He stripped off line from the reel with his left hand and let it run free.

> <font color=red>He stripped off line from the reel with his left hand and let it run free.</font>
>
> 他用左手从卷轴上解开钓丝，让它没阻挡地溜出去。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> stripped off line 解开钓丝，strip off表示“解开，脱掉”，比如：He stripped off his wet clothes and stepped into the shower.
>
> 他脱掉湿衣服走进浴室。

He could see the hopper in the littlewaves of the current.

It went out of sight. There was a tugon the line.

Nick pulled against the taut line. It was his first strike.

Holding the now living rod across the current, he brought in the line with his left hand.

The rod bent in jerks, the trout pumping against the current.

Nick knew it was a small one. He lifted the rod straight up in the air. Itbowed with the pull.

He saw the trout in the water jerking with his head and body against the shifting tangent of the line in the stream.

Nick took the line in his left hand and pulled the trout, thumping tiredly against the current, to the surface.

His back was mottled the clear, water-over-gravel color, his side flashing in the sun.

The rod under his right arm, Nick stooped, dipping his right hand into the current.

He held the trout, never still, with his moist right hand, while he unhooked the barb from his mouth, then dropped him back into the stream.

He hung unsteadily in the current, then settled to the bottom beside a stone.

Nick reached down his hand to touch him, his arm to the elbow under water.

The trout was steady in the moving stream, resting on the gravel, beside a stone.

As Nick’s fingers touched him, touched his smooth, cool, underwater feeling he was gone, gone in a shadow across the bottom of the stream.

He’s all right, Nick thought. He was only tired.

He had wet his hand before he touched the trout, so he would not disturb the delicate mucus that covered him.

If a trout was touched with a dry hand, a white fungus attacked the unprotected spot.

> ==fungus英 [ˈfʌŋgəs] 美 [ˈfʌŋɡəs] n. 真菌；真菌类==

Years before when he had fished crowded streams, with fly fishermen ahead of him and behind him, Nick had again and again come on dead trout, furry with white fungus, drifted against a rock, or floating belly up insome pool.

> <font color=red>Years before when he had fished crowded streams, with fly fishermen ahead of him and behind him,  Nick had again and again come on dead trout, furry with white fungus, drifted against a rock, or floating belly up in some pool.</font>
>
> 尼克曾到人头济济的小溪边钓鱼，前前后后都是用假蝇钓鱼的人，他曾一再看到身上长满毛茸茸的白色真菌的死鳟鱼，被水冲到石头边，或者肚子朝天，浮在水潭里。
>
> **💧知识拓展**
>
> fly fishermen 用假蝇钓鱼的人，飞钓（fly fishing）就是使用特殊的飞钓线（Fly line）、飞钓杆（Fly rod）和人工拟饵（fly），利用独特的挥舞技术和线本身的重量，将线和饵打出去，然后慢慢回收线，利用不同手法和水流状况表现拟饵的活动，吸引鱼儿攻击上钩的一种钓鱼方法。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①fished crowded streams 到人头济济的小溪边钓鱼，fish the streams 表示“在溪流里钓鱼”，比如：Others came to fish the streams, pools or ponds. 
>
> 也有人来到溪流或池塘边享受垂钓之乐。
>
> ②dead trout furry with white fungus, 身上长满毛茸茸的白色真菌的死鳟鱼，furry with 指的是“表面覆盖着毛茸茸的......” 比如：In winter, the bare branches grow furry with frost. They sparkle in the sun, and you're afraid to touch them in case they shatter. 
>
> 冬天的时候，光光的树枝附上了毛茸茸的一层霜，在太阳底下发着光，你都害怕一不小心碰到它们就散落一地。

Nick did not like to fish with other men on the river.

Unless they were of your party, they spoiled it.

> <font color=red>Unless they were of your party, they spoiled it.</font>
>
> 除非同你自己是一伙中的，他们总使人扫兴。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> spoil 意为“扫兴”，to spoil the fun / somebody's fun 表示“扫兴/扫某人的兴”，比如：David was surprised, but Joe's absence did not spoil his pleasure. 
>
> 大卫感到奇怪，但乔不在家倒也并未使他扫兴。

He wallowed down the stream, above his knees in the current, through the fifty yards of shallow water above the pile of logs that crossed the stream.

> ==wallow英 [ˈwɒləʊ] 美 [ˈwɑ:loʊ] vi. 沉湎，放纵；打滚，翻滚 n. (烂泥或水里)打滚嬉戏，翻滚==
>
> <font color=red>He wallowed down the stream, above his knees in the current, through the fifty yards of shallow water above the pile of logs that crossed the stream.</font>
>
> 他朝下游涉水前进，流水没过他的膝盖，他穿过在小河上那几根圆木上游的五十码浅水。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①wallowed down the stream 朝下游涉水前进, down the stream 向下游，比如：The logs drifted down the stream. 
>
> 木材顺流漂下。
>
> wallow作动词意为“颠簸，打滚”（to lie and roll about in water or mud, to keep cool or for pleasure），这里表示“涉水前进”，比如：Dogs love splashing in mud and hippos wallow in it. 
>
> 狗喜欢在泥水洼里扑腾，河马则喜欢在其中打滚撒欢儿。
>
> wallow in 表示“沉溺于”（to enjoy sth that causes you pleasure），比如：His tired mind continued to wallow in self-pity.
>
> 他疲惫的心灵继续沉溺于自怜之中。
>
> ②fifty yards of shallow water 五十码浅水，yard 表示“码”，是一个英制长度单位，1码=0.9144米＝3英尺。比如：The incident took place about 500 yards from where he was standing.
>
> 事件发生在距他所站位置大约500码远的地方。

He did not rebait his hook and held it in his hand as he waded.

He was certain he could catch smalltrout in the shallows, but he did not want them.

There would be no big trout in the shallows this time of day.

Now the water deepened up his thighs sharply and coldly.

Ahead was the smooth dammed-back flood of water above the logs.

> <font color=red>Ahead was the smooth dammed-back flood of water above the logs.</font>
>
> 这时冷冷的河水陡的深得没上了他的大腿。前面就是被圆木拦住的平坦的水面。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> dammed-back flood of water 被拦住的水面，dammed 指“被水坝阻止的”，dammed-back 表示“被拦住的”，比如：The dammed stream backed up and flooded the meadow. 
>
> 被坝堵住的河流水位上升，淹没了附近的草地。

The water was smooth and dark; onthe left, the lower edge of the meadow; on the right the swamp.

Nick leaned back against the current and took a hopper from the bottle.

He threaded the hopper on the hook and spat on him for good luck.

> <font color=red>He threaded the hopper on the hook and spat on him for good luck.</font>
>
> 他把蚁蜢穿上钓钩，为了求得好运，朝它唾了一口。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> spit on 表示“吐唾沫”，比如：The German Minister was publicly insulted, and the crowd spat on his car. 
>
> 德国公使公然受到侮辱，群众向他的汽车吐唾沫。

Then he pulled several yards of linefrom the reel and tossed the hopperout ahead onto the fast, dark water.

It floated down towards the logs, then the weight of the line pulled the bait under the surface.

Nick held the rod in his right hand, letting the line run out through his fingers.

There was a long tug. Nick struck and the rod came alive and dangerous, bent double, the line tightening, coming out of water, tightening, all in a heavy, dangerous, steady pull.

Nick felt the moment when the leader would break if the strain increased and let the line go.

The reel ratcheted into a mechanical shriek as the line went out in a rush.

> ==mechanical英 [məˈkænɪkl] 美 [mɪˈkænɪkəl] adj. 机械的；行为机械的；呆板的==
>
> adj. 机械的 (operated by power from an engine)
>
> 原文：The reel ratcheted into a mechanicalshriek as the line went out in a rush.
>
> 钓丝飞速地朝外溜，卷轴上的棘轮吱吱的响。
>
> 💧mechanical 作形容词，还有“呆板的”意思，比如：a mechanical gesture/response 
>
> 呆板的手势 / 回答
>
> ==shriek英 [ʃri:k] 美 [ʃrik] vt.&vi. 尖叫；发出类似尖叫的声音 n. 尖叫声；尖锐的声音==

Too fast. Nick could not check it, the line rushing out, the reel note rising as the line ran out.

With the core of the reel showing, his heart feeling stopped with the excitement, leaning back against thecurrent that mounted icily his thighs,Nick thumbed the reel hard with his left hand.

It was awkward getting his thumb inside the fly reel frame.

As he put on pressure the line tightened into sudden hardness and beyond the logs a huge trout went high out of water.

As he jumped, Nick lowered the tip of the rod.

But he felt, as he dropped the tip to ease the strain, the moment when the strain was too great; the hardness too tight.

Of course, the leader had broken. There was no mistaking the feeling when all spring left the line and it became dry and hard.

Then it went slack. His mouth dry, his heart down, Nick reeled in.

> <font color=red>Then it went slack.</font>
>
> 跟着它变得松弛了
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> go slack 表示“松弛”，比如：His grimacing face began to go slack. 
>
> 他歪扭的脸开始舒展了。

He had never seen so big a trout. There was a heaviness, a power not to be held, and then the bulk of him, as he jumped.

He looked as broad as a salmon.

> ==salmon英 [ˈsæmən] 美 [ˈsæmən] n. 鲑鱼；鲑鱼肉；橙红色==

Nick’s hand was shaky. He reeled in slowly.

The thrill had been too much. He felt, vaguely, a little sick, as though it would be better to sit down.

The leader had broken where the hook was tied to it.

Nick took it in his hand. He thought of the trout somewhere on the bottom, holding himself steady over the gravel, far down below the light, under the logs, with the hook in his jaw.

Nick knew the trout’s teeth would cut through the snell of the hook.

The hook would imbed itself in his jaw. He’d bet the trout was angry.

Anything that size would be angry. That was a trout.

He had been solidly hooked. Solid as a rock.

He felt like a rock, too, before he started off.

By God, he was a big one. By God,he was the biggest one I ever heardof.

Nick climbed out onto the meadow and stood, water running down his trousers and out of his shoes, his shoes squelchy.

He went over and sat on the logs. He did not want to rush his sensations any.

He wriggled his toes in the water, inhis shoes, and got out a cigarette from his breast pocket.

He lit it and tossed the match into the fast water below the logs.

A tiny trout rose at the match, as it swung around in the fast current.

Nick laughed. He would finish the cigarette.

He sat on the logs, smoking, drying in the sun, the sun warm on his back, the river shallow ahead entering the woods, curving into the woods, shallows, light glittering, big water-smooth rocks, cedars along the bank and white birches,

the logs warm in the sun, smooth tosit on, without bark, gray to the touch; slowly the feeling of disappointment left him.

It went away slowly, the feeling of disappointment that came sharply after the thrill that made his shoulders ache.

It was all right now. His rod lying out on the logs, Nick tied a new hook on the leader, pulling the gut tight until it grimped into itself in a hard knot.

He baited up, then picked up the rod and walked to the far end of thelogs to get into the water, where it was not too deep.

Under and beyond the logs was a deep pool.

Nick walked around the shallow shelf near the swamp shore until hecame out on the shallow bed of the stream.

On the left, where the meadow ended and the woods began, a great elm tree was uprooted.

Gone over in a storm, it lay back into the woods, its roots clotted withdirt, grass growing in them, rising a solid bank beside the stream.

The river cut to the edge of the uprooted tree.

From where Nick stood he could see deep channels, like ruts, cut in the shallow bed of the stream by the flow of the current.

Pebbly where he stood and pebbly and full of boulders beyond; where it curved near the tree roots, the bed of the stream was marly and between the ruts of deep water green weed fronds swung in the current.

Nick swung the rod back over his shoulder and forward, and the line, curving forward, laid the grasshopper down on one of the deep channels in the weeds.

A trout struck and Nick hooked him.

### 背景知识

**💧****Salmon**

**三文鱼？鲑鱼？**

我们今天的内容中一直围绕着Nick来到河边垂钓来讲述，（He had never seen so big a trout. There was a heaviness, a power not to be held, and then the bulk of him, as he jumped. He looked as broad as a salmon. 他从没见过这样大的鳟鱼，分量很沉，力气大得拉不住，再说，它跳起来时露出的个头多大啊。它看上去象鲑鱼般宽阔。）这里trout是指“鳟鱼”，salmon是指“鲑鱼”，我们生活中常见的三文鱼译为salmon，我们今天来一起了解一下三文鱼吧～



说起三文鱼，我们脑海中肯定会浮现出以下关键词：日料、刺身。超市的生鲜柜台里，三文鱼鱼腩、鱼头，鱼骨，以及一盒又一盒的三文鱼寿司摆放整齐，等着被吃掉。

三文鱼（salmon），来源于拉丁语中的“salmo”，意为奋力跃起。之所以取这样的名字，源于三文鱼的洄游特征。每年到了产卵期，它们千里逆流，甚至还要跳跃和冲撞数十英尺高的障碍，只为回到当初出生的河流产卵。



18世纪，生物命名法的创立者林奈把这种鱼的学名形象地定为“salmo salar”，也就是现在的鲑鱼属大西洋鲑。而大西洋鲑以外的各种“三文鱼”，中国人给它们起了一个更通俗的名字——大马哈鱼。市面上的三文鱼种类很多，有挪威的、芬兰的、美国阿拉斯加产三文鱼。挪威是世界上最大的大西洋三文鱼生产国，出口到世界上上百个国家。买的时候看清产地即可，不需要过多挑剔。

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/61756928ab92a3386b3e58c86e788326-sz_178162.png)



在英文世界里“Salmon”不光指大西洋鲑，还指太平洋鲑属的很多种鱼。为了进一步区分，又在统称前加上了产地、形态等特征，诸如Pink salmon（粉三文鱼）、Coho salmon（银三文鱼）、Sockeye salmon（红三文鱼）等众多鱼种。

而经常冒充三文鱼的虹鳟鱼虽属于太平洋鲑属，但虹鳟的通用英文名是rainbow trout，trout对应的概念是“鳟鱼”，指的是大马哈鱼属和鲑鱼属的鱼中，生活史全部于淡水中完成，没有跨盐度洄游行为的一个类群。价格便宜 + 肉色偏红+ 刺身厚度薄+ 脂肪纹理窄且很清晰+ 肉表面无光泽的所谓三文鱼，通常就是虹鳟鱼。

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/2177f13721ec5202806a05472326b41d-sz_158853.png)



三文鱼最为常见的，就是架在冰块上，以刺身生吃，沾着日本酱油与青芥末，再搭配点白萝卜丝解腻，或卷着一起吃。生吃三文鱼，确实是营养价值最高、吸收最好的吃法。



野生的三文鱼是有寄生虫的。所以，吃生鱼片会有得寄生虫病的危险，日本是发达国家中寄生虫病高发国家。但是，实际生活中，我们并非把单纯的野生的三文鱼直接生吃。三文鱼食用前用低温冷冻可杀灭寄生虫，通常可以用零下30摄氏度左右的低温，急速冷冻保存24个小时左右。



如果不太接受生吃方法，或不能完全保证三文鱼非常新鲜的情况下可以选择熟吃的方法，但为了尽量保留其中的营养，最好是五成熟即食。推荐两种吃法：一种是涮食，在大约70度左右的汤中，薄的肉片沾过即可食用；另外可以微煎，将三文鱼切近一厘米左右的厚度，在少油的煎锅中将两面微微煎黄即可。

### 课文理解

Nick起先钓到了一只鳟鱼，但他觉得不够大，所以又把这条鳟鱼放生了（...he unhooked the barb from his mouth, then dropped him back into the stream）. 这里有一个细节说明了Nick和其他垂钓者的不同，他对自然更存敬畏和爱护之心，也更有道德责任感——



💧**Clue 1**: Nick sets himself apart from other fishermen.



**Evidence 1**: He had wet his hand before he touched the trout, so he would not disturb the delicate mucus that covered him. If a trout was touched with a dry hand, a white fungus attacked the unprotected spot.

他先弄湿了手才去摸那鳟鱼，这样才不会弄坏覆盖在鱼身上的那一层薄薄的黏液。如果干手去摸鳟鱼，黏液被弄破的地方就会被白色真菌感染。



**Evidence 2**: Nick did not like to fish with other men on the river. Unless they were of your party, they spoiled it.

尼克不喜欢跟别人一起在河边钓鱼。除非大家是一伙的，否则有些人总使人扫兴。



这里说的“一伙”（of your party）其实就是指像Nick这样爱护生灵并且有道德感的垂钓者，可以看出来Nick骨子里有很强的正义感。



接着Nick继续寻找可以钓到大鳟鱼的地方（He was certain he could catch small trout in the shallows, but he did not want them. There would be no big trout in the shallows this time of day.）他开始往深水的区域前进。果然在这里有一只大鱼上了钩，但随之而来的是一场悲伤的意外，接钩绳因为无法承受压力直接绷断了（Of course, the leader had broken.）Nick这时候表现出了既有沮丧又有快意的复杂情感——



💧**Clue 2**: Nick feels at once depressed and thrilled.



**Evidence 1**: His mouth dry, his heart down, Nick reeled in. He had never seen so big a trout. There was a heaviness, a power not to be held, and then the bulk of him, as he jumped.

尼克嘴巴发干，心情低沉，把钓线收起来，绕到卷轴上。他从来没见过这样大的鳟鱼，分量真重，力气真大，拉也拉不住，还有，它跳起来的时候，那块头多大啊。



**Evidence 2**: Nick’s hand was shaky. He reeled in slowly. The thrill had been too much. He felt, vaguely, a little sick, as though it would be better to sit down.

尼克的手在发抖。他慢慢地收起钓线，绕到卷轴上。这实在太刺激了。恍惚之间，他感到一点点恶心，还是坐下来为好。



这一条大鳟鱼就像我们人生中曾经憧憬向往并短暂拥有的幸福，但却一不小心被夺走了，并且无法失而复得。对于Nick来说也是如此，他有过的青春美好，随着战争的来临，都被湮没甚至摧毁掉了。而他如此地想要使一切恢复原样，也难免因为希冀过高而出现失望。



但是他的钓鱼旅程还没有结束。明天是我们这篇故事的结尾部分，Nick的态度是否会发生转变，他最后能不能治愈自己在战争中所受的创伤呢？

### 今日彩蛋

**💧**美国森林旅行

Forest Travelling in America



我们今天的内容中有Nick在森林边的场景：他坐在圆木上，抽着烟，在阳光里晒干裤腿，太阳晒得他背脊很暖和，前面的河边浅滩钻进树林，弯弯曲曲地进入树林，望着这些浅滩，闪闪发亮的阳光，被水冲得很光滑的大石块，河边的雪松和白桦树，被阳光晒暖的圆木，光滑可坐，没有树起，摸上去很古老。（He sat on the logs, smoking, drying in the sun, the sun warm on his back, the river shallow ahead entering the woods, curving into the woods, shallows, light glittering, big water-smooth rocks, cedars along the bank and white birches, the logs warm in the sun, smooth to sit on, without bark, gray to the touch; slowly the feeling of disappointment left him.）森林旅行在现在越来越流行，森林公园成为了大家在这个喧嚣的世界放松身心的好去处。



美国可以说是森林旅游的鼻祖，1872年被正式命名的黄石国家公园算是森林旅游的前身，二战之后，依托森林发展旅游的趋势逐渐兴起，到1960年，森林旅游的现实价值获得了各界人士的承认，并一跃成了森林资源开发的主要部分之一。



森林旅游是指人们以森林、湿地、荒漠和野生动植物资源及其外部物质环境为依托，开展的观光游览、休闲度假、健身养生、文化教育等旅游活动。目前森林旅游度假的一些类型包括：度假村项目、露营地和私人度假社区等。



\1. 通加斯国家森林（Tongass National Forest）Alaska



通加斯国家森林是美国最大的国家森林，占地六百八十万公顷，面积是美国第二大国家森林的三倍。通加斯国家森林包含19个自然保护区、阿德默勒尔蒂群岛国家纪念公园、以及薄雾峡湾国家风景区。



它拥有美国境内现存最大的巨树保留区，以及全球仅存老龄温带雨林的将近三分之一，且树龄悠久至最高800年岁数的云杉、铁木衫、西洋杉。因其地理形势和气候条件形成大量冰河、结冰区。太平洋里的五种野生鲑鱼都能在通加斯国家森林的河里看到，还有其他如比目鱼等鱼种。



\2. 吉福德·平肖国家森林（Gifford Pinchot National Forest ）Washington



吉福德·平肖国家森林因有许多几万年前因火山爆发而形成的隧道、山洞等而出名，其中长达2.5英里长的“猿洞”最受观光客欢迎，其太平洋峰步道也是许多健行登山客的最爱。 你可以在吉福德·平肖国家森林中许多的河流里看到各种不同的鲑鱼及鳟鱼，在森林间也有机会一睹驼鹿、黑熊、山羊、山猫的踪迹。



3.科科尼诺国家森林（Coconino National Forest）Arizona



科科尼诺国家森林位于亚利桑那州，是一片全美知名、涵盖最多元生态的高海拔森林。树木生长在12000米的高山上。主要的树种是山杨和黄松，树叶交相辉印，构成一幅美丽的彩绘画。科科尼诺国家森林之所以如此命名是因为它穿过了莫戈永和科科尼诺高原。从知名的红岩、松木林、到高山苔原，都能在科科尼诺国家森林一次满足你的探索。



\4. 毗斯迦山国家森林（Pisgah National Forests） North Carolina



毗斯迦山国家森林最吸引人的是随季节变化色彩、满山满谷的簇叶，宛如大自然替这森林画上的美丽地毯。长达200英里的健行步道，是吸引游客前来散步、慢跑、欣赏自然美景的人气之选。



5.大提顿国家森林（Bridger-Teton National Forest）Wyoming



大提顿国家森林为目前世界上最大、最完整的温带生态系统之一，在森林里以大陆分水岭界分了约有120万英亩的联邦保护生态地区。其中最热门的景点为一条由1925年一场不知名的山崩造成的5英里长的下滑河川（Gros Ventre Slide Geologic Area）还可能看到麋鹿、大角羊、灰熊、山猫、秃鹰、驼鹿，森林主要涵盖树种有山杨、道格拉斯冷杉、松树林、云杉、和白皮松。



\6. 西波拉国家森林（Cibola National Forest）New Mexico



从北连至新墨西哥中部，西波拉国家森林总长一千六百万英亩、海拔一万一千三百英尺，被誉为广阔的天空岛。有四个保护林区，为麋鹿、驼鹿、黑熊、山猫等动物之栖息地。

## Chapter 9.5

![img](http://img.xiumi.us/xmi/ua/anoo/i/aeabe390123b42fd10788dd6de2c6046-sz_2297884.jpg?x-oss-process=style/xmhigh)

Big Two-Hearted River

Holding the rod far out toward the uprooted tree and sloshing backward in the current, Nick worked the trout, plunging, the rod bending alive, out of the danger of the weeds into the open river.

> ==slosh英 [slɒʃ] 美 [slɑ:ʃ] vt.&vi. (指液体)晃动作响==
>
> ==plunge英 [plʌndʒ] 美 [plʌndʒ] vt. 猛地投入；使陷入 vi. 俯冲；暴跌，骤降；猛烈颠簸 n. 突然跌落；卷入；跳水==

Holding the rod, pumping alive against the current, Nick brought thetrout in.

He rushed, but always came, the spring of the rod yielding to the rushes, sometimes jerking under water, but always bringing him in.

> ==yield英 [ji:ld] 美 [jild] vt. 产生；产出；放弃；泄露 vi. 屈服；倒塌；被取代；让行 n. 产量；利润，收益==
>
> v. 屈服，顺从（to stop resisting sth/sb; to agree to do sth that you do not want to do）相当于give way，通常与to搭配。
>
> 原文：He rushed, but always came, the spring of the rod yielding to the rushes, sometimes jerking under water, but always bringing him in.
>
> 他性急慌忙地拉着，不过总是有成效，这有弹性的钓竿顺从着这一次次的猛拉，有时候在水里弹跳着，但是始终在把鱼往回拉。
>
> 💧yield作动词，还有“产生”的意思，比如：Higher-rate deposit accounts yield good returns.
>
> 高利率的存款会产生丰厚的收益。

Nick eased downstream with the rushes. The rod above his head he led the trout over the net, then lifted.

The trout hung heavy in the net, mottled trout back and silver sides in the meshes.

Nick unhooked him; heavy sides, good to hold, big undershot jaw, and slipped him, heaving and big sliding, into the long sack that hung from his shoulders in the water.

Nick spread the mouth of the sack against the current and it filled, heavy with water.

He held it up, the bottom in the stream, and the water poured out through the sides.

Inside at the bottom was the big trout, alive in the water.

Nick moved downstream. The sack out ahead of him sunk heavy in the water, pulling from his shoulders.

It was getting hot, the sun hot on the back of his neck.

Nick had one good trout. He did not care about getting many trout.

Now the stream was shallow and wide. There were trees along both banks.

The trees of the left bank made short shadows on the current in the forenoon sun.

Nick knew there were trout in each shadow.

In the afternoon, after the sun had crossed toward the hills, the trout would be in the cool shadows on the other side of the stream.

The very biggest ones would lie up close to the bank.

> <font color=red>The very biggest ones would lie up close to the bank.</font>
>
> 最最大的鱼会待在靠近河岸的地方。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> lie up close to the bank 待在靠近河岸的地方，lie up表示“待在”，比如：The cables we're dealing with here lie up to 4,000 metres deep. 
>
> 我们正在维修的这些光缆在海底4000米深的地方。

You could always pick them up there on the Black.

When the sun was down they all moved out into the current.

Just when the sun made the water blinding in the glare before it went down, you were liable to strike a bigtrout anywhere in the current.

> <font color=red>Just when the sun made the water blinding in the glare before it went down, you were liable to strike a big trout anywhere in the current.</font>
>
> 太阳下山前使河水射出一起耀眼的反光，就在此时，你可能在激流中的任何地方使一条大鳟鱼上钩。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> ①the water blinding in the glare 河水射出一起耀眼的反光，blind在这里作动词，表示“使目眩”（to make it difficult for sb to see for a short time），比如：When she went outside she was temporarily blinded by the sun.
>
> 走出户外时，她一时被阳光照得眼睛昏花。
>
> ②be liable to 表示“可能“，比如：Only a small minority of the mentally ill are liable to harm themselves or others. 
>
> 在精神病患者中，只有一小部分有可能会伤害自己或他人。

It was almost impossible to fish then, the surface of the water was blinding as a mirror in the sun.

Of course, you could fish upstream, but in a stream like the Black, or this, you had to wallow against the current and in a deep place, the water piled up on you.

> <font color=red>Of course, you could fish upstream, but in a stream like the Black, or this, you had to wallow against the current and in a deep place, the water piled up on you.</font>
>
> 当然啦，你可以到上游去钓，可是在黑河或这条河那样的河道上，你不得不逆水吃力地走，而在水深的地方，水会朝你身上直涌。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> the water piled up on you 水会朝你身上直涌，pile up 表示“堆积”，这里引申为“涌来”。比如：Cargoes pile up on the dockside and ships wait empty because exporters cannot get letters of credit to secure payment on delivery. 
>
> 货物堆满了港口，空船就等在岸边，因为出口商得不到信用证，无法保证发出货物之后能够收到货款。

It was no fun to fish upstream with this much current.

Nick moved along through the shallow stretch watching the banks for deep holes.

A beech tree grew close beside the river, so that the branches hung down into the water.

> <font color=red>A beech tree grew close beside the river, so that the branches hung down into the water.</font>
>
> 紧靠河边长着一棵山毛榉，所以它的枝桠直垂到河水里。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> hung down into the water 垂到河水里。hang down表示“垂下来”，比如：Her braids hung down on her shoulders. 
>
> 她的辫子下垂到肩头。

The stream went back in under the leaves.

There were always trout in a place like that.

Nick did not care about fishing that hole.

He was sure he would get hooked in the branches.

> <font color=red>He was sure he would get hooked in the branches.</font>
>
> 他肯定知道钓钩会让枝桠钩住。
>
> **💧表达精讲**
>
> get hooked in the branches 让枝桠钩住，get hooked表示“钩住”，比如：The bigger ones get hooked with a special gaff. 
>
> 大鱼就用特制的鱼钩钩住。
>
> get hooked 还可以表示“迷住”，比如：I bet that if you give robotics a try, many of you will get hooked on it. 
>
> 我相信，如果尝试一下机器人技术的话，那么许多人都会被它迷住的。

It looked deep though. He dropped the grasshopper so the current took it under water, back in under the overhanging branch.

The line pulled hard and Nick struck. The trout threshed heavily, half out of water in the leaves and branches.

The line was caught. Nick pulled hard and the trout was off.

He reeled in and holding the hook in his hand, walked down the stream.

Ahead, close to the left bank, was a big log.

Nick saw it was hollow; pointing up river the current entered it smoothly,only a little ripple spread each side of the log.
